                                             GLOSSARY
 Affected         : Individuals, organizations or businesses that are directly affected socially and
 persons (APs)      economically by WB-funded Projects caused by the involuntary taking of land
                    and other assets that results in (i) relocation or loss of shelter; (ii) loss of assets
                    or access to assets; or (iii) loss of income sources or means of livelihood,
                    whether or not the affected persons must move to another location. In addition,
                    affected person is one for whom involuntary restriction of access to legally
                    designated parks and protected areas that result in adverse impacts on
                    livelihoods.
 Associated       : Means facilities or activities that are not funded as part of the project and, in the
 Facilities         judgment of the Bank, are: (a) directly and significantly related to the project;
                    (b) carried out, or planned to be carried out, contemporaneously with the project;
                    and (c) necessary for the project to be viable and would not have been
                    constructed, expanded or conducted if the project did not exist. For facilities or
                    activities to be Associated Facilities, they must meet all three criteria.
 Cut-off date     : The Borrower will establish a cut-off date for eligibility. Information regarding
                    the cut-off date will be well documented and will be disseminated throughout
                    the project area at regular intervals in written and (as appropriate) nonwritten
                    forms and in relevant local languages. This will include posted warnings that
                    persons settling in the project area after the cutoff date may be subject to
                    removal.
                     For the project, the cut-off date is established when the CPC issue the
                     Notification of Land Acquisition (NLA) for the project area (Article 85, Land
                     Law 2024), followed by the detailed measurement survey. Affected persons and
                     local communities will be informed of the cut-off date for each Project’s
                     component, and that anyone moving into the Project areas after that date will not
                     be entitled to compensation and assistance under the Project. The project
                     planning (based on the basic design) has not been approved yet.
 Disadvantaged    : Refers to those who may be more likely to be adversely affected by the
 or vulnerable       project impacts and/or more limited than others in their ability to take advantage
                     of a project’s benefits. Such an individual/group is also more likely to be
                     excluded from/unable to participate fully in the mainstream consultation process
                     and as such may require specific measures and/or assistance to do so. This will
                     take into account considerations relating to age, including the elderly and
                     minors, and including in circumstances where they may be separated from their
                     family, the community or other
                     individuals upon which they depend.
 Eligibility      : The criteria for establishment of entitlements under the resettlement program.
 Forced           : Is defined as the permanent or temporary removal against the will of individuals,
 eviction           families, and/or communities from the homes and/or land which they occupy
                    without the provision of, and access to, appropriate forms of legal and other
                    protection, including all applicable procedures and principles in ESS5. The
                    exercise of eminent domain, compulsory acquisition or similar powers by a
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                 Page | viii
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


                     Borrower will not be considered to be forced eviction providing it complies with
                     the requirements of national law and the provisions of ESS5, and is conducted
                     in a manner consistent with basic principles of due process (including provision
                     of adequate advance notice, meaningful opportunities to lodge grievances and
                     appeals, and avoidance of the use of unnecessary, disproportionate or excessive
                     force).
 Involuntary      : Project-related land acquisition or restrictions on land use may cause physical
 resettlement       displacement (relocation, loss of residential land or loss of shelter), economic
                    displacement (loss of land, assets or access to assets, including those that lead to
                    loss of income sources or other means of livelihood), or both. The term
                    “involuntary resettlement” refers to these impacts. Resettlement is considered
                    involuntary when affected persons or communities do not have the right to refuse
                    land acquisition or restrictions on land use that result in displacement.
 Land             : Refers to all methods of obtaining land for project purposes, which may include
 acquisition        outright purchase, expropriation of property and acquisition of access rights,
                    such as easements or rights of way. Land acquisition may also include: (a)
                    acquisition of unoccupied or unutilized land whether or not the landholder relies
                    upon such land for income or livelihood purposes; (b) repossession of public
                    land that is used or occupied by individuals or households; and (c) project
                    impacts that result in land being submerged or otherwise rendered unusable or
                    inaccessible. “Land” includes anything growing on or permanently affixed to
                    land, such as crops, buildings and other improvements, and appurtenant water
                    bodies.
 Livelihood       : Refers to the full range of means that individuals, families, and communities
                    utilize to make a living, such as wage-based income, agriculture, fishing,
                    foraging, other natural resource-based livelihoods, petty trade, and bartering.
 Project impact : Any consequence immediately related to the taking of a parcel of land or to
                  restrictions in the use of legally designated parks or protected areas. People
                  directly affected by land acquisition may lose their home, farmland, property,
                  business, or other means of livelihood. In other words, they lose their ownership,
                  occupancy, or use rights, because of land acquisition or restriction of access.
 Replacement      : Is defined as a method of valuation yielding compensation sufficient to replace
 cost               assets, plus necessary transaction costs associated with asset replacement.
                    Where functioning markets exist, replacement cost is the market value as
                    established through independent and competent real estate valuation, plus
                    transaction costs. Where functioning markets do not exist, replacement cost may
                    be determined through alternative means, such as calculation of output value for
                    land or productive assets, or the undepreciated value of replacement material
                    and labor for construction of structures or other fixed assets, plus transaction
                    costs. In all instances where physical displacement results in loss of shelter,
                    replacement cost must at least be sufficient to enable purchase or construction
                    of housing that meets acceptable minimum community standards of quality and
                    safety. The valuation method for determining replacement cost should be
                    documented and included in relevant resettlement planning documents.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | ix
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


                      Transaction costs include administrative charges, registration or title fees,
                      reasonable moving expenses, and any similar costs imposed on affected persons.
                      To ensure compensation at replacement cost, planned compensation rates may
                      require updating in project areas where inflation is high or the period of time
                      between calculation of compensation rates and delivery of compensation is
                      extensive.
 Restrictions       : Refers to limitations or prohibitions on the use of agricultural, residential,
 on land use          commercial or other land that are directly introduced and put into effect as part
                      of the project. These may include restrictions on access to legally designated
                      parks and protected areas, restrictions on access to other common property
                      resources, restrictions on land use within utility easements or safety zones.
 Security       of : Means that resettled individuals or communities are resettled to a site that they
 Tenure              can legally occupy, where they are protected from the risk of eviction and where
                     the tenure rights provided to them are socially and culturally appropriate. In no
                     event will resettled persons be provided with tenure rights that are in effect
                     weaker than the rights they had to the land or assets from which they have been
                     displaced.
 Severely           : Where land-based livelihood of small-scale subsistence farming is severely
 affected             affected by substantial loss of productive land, particular attention needs to be
                      paid to fragility, including food security risks for affected households.
                      Additional fragility factors such as erosion and climate risks (drought, floods,
                      climate change trends, and so forth) should be taken into account in assessing
                      livelihood risks and developing additional support measures.
 Stakeholders       : Any and all individuals, groups, organizations, and institutions interested in and
                      potentially affected by a Project or having the ability to influence a Project.




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project

RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)



EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Introduction of the project
The Government of Viet Nam, with financial and technical support from the World Bank, is
preparing the Hai Phong Resilience Development Project (HPRDP). The project has the following
main components: (i) Component 1: Synchronous development of Thuy Nguyen urban infrastructure
to adapt to climate change; (ii) Component 2: Upgrading the environment of the Re River; (iii)
Component 3: Mitigating the central urban area and (iv) Component 4: Developing systems and
capacity to improve urban adaptation to climate change. The project is developed in the wards of
Bach Dang, Hoa Binh, Dong Hai, Luu Kiem, Thuy Nguyen, Nam Trieu, Hong Bang, An Hai, Ngo
Quyen, Gia Vien, Le Chan, An Bien, An Duong in Hai Phong city. The project aims to develop and
increase the socio-economic growth of Hai Phong city, and develop urban sustainability through an
integrated investment package focusing on urban connectivity and regional linkages, ensuring
environmental sustainability, water security and reducing urban flooding, adapting to regional
climate change, upgrading public spaces and enhancing urban resilience.
Objectives of Resettlement Plan (RP)
The main objective of this RP is to establish a set of criteria for compensation, assistance and
resettlement for project affected households (PAHs) based on the principle of full replacement cost.
PAHs will be provided with various forms of support to stabilize their lives.
Project’s impact and scope of land acquisition
The project is expected to affect approximately 2,460 households and organizations, of which there
are 2,433 individual households, equivalent to 9,245 peoples and 8 Ward People's Committees and
other organizations. There are 1,292 PAHs that will be severely affected from losing 30% or more of
total productive landholdings, 181 of AHs will need to be relocated, 175 households belonging to
vulnerable groups, and 51 households that will be affected in terms of business operations. Among
the 181 households to be relocated, there are 99 households qualify for family split. Therefore, the
project will need to arrange 280 resettlement plots for: (i) 181 households whose houses and
residential land are affected and must be relocated, and (ii) 99 households living together and are
entitled to household split. There are no affected households belonging to ethnic minority groups, as
there are no ethnic minorities in the project area.
The implementation of the project will result in permanent acquisition of 1,975,297.5 m² (197.53
hectares) of various types of land, including: annual crop land of 643,761.7 m², aquaculture land of
234,571.8 m², perennial land of 10,940.2 m², non-agricultural land of 1,071,946.2 m² land
comprising: urban residential land area of 49,605.3 m²; non-agricultural production and business land
area of 64,664.8 m²; public service facility land area of 3,092.6 m²; special-purpose water surface
land area of 642,293.7 m²; transportation works land area of 305,380.5 m²; land for construction of
belief establishments of 1,778.9 m², land for cemetery of 5,130.4m². The unused land area totals
6,501 m².
Mitigation measures to minimize the scope of land acquisition
PMU will work closely with the design consultant, and social and environmental experts to avoid
and minimize the scope of land acquisition and the level of impact in all works items of the project,
to the extent possible. Measures to minimize negative impacts are carried out through feasibility
studies and design options.
Policy and entitlement framework
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 1
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


Land acquisition, compensation, support and resettlement for the project will comply with the World
Bank’s Environmental and Social Standard 5 (ESS5: Land Acquisition, Land Use Restrictions and
Involuntary Resettlement) and the Laws and regulations of the Vietnamese government and Hai
Phong CPC on compensation, support and resettlement when land is acquired by the State. The basic
principles applied during the preparation of the resettlement plan are that all PAPs will be
compensated at replacement cost associated with restoration measures to contribute to the
improvement of living conditions compared to the pre-project stage or at least equal to the living
conditions before the project implementation.
Livelihood Restoration Program (LRP)
The Livelihood Restoration Program (LRP) is necessary to help the adversely affected households
and vulnerable households improve or at least restore their income and livelihoods to the pre- project
level. In addition, financial support and vocational training will be provided to those affected.
According to the project's policy, out of the 2,433 affected households, 1,373 households are eligible
to participate in the livelihood restoration program, in which 1,292 of AHs are severely affected by
losing 30% or more of total productive landholding and 181 relocated households. According to
occupational data from members of affected households, approximately 959 individuals are likely to
experience income impacts due to land acquisition activities, of which around 620 are of working
age. Therefore, a Livelihood Restoration Program will be prepared for the group of individuals whose
incomes are affected by land acquisition.
Implementation arrangement
The compensation, support and resettlement of the project will be under the management and
supervision of Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and Sustainable Development
Projects (HPRSDP PMU), the WPCs and Land Fund Development Center/Compensation Council of
the communes implementing the project. During the implementation process, implementing
organizations need to have close coordination with functional agencies, commune authorities and
communities in the project area to ensure that compensation, assistance and resettlement is carried
out openly, transparently and on schedule and in compliance with the approved RP.
Consultation and participation
The project's Resettlement Plan (RP) is developed in close cooperation with local authorities,
representatives of community and affected people. The authorities in the communes and
representatives of the affected households were consulted through community consultation meetings,
survey by questionnaire has been carried out for most of the households in the affected areas. The
information obtained during the consultation process is an important basis for establishing the
project's RP, including compensation, support and livelihood restoration programs. A consultation
mechanism has also been established in the RP and the Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP) for
implementation throughout the project cycle.
Monitoring and evaluation
The resettlement plan will be implemented under the supervision of then Hai Phong Project
Management Unit for Transport and Agricultural Works (PMU). And it also recruits an independent
monitoring unit/individual to monitor the implementation of the Resettlement Plan. After completion
of the project, the Independent Monitoring Unit will assess to determine whether the objectives of
the resettlement policy is achieved or not. In the event that these objectives is not achieved, the PMU
will propose further measures to achieve the objectives.
Grievance Redress Mechanism

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 2
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


To ensure that all complaints and grievances of PAPs regarding any aspect of land acquisition,
compensation and resettlement are resolved in a timely and satisfactory manner, a well-defined
grievance redressing mechanism (GRM) have been established in the RP. All PAPs, including
vulnerable PAPs, can submit any questions or complaints verbally or in writing to the GRM. If the
complainant disagrees with the handling decision, he/she has the right to complain in accordance
with the Law on Complaints. The PMU will appoint its staff in charge to monitor and follow the
grievance/complaints of the PAPs until they are completely resolved.
Cost estimate
The estimated budget for the RP implementation of the project is approximately VND
1,729,374,156,689 (equivalent to USD 65,655,814.60 with an exchange rate of 1 USD = 26,340
VND). This budget includes compensation/support costs for land and non-land assets affected by the
project, livelihood restoration programs, management and land acquisition implementation costs,
replacement cost surveys, cost for independent monitoring activity and contingency fees. The funding
for land acquisition and site clearance activities will be allocated from the counterpart fund of Hai
Phong City People's Committee.




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 3
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


I.       INTRODUCTION
1.1.     Background
1.       Hai Phong City is Viet Nam’s principal seaport and one of the five centrally administered
cities. It lies in the Red River Delta about 100 km east of Ha Noi and serves as the industrial and
logistics gateway of Northern Viet Nam. Rapid economic growth and urban expansion over the past
20 years have exerted strong pressure on urban drainage, wastewater, and transport systems.
2.      Recurrent flooding occurs in the low-lying districts of Hong Bang, Le Chan, An Duong and
Ngo Quyen because the existing river channels (Re, Tam Bac and Lach Tray) are silted, the pumping
capacity is insufficient, and the tidal influence from Lach Huyen Estuary restricts drainage. Untreated
domestic wastewater is still discharged directly into open canals, causing deterioration of water
quality and sanitary conditions.
3.      Climate-change projections from MONRE (2023) indicate sea-level rise of 0.26–0.34 m by
2050 and more frequent extreme rainfall events. Hai Phong ranks among the most climate-vulnerable
coastal cities in Viet Nam and was listed by OECD (2016) as one of 13 port cities worldwide facing
the highest potential economic losses from sea-level rise by 2070.
4.     To cope with these challenges, the Government of Viet Nam, with financial and technical
support from the World Bank, is preparing the Hai Phong Resilient and Sustainable Urban
Development Project (HPRSDP). The Project supports implementation of the National Climate
Change Strategy (Decision 896/QĐ-TTg, 2022), the National Green Growth Strategy (Decision
1658/QĐ-TTg, 2021), and the Hai Phong City Master Plan to 2040 (Vision 2050) approved by
Decision 323/QĐ-TTg (2023).
5.     The Project aims to build an integrated system for flood protection, drainage, wastewater
treatment, and transport resilience that will strengthen the city’s adaptive capacity and improve
environmental quality for approximately 1.5 million residents.
1.2.     Project Overview
6.      The Project Development Objective (PDO) is to enhance climate resilience, environmental
sustainability, and urban livability in Hai Phong City through integrated flood-risk management,
wastewater collection and treatment, and resilient transport infrastructure.
7.       Specific objectives are to:
     ❖   Reduce urban flooding and tidal inundation through rehabilitation of Re and Tam Bac Rivers,
         construction of sluice gates and pumping stations, and improvement of the city’s drainage
         network;
     ❖   Improve water-environment quality by expanding wastewater collection and treatment,
         thereby reducing pollutant loads discharged to surface waters;
     ❖   Strengthen urban connectivity and transport resilience by upgrading key corridors such as
         Ring Road No. 3 and associated bridges;
     ❖   Promote institutional capacity building for integrated flood-risk and environmental
         management consistent with the World Bank Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
1.3.     Project’s Components
8.       The HPRSDP consists of four inter-related components combining physical investments and
institutional support:


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 4
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


Component 1 – Thuy Nguyen Climate-Resilient Urban Infrastructure Development (Ring
Road No. 3)
9.      This component implements a key regional corridor connecting the northern urban area of
Hai Phong (Thuy Nguyen District) with the Hai Phong city center and the Hanoi – Hai Phong
Expressway. It will promote socio-economic integration and support safe urban expansion toward
the north bank of Cam River.
10.    Main works include:
 ❖     Construction of Ring Road No. 3: total length ≈ 18.65 km (from Km0 at the intersection
       with Hanoi – Hai Phong Expressway to Km18 + 650 at National Highway 10). The cross-
       section width is 68 m (planned), implemented in Phase 1 with a 27 m carriageway. Design
       speed 80 km/h.
 ❖     Bridges and interchanges: Construction of Ngo Quyen Bridge and Ruot Lon Bridge
       crossing Cam and Ruot Lon Rivers (total length ≈ 2.67 km), category I and special-grade
       bridges with reinforced concrete structure.
 ❖     Drainage and lighting system, green belts and safety corridors synchronized with the
       road.
11.    This component will significantly improve regional connectivity and facilitate resilient urban
development in Thuy Nguyen.
Component 2 – Re River Environmental Improvement and Wastewater System (An Duong 1
WWTP and Pumping Stations)
12.     This component aims to restore and protect the Re River as a strategic urban waterway by
improving its environmental condition and enhancing wastewater collection and treatment capacity
for the western urban area. Key works include:
 ❖     River embankment and management roads: Rehabilitation of approximately 9.5 km of
       riverbanks (4.7 km left bank, 4.8 km right bank) with revetment slopes and vertical
       reinforced-concrete walls combined with management roads (7–9 m wide).
 ❖     Drainage and wastewater collection network: Construction of interceptor sewers (D400–
       D2000) along both banks of Re River and secondary sewer branches within An Duong
       District and adjacent areas (total ≈ 15 km).
 ❖     Pumping stations: three stations (PS-01 to PS-03) with individual capacities of 5,000–
       15,000 m³/day each, transmitting wastewater to the central treatment plant.
 ❖     Construction of An Duong 1 Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP): capacity of 35,000
       m³/day (as applied in ESIA; Phase 1 in FS = 10,000 m³/day). The plant is located in An Dong
       commune, An Duong district, occupying 6.5 ha; treatment technology: combined biological
       process (A2/O – secondary sedimentation – disinfection) meeting QCVN 14:2008/BTNMT,
       Column A before discharge to Re River.
13.    The component will directly benefit about 215,000 residents in An Duong and adjacent urban
wards by reducing pollution and improving the urban water environment.
Component 3 – Central Urban Flood Control and Water Environment Improvement (Tam
Bac – Lach Tray System)
14.   This component addresses flood risks in the central urban core (Hong Bang, Ngo Quyen, Le
Chan, Hai An districts) through structural measures on the Tam Bac and Lach Tray river systems.
Main works include:
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 5
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


 ❖     Tam Bac regulating sluice and floodgate complex: new reinforced concrete gates with
       automated control to manage tidal inflows and urban runoff.
 ❖     Thuy Doi sluice and drainage pumping station: capacity ≈ 12 m³/s for storm water
       discharge into Lach Tray River.
 ❖     Rehabilitation of existing canals and box culverts: total length ≈ 7.8 km (D800–B3000),
       connecting urban wards to receiving rivers.
 ❖     Roads and embankments along Tam Bac River: improvement of 4.3 km urban
       embankment with pedestrian paths, green spaces, and lighting.
15.    These measures will reduce flooding duration and extent in the city core by 40–60 %, protect
approximately 3,500 ha of urban area, and improve water quality and amenities along Tam Bac and
Lach Tray Rivers.
Component 4 – Systems and Capacity Development for Climate-Resilient Urban
Management
16.    This component focuses on enhancing institutional capacity, data management and smart
urban governance to ensure effective implementation and operation of resilient infrastructure. It
includes:
 ❖     Development of an Integrated Flood and Drainage Management Information System
       (GIS & SCADA platform for hydraulic operations and early warning).
 ❖     Establishment of a Climate Resilience and Urban Management Center under Hai Phong
       City People’s Committee.
 ❖     Capacity-building programs for urban planning, environmental management and disaster risk
       reduction.

II.    OBJECTIVES OF THE RESETTLEMENT PLAN
2.1.   Objectives of the RP
17.     This Resettlement Plan has been developed in accordance with Vietnam's current laws and
regulations governing land acquisition, compensation, support and resettlement, as well as the WB’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) in general and Environmental and Social Standard 5
(ESS5) on Land Acquisition, Restrictions on Land Use and Involuntary Resettlement in particular.
18.    The objectives of the Resettlement Plan are:
  o    To avoid involuntary resettlement, or if unavoidable, minimize it by considering other project
       design options.
  o    To restore, at least to the pre-project levels or improve the livelihoods and living standards of
       project-affected households..
  o    To improve living standards for poor and vulnerable households.
19.    The RP aims to:
  o    Ensure accuracy and adequacy of impacts and damages on land, houses, structure and assets
       of local people and organizations.
  o    Develop criteria, conditions and entitlement for compensation, support and resettlement.
  o    Prepare resettlement sites for displaced households.
  o    Implement livelihood restoration program to mitigate impacts on households within and after
       relocation, to improve or at least maintain their living conditions and income earning capacity
       at pre-project levels.
  o    Timely and adequately provide costs for compensation, support for PAHs.
  o    Ensure land acquisition and handover to comply with implementation schedule.
  o    Encourage participation of affected people and community during preparation,
       implementation and monitoring of resettlement plan.
  o    Establish grievance redress mechanism to resolve complaints of PAHs promptly,
       satisfactorily and transparently.
  o    Establish consultation, participation and monitoring mechanism for PAHs.
20.    The RP is prepared based on the Project’s basic design. The brief information of this RP will
be incorporated in the FS to ensure the counterpart fund allocation by the Government for the Project
implementation, including compensation and resettlement budget. This RP will be updated (if
necessary) after the detailed technical design is available, and the detailed measurement survey
(DMS) and replacement cost survey (RCS) have been completed.
21.     This RP will be submitted to the Hai Phong City People’s Committee (CPC) for reviewing
and approval once receiving concurrence from the World Bank. The RP will be disclosed publicly in
the Vietnamese language and made available on the Project website(s) and made available and
accessible in the Project areas. The English version will also be publicly disclosed at the World Bank
internal and external websites.
2.2.   Scope of the RP
22.     As the land acquisition activities of the Project will negative impact to the local people in
project area, this RP is prepared covering all work items of the Project following the requirements of
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 8
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


WB ESS5. The RP will be updated reflecting any changes once the detailed technical design is
available. This RP needs to be:
  o      Updated to reflect the following key technical information: (i) Detailed Measurement Survey
         (for the actually affected households); (ii) Additional Public Consultations with newly
         identified affected households, particularly on issues related to resettlement and livelihood
         restoration; (iii) Replacement Costs Survey; (iv) Needs Assessment, particularly for those
         who are severely affected, including those who physically relocate; and (v) Resettlement
         site(s).
  o      Re-submited to Hai Phong CPC and the WB for approval prior to compensation and
         resettlement implementation.
2.3.     Methodologies for RP Preparation
23.      The following methods were used to develop the Resettlement Plan:
  i)     Data collection:
  o      Collect land use maps and cadastral maps of the project area: data sources include (i) the land
         acquisition boundaries of each investment item as supplied by feasibility study consultants
         (FS consultants); (ii) the cadastral map of the project area; and (iii) the extracted map managed
         by the cadastral officer of commune.
  o      Collect contracts for the transfer of land use rights and ownership of assets attached to land
         in the project area or surrounding area to determine replacement costs.
  ii)    The map overlay approach uses a land acquisition boundary layer (provided by the technical
         consultants) and the most recent cadastral map of the project area to construct a list of
         impacted households and assess the project's impact. This method ensures quick and
         reasonably accurate statistics on the number of affected households, the number of individuals
         living in a single house, the land types acquired, and the current land use conditions. The
         digitized database classifies households as vulnerable. The digitized database determines the
         extent of occupancy and the magnitude of the land acquisition's impact. Cadastral maps,
         which are updated annually, serve as the legal basis for land use and management in the
         project area. Based on the above list of affected households and level of impact, the
         Consultant worked with the neighborhood/hamlet heads and cadastral officers to assess the
         inventory of losses (IOL).
  iii)   The quantitative methods through a questionnaire was used to interview affected people
         randomly selected from the list of affected households (household survey). The surveys
         collected information from households on (i) demographic characteristics; (ii) occupation;
         (iii) living standards (income, expenditure, bank debt, health situation, environmental
         sanitation, water supply); (iv) production conditions; (v) social network; (vii) access to public
         services; (viii) vulnerability of affected households; (ix) ability to restore livelihoods; (x)
         selection of resettlement options (if any) and (xi) support for the project implementation. For
         the household survey using a questionnaire, a sample comprising 1,708 affected households
         participated in the IOL questionnaire survey, and 463 households were selected from the
         1,708 affected households to participate in the household socio-economic survey, accounting
         for 31%.
  iv)    The qualitative methods included (i) focus group discussions, (ii) key informant interviews,
         and (iii) field observations. The qualitative methods are applied to gain an in-depth
         understanding of the potential impacts of the projects on specific affected households, such
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                  Page | 9
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


       as (i) displaced households and/or households losing more than 30% of their productive land;
       (ii) households with production and business activities; and (iii) households with land
       acquired. 11 Focus Group Discussions (FGDs) were conducted in 11 wards, focusing on
       livelihoods, social impacts, gender, and vulnerable groups. Key Informant Interviews (KIIs):
       11 in-depth interviews were conducted. Target groups included: severely affected
       households, vulnerable households, representatives of local authorities, business households
       along the wastewater collection and drainage routes, and fishing households on the Re River.
 v)    Information disclosure and public consultation, such as rapid assessments and
       consultations with stakeholders, on-site interviews and meetings with households, community
       meetings, group discussions and social and economic surveys. A total of 16 consultation
       meetings were organized in 11 out of 13 wards within the Project area (remaining Thuy
       Nguyen and Ngo Quyen wards will be organized during the later stage due to the absence of
       residential populations), with 1,917 participants (1,145 male and 772 female). Regarding
       online consultation, the Project Owner issued Official Letter No. 1593/BQL-DA1 dated 01
       October 2025 to the Ministry of Natural Resources and Environment (MONRE) to conduct
       consultation through public disclosure on the electronic information portal for a period of 15
       days, in accordance with regulations.
 vi)   The Replacement Cost Survey (RCS) method was applied to calculate compensation unit
       rates for all assets affected by the project, in compliance with the requirements of ESS5.
       During the preparation of the Resettlement Plan (RP), a rapid assessment of replacement costs
       was conducted concurrently with the Inventory of Losses (IOL) and the socio-economic
       survey of affected households. The replacement cost assessment was undertaken by the
       Resettlement Planning Consultant in the project area during October and November 2025 to
       determine: (i) land prices as of the time of RP preparation; (ii) current market prices of trees
       and livestock; and (iii) current market prices of construction materials, labor, housing, and
       other structures. Replacement cost data were collected through interviews with: (i) project-
       affected persons; (ii) non-affected households; (iii) suppliers of construction materials; and
       (iv) representatives of local authorities and mass organizations. For the replacement cost
       assessment, 10 information forms were collected in each ward where land acquisition occurs,
       including: 03 from households with affected land, 03 from non-affected households, 03 from
       construction material suppliers, and 01 from a representative of the village or residential
       group. The replacement price shall be determined and updated at the time of resettlement
       implementation, ensuring conformity with the market price prevailing at such time. The
       competent State agency performing the function of State management over land shall select
       a land price appraisal consultancy organization or assign a qualified public non‑business unit
       to determine the replacement price applicable to the project in accordance with the law on
       land and other relevant laws. The determination of the replacement price shall be carried out
       in accordance with the land valuation methods provided in the Land Law and its
       implementing legal documents. The specific land price used as the basis for compensation for
       households and individuals whose land is recovered within the project area shall be approved
       by the Chairperson of the ward‑level People’s Committee in accordance with law.
24.    In addition to the methodologies indicated above, tools such as Microsoft Office, SPSS,
Microstation, Autocad, Hhmaps, and GIS were utilized to process and analyze data and information
from field surveys, household interviews, and loss inventories to estimate the impact of land
acquisition the project.

RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


III.   SCOPE OF LAND ACQUISITION AND RESETTLEMENT
3.1.   Mitigation Measures for Land Acquisition and Resettlement
25.     The first principle in WB's ESS5 is to avoid or minimize impacts on land acquisition and
resettlement. In cases where resettlement is unavoidable, adequate compensation rates should be
provided to the PAPs.
26.    During the project design process, the PMU worked closely with the Project Preparation
Consultant and Resettlement Experts to avoid or minimize land acquisition, and to ensure that the
scope of the impacts of land acquisition and resettlement is minimized in all work items of the project
components, including:
  ❖    Coordinate collection of current status data (topography, geology, current population status,
       technical infrastructure, flood drainage corridors, national defense land…);
  ❖    Analyse and compare multiple route options based on technical, economic, environmental,
       and social criteria, thereby proposing selected options minimising land acquisition and
       construction impacts to the maximum extent;
  ❖    Assess land acquisition and site clearance impacts of each option, prioritising options limiting
       impacts on existing residential areas and production land to the greatest extent;
  ❖    Work with local authorities and consult local opinions, incorporating reasonable
       recommendations;
  ❖    Design consultants report to the Hai Phong Project Management Unit (PMU) and competent
       authorities for review and selection of the optimal option.
27.     To minimize the impacts of the project on the HHs, including directly and indirectly affected
HHs, mitigation measures have been implemented. PMU has coordinated with the design consultancy
units of the project to carry out surveys, research on location and socioeconomic situation of each
project item to select the best design options to minimize the level of land acquisition impact of HHs.

28.     During the preparation of this RP, many consultations with different stakeholders, including
PAPs have been organized by the resettlement consultants in the project area. During consultations,
a number of issues were discussed, such as project designs, mitigation measures, compensation and
assistance policies of the project, livelihood restoration programs for severely affected HHs, to
provide suitable solutions. All residents supported the project and expected the project to be
implemented soon.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                           Page | 13
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


29.     To minimize impacts on households living on both sides of the road and river during the
construction phase, the resettlement consultants have consulted with local authorities and households
there to propose mitigation measures appropriate to each local area. For areas with high traffic
density, divide into segments of 20-30m for construction. Construct at night and restore during the
day (for positions that cannot be completed, cover with steel plates with thickness ≥2cm to ensure
safety), construct in a rolling manner, construct to where restore the site to that point (by segment).
For the Re River area, construction will be divided into small segments of 20-30m, construction
machinery will be placed on platforms/pontoons measuring 10x20m, ensuring no impact on traffic
as well as fishing activities (if any) on the river. Construct using the rolling method (construct to
where complete to there). Prioritize construction along with the existing embankment, minimizing
demolition of the existing embankment to the maximum extent. These mitigation measures will be
applied in each construction step to minimize negative impacts on local residents
30.     Despite the above efforts, land acquisition is unavoidable. In addition, temporary impacts and
community disturbances may occur during the construction period. However, all potential negative
impacts of the project are foreseeable, and mitigation measures have been proposed in the
ESIA/ESMP and RP. During the project implementation, the implementing agencies will notify
affected people 90 days and 180 days in advance of the acquisition of agricultural and residential
land, respectively. The PMU and construction supervision consultant will closely monitor the
implementation of mitigation measures by contractors and disclose the construction plan in advance
for local people to implement.
31.    Inventory of Losses (IOL) is conducted based on the preliminary design to determine the
preliminary number of affected households and the amount of land and non-land assets for the
preparation of RP. Detailed survey and measurement of affected land and non-land assets of each
affected household will be carried out when the detailed measurement design is established and
measured at the project implementation stage to prepare the compensation plan.
3.2.   Permanent Impact of the Project
32.     Among four components of the project, component 1 and component 2 requires land
acquisition for construction of roads, river embankment. Project impact on land acquisition is
substantial. An initial inventory of losses (IOL) was conducted by the PMU and social consultants
based on basic design of the road and the river to collect data and information for the preparation of
the RP. Therefore, the resettlement data provided by this RP is not the final data to be used for
compensation. Results of the IOL are summarized as follows.
3.2.1. Impacts on households and organizations
33.     It is estimated that approximately 2,460 households and organizations will be affected.
Among them, 2,433 households, equivalent to 9,245 people, will be permanently affected by the
project due to land recovery. Of these, 1,292 households (equivalent to 53.14%) will be severely
affected in their livelihoods/income (due to losing more than 30% of their total agricultural land area),
350 households affected by housing and architectural structures, of which 181 households will need
to relocate, while 169 households may self-resettle at their original location. Of the 181 households
to be relocated, there are 99 households qualifying for family split. Therefore, 280 households will
need to relocate to the designated resettlement sites. The project will also impact 175 vulnerable
households and 51 business households. There are no ethnic minority households affected, as there
are no ethnic minority communities in the project area
34.    Table below shows the summary of HHs affected by 8 wards.

3.2.2. Impacts on land
35.     According to the results of the inventory of loss (IOL), the project will permanently recover
a total area of 1,975,297.5 m2 of various types of land from 2,433 households and 27 organizations,
including:
 ❖     Land for annual crops is 643,761.7 m2 (2,080 households and 13 organizations)
 ❖     Land for aquaculture is 234,571.8 m2 (122 households and 2 organizations)
 ❖     Land for perennial crop is 10,940.2 m2 (35 households)
 ❖     Affected non-agricultural land area of 1,071,946.2 m2, including: residential land is 49,605.3
       m2 (321 households and 1 organization); non-agricultural production and business land of
       64,664.8 m2 (8 organizations); public service works land of 3,092.6 m2 (4 organizations);
       specialized water surface land of 642,293.7 m2 (8 organizations); transportation works land
       of 305,380.5 m2 (11 organizations); religious establishment land of 1,778.9 m2 (3
       organizations); cemetery land of 5,130.4 m2 (1 households and 4 organization)
 ❖     Unused land area of 6,501 m2 (3 organizations)




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                             Page | 17

3.2.5.      Impacts on business
39.     According to the IOL survey results, there are 51 households affected in business activities
across both components of the project. Among them, the highest concentration is in Bạch Đằng Ward,
An Dương Ward, and An Hải Ward.The social assessment (SA) details the description of business
impacts.

3.2.6. Impact on vulnerable households and ethnic minorities
40.    According to the inventory results, there are 175 households belonging to vulnerable groups,
and no ethnic minorities reside in the project area. Among these, there are 81 policy households, 10
poor households, 49 female-headed households with dependents, and 35 households with disabled
members, or elderly living alone without support.
3.2.7. Public assets and cultural heritages
41.     According to the damage inventory results, the land recovery area of the project partially
affects one pagoda, one worship shrine, and one communal house. During the design process, the
design consultant and the Project Management Board worked with the local authorities to avoid
relocating these structures
3.3.   Temporary Impacts
42.     Based on discussions between the Project Management Unit (PMU) and the technical design
consultant, impacts resulting from temporary land acquisition for project construction activities have
not yet been identified at the current stage. Should any such impacts be identified in subsequent steps,
supplementary assessments will be conducted, and appropriate mitigation measures will be
implemented.
43.     During the construction phase, certain households engaged in business and livelihood
activities along the construction sites of Component 2 and Component 3 will experience a certain
level of impact. According to the rapid assessment, the potentially affected households are primarily
engaged in food services, general stores, and consulting services (specifically for Component 2).
However, practical observations of streets with similar ongoing construction activities within the city
suggest that impacts on the business operations of these households are negligible. Regarding fishing
activities on the Re River, these are of a very small scale (involving approximately 20 small boats)
and serve primarily as a source of supplementary income during idle periods.
44.     To mitigate these issues, the Contractor will employ the rolling construction method
(executing short segments), conduct work at night, complete sections definitively, and restore the site
immediately in alignment with construction progress. Furthermore, should the social impact
assessment indicate that the income of affected groups is significantly reduced over an extended
period, the Project will develop a financial support plan for these households.
3.4.   Associated Facilities
45.     The ESF requires the application of ESSs to associated works that are not financed as part of
the project, but according to the assessment of the Bank: (a) directly and significantly related to the
project; and (b) are implemented, or are planned to be implemented concurrently with the project;
and (c) are necessary for the project to be viable and would not be constructed, expanded, or
implemented if the project did not exist.
46.    The project-displaced households will be allocated to two resettlement areas constructed by
the Haiphong City People's Committee for resettling land acquisition projects across the city. These
two resettlement areas will still be constructed and completed independently of the Haiphong
Resilience Development Project.

47.     In accordance with the footnote 12 of the ESF “for facilities or activities to be Associated
Facilities, they must meet all three criteria”, with the above assessment of three criteria, the Hai
Phong City Resilience Development Project does not apply “Associated Facilities” for the two
resettlement sites as not all three criteria met. The third criterion, which states that facilities “(c) are
necessary for the project to be viable and would not be constructed, expanded, or implemented if the
project did not exist,” is not satisfied in this case. The two resettlement sites in Nam Trieu and Bac
Dang wards are being developed independently by the Hai Phong City People’s Committee as part
of the city’s overall resettlement strategy. These sites are intended to accommodate resettlement
needs for multiple projects across the city, including—but not limited to—the World Bank–financed
project. Appendix 6 provides further detailed due diligent assessment.

IV.    LEGAL FRAMEWORK
4.1.   Legal Laws of Vietnam
48.    The following legal documents related to land acquisition and resettlement are currently
applied in Vietnam:
  ❖     The Constitution 2013, which came into effect on January 1, 2014 and it has been amended
        and supplemented in several articles by Resolution No. 203/2025/QH15 dated June 16, 2025.
  ❖     Law on Environmental Protection No. 72/2020/QH14 dated November 17, 2020.
  ❖     Construction Law No. 62/2020/QH14 dated June 17, 2020.
  ❖     Law amending and supplementing a number of articles of Construction Law No.
        62/2020/QH14 dated June 17, 2020.
  ❖     Land Law No. 31/2024/QH15 dated August 1, 2024.
  ❖     Law on Public Investment No.58/2024/QH15, dated Novenber 29, 2024
  ❖     Law on Complaints No. 02/2011/QH13 dated November 11, 2011.
  ❖     Law on Denunciations No. 25/2018 dated June 12, 2018 and Decree No. 31/2019/ND-CP
        dated April 10, 2019 specifically guide the provisions of the Law on Denunciations.
  ❖     Resolution No. 203/2025/QH15 of the National Assembly dated 16 June 2025 on the
        Amending and Supplementing a number of articles of the Constitution of the Socialist
        Republic of Viet Nam
  ❖     Decree No. 102/2024/ND-CP date July 30, 2024 of the Government detailing the
        implementation a number of articles of the Land Law.
  ❖     Decree No.71/2024/ND-CP dated June 27, 2024 of the Government regulating land prices;
  ❖     Decree No.88/2024/ND-CP dated July 15, 2024 stipulates compensation, support and
        resettlement when the State recovers land.
  ❖     Decree No. 124/2020/ND-CP dated October 19, 2020 specifically guides the provisions of
        the Law on Complaints.
  ❖     Decree No. 103/2024/ND-CP dated July 30, 2024 of the Government regulating land use levy
        and land rent; Decree 114/2021/ND-CP dated December 16, 2021 of the Government on the
        management and use of official development assistance (ODA) and concessional loans of
        foreign donors and donors.
  ❖     Decree No.95/2024/ND-CP dated July 24, 2024 of the Government detailing a number of
        articles of the Law on Housing.

RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

       Hai Phong City.
4.2.   The World Bank’s Land Acquisition, Restrictions on Land Use and Involuntary
       Resettlement (ESS5)
50.     In October 2018, the World Bank launched the ESF, in which the Environmental and Social
Standard 5 - Land Acquisition, Restrictions on land use, and Involuntary Resettlement (hereafter
called ESS5) - states that project-related land acquisition and land use restrictions can have a negative
impact on communities and people. Land acquisition activities or land use restrictions can result in
displacement circumstances (resettlement, loss of residential land, houses), economic impacts (loss
of land, assets, or access to assets, resulting in loss of income or other means of livelihood), or both.
We refer to these impacts as “involuntary resettlement”.
51.   Experience and research show that the displacement and economic impact can cause serious
economic, social and environmental risks if mitigation measures are not taken. These risks include
damage to the production system, poverty due to loss of income from production or other sources of
income, relocation to places with unsuitable conditions or increased competition for resources, poor
community organizations and social networks, being apart from family members, cultural identity,
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 27
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


traditions, and the ability to support each other are fading and disappearing. Therefore, involuntary
resettlement should be avoided. If the involuntary resettlement cannot be prevented, the project must
be carefully designed and carried out to reduce involuntary resettlement and, at the same time, take
the necessary steps to lessen negative effects on the residents who are subject to it and the new
community where the involuntarily resettled person settles.
52.    Therefore, ESS5 aims at:
 ❖     Avoiding involuntary resettlement, or, if unavoidable, minimizing it by considering other
       project design options,
 ❖     Avoiding coercion.
 ❖     Minimizing negative social and economic impacts from land acquisition or land use
       restrictions by: (a) providing timely compensation for lost assets at replacement cost; and (b)
       assisting displaced people in their efforts to improve or restore their livelihoods and living
       standards to pre-project levels, whichever is higher.
 ❖     Improving the living conditions of poor and vulnerable people who must relocate by
       providing adequate housing, services, and facilities, as well as protecting ownership rights.
 ❖     Recognizing and conducting resettlement activities such as Sustainable Development
       Programs, providing sufficient investment resources to create conditions for displaced people
       to benefit directly from the project, depending on the nature of the project.
 ❖     Ensuring that resettlement activities are planned and carried out with appropriate disclosure
       measures, meaningful consultation, and informed participation of affected parties.
53.     In addition, the following measures will be required to be applied to the project to achieve the
best resettlement results:
 ❖     Consult with affected people on measures proposed in the compensation, support and
       Resettlement Plan.
 ❖     Provide affected people with options for resettlement and livelihood restoration.
 ❖     Conduct compensation at full replacement costs for damages to assets other than land.
 ❖     Resettlement sites must provide living conditions at least equal to those previously enjoyed
       or in accordance with applicable minimum regulations or standards, whichever is higher.
 ❖     Provide affected people with subsidies and assistance during the relocation process,
       occupational training, and job finding to restore their income.
 ❖     Identify and support vulnerable groups to restore livelihoods.
54.    Furthermore, the procedures utilized to assess damages in WB-financed projects are full
replacement costs. For this project, damages to land, structures, and other assets, and replacement
costs will be determined as follows:
 ❖     For land, the replacement cost includes the land value determined according to the prevailing
       market price plus transaction costs (i.e. administrative fees, registration fees, ownership
       confirmation...).
 ❖     For houses and other structures, valuation is based on the market price of building materials
       and labor costs to build a new house or structure of equal or better quality and area than with
       affected houses/structures.
 ❖     For public utilities partially or completely affected by the project, the project will construct
       or repair to ensure that they are fully restored to their functions. In the case of cash
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 28
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


       compensation, it includes the market price of construction materials plus transportation costs,
       labor and contractor fees, registration fees and transfer taxes. No depreciation of assets and
       deduction of salvageable materials.
  ❖    The replacement cost survey will be carried out by an independent and professional asset
       valuation consultant. A replacement cost survey is a method of assessing compensation at the
       amount required to replace the old asset, plus the transaction expenses involved with the
       replacement. Transaction costs include administrative fees, registration fees, rights
       confirmation, reasonable relocation costs, and similar costs that affected people must bear.
4.3.   Comparison of National Laws and Regulations and World Bank’s Policies on Land
       Acquisition and Resettlement and Measures to Fill Gaps
4.3.1. Similarities between the Vietnamese Government's policies and the requirements of ESS5
55.   Vietnam's laws and practices on compensation and resettlement are comparable to the World
Bank’s guidelines on involuntary resettlement, which include:
  ❖    Vietnam promulgated procedures to compensate people with affected land who lack legal
       land use rights but can legalize their land use rights.
  ❖    Those with permanent residence can choose their preferred form of compensation, which
       includes relocation to a designated resettlement site, cash compensation, or a combination of
       the two.
  ❖    Resettlement sites for displaced people should have greater infrastructure and public
       amenities than their current location.
  ❖    Those displaced will be supported during the transition period.
  ❖    Affected people will be consulted and given the opportunity to negotiate compensation
       payments and income restoration support.
  ❖    The complaints of the affected people are handled through steps legalized under the Law on
       Complaints.
  ❖    Affected people who are not eligible for compensation for the land they occupy will be
       supported to restore their livelihoods.
4.3.2. Differences between Vietnamese Government policies and ESS5 requirements
56.   Aside from the commonalities, Vietnam's policies somewhat differ from the World Bank's
ESS5 in terms of compensation, support, resettlement, and livelihood restoration for affected people.
57.    Table 4 summarizes the main differences and measures proposed for the project to harmonize
the requirements of both Vietnam and the World Bank.




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project

V.       ELIGIBILITY AND ENTITLEMENT
5.1.      Project Affected Peoples (PAPs)
58.     Project affected people are those who are directly affected by the Project through the loss of
land, residences, other structures, business, assets, or access to resources, specifically:
  ❖       Persons whose agricultural land will be affected (permanently or temporarily) by the Project.
  ❖       Persons whose residential land/houses will be affected (permanently or temporarily) by the
          Project.
  ❖       Persons whose leased houses will be affected (permanently or temporarily) by the Project.
  ❖       Persons whose businesses, agricultural activities, occupations, or places of work will be
          affected (permanently or temporarily) by the Project.
  ❖       Persons whose crops/ trees (annual and perennial) will be affected in part or in total by the
          Project.
  ❖       Persons whose other assets or access to those assets will be affected in part or in total by the
          Project.
  ❖       Persons whose livelihoods will be affected (permanently or temporarily) due to restriction of
          access to protected areas by the Project.
5.2.      Identification of Vulnerable Groups or Households
59.     According to the World Bank's Environmental and Social Standard 5 and Vietnamese
regulations, individuals or groups of individuals who may be adversely affected by land acquisition
and resettlement and/or less able to access benefits brought by the project and property compensation,
including livelihood restoration, are considered vulnerable compared to other affected subjects of the
project. According to the initial socioeconomic surveys, the project's vulnerable groups will generally
include:
  ❖       Female-headed households with dependents and economic difficulties (single, widow,
          disabled husband).
  ❖       Poor households according to national standards.
  ❖       Disable headed household (not able to work),
  ❖       Elderly headed household without any supports
  ❖       Policy households4.
                Table 8. Distribution of vulnerable household groups by affected wards
                                  Luu          Nam        Bach                        Hong         An

                                  Kiem         Trieu      Dang                        Bang        Duong

Poor households                      0            2            3           5            0            0            0           10



4 Policy Households (hộ gia đình chính sách) refers to households entitled to special state priorities and support due to their

contributions to the revolution or their particularly difficult circumstances. The main groups classified as policy households:
Households of People with Meritorious Services to the Revolution. This is the most prioritized group, including Individuals with Merit
(Revolutionary veterans (pre-1945), Heroic Vietnamese Mothers, Heroes of the People's Armed Forces, Labor Heroes of the resistance
periods, war invalids, and those affected by chemical toxins (Agent Orange); Relatives of Martyrs: Biological parents, spouses, and
children of martyrs, or those who raised martyrs; Those entitled to war invalid policies: Civilians who lost 21% or more of their
working capacity while performing state-recognized duties.
