60.    There are special groups that may be adversely impacted or are exposed to the risks of further
impoverishment from resettlement. Hence, the Compensation Board and the Project Management
Unit, during the process of devising compensation, assistance and resettlement methods, must co-
operate with the People's Committees of communes to survey and update the list of vulnerable groups
or HHs to provide timely and proper assistance.
5.3.    Eligibility Classification
61.    Three categories of affected persons who are eligible for coverage. While people in all three
categories are entitled to assistance of some sort under the project, the nature of that assistance may
vary.
Category (a):      Affected persons who have formal legal rights to land or assets are those who have
                   formal documentation under national law to prove their rights or are specifically
                   recognized in national law as not requiring documentation. In the simplest case, an
                   area is registered in the name of individuals or communities. In other cases, persons
                   may have a lease on the land and therefore have legal rights.
Category (b):      Affected persons who do not have formal rights to land or assets, but who have a
                   recognized or recognizable claim under national law can fall into a number of
                   groups. They may have been using the land for generations without formal
                   documentation under customary or traditional tenure arrangements that are
                   accepted by the community and recognized by national law. In other cases, they
                   may never have been provided with a formal title or their documents may be
                   incomplete or lost. They may have a claim for adverse possession if they have
                   occupied land for a certain period as defined by national law, without the formal
                   owner contesting the occupation. In such cases, national law often has legal
                   procedures by which such claims can become recognized.
Category (c):      Affected persons who have no recognizable legal right or claims to the land or
                   assets they occupy or use are eligible for assistance under ESS5. These can be
                   seasonal resource users, such as herders, grazers, fishers, or hunters (although if the
                   rights of such users are recognized by national law, they may fall into category (a)
                   or (b)). They can also be persons occupying land in violation of applicable laws.
                   Affected persons in these groups are not eligible for compensation for land, but are
                   eligible for resettlement and livelihood assistance and compensation for assets.
62.     Persons covered under item (a) and (b) are provided compensation for the land they lose, and
other assistance as regulated in the Resettlement Plan. Persons covered under (c) are provided
resettlement assistance in lieu of compensation for the land they occupy, and other assistance, as
necessary, to achieve the objectives set out in this policy, if they occupy the Project area prior to a
cut-off date established by the Borrower and acceptable to the World Bank. Persons who encroach
on the area after the cut-off date are not entitled to compensation or any other form of resettlement

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                 Page | 40
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


assistance. All persons included in (a), (b), or (c) are provided compensation for loss of owned or
used assets other than land.
5.4.   The Cut-off-date
63.     As defined, a cut-off-date is the date that a State competent agency issues the announcement
of land acquisition before detailed measurements (Point 1, Article 85, Land Law 2024). PAHs and
local communities will be informed about cut-off date and information related to the Project so that
they can work out their own production/investment/construction plans, avoiding damages or losses
otherwise caused by a lack of information the Project. As the project planning (based on the basic
design) has not been approved yet. Therefore, the cut-off date has not been identified.
64.     All affected people before the cut-off date will receive compensation, support for loss of land
and assets, and restoration of livelihoods. After the cut-off date, those who are present or build
houses/structures, plant trees, or start businesses will not be eligible to receive any compensation or
assistance.
5.5.   Households Separated After the Cut-Off Date
65.     Those affected households splitting from the large families after the cut-off-date who meet
the following conditions will be eligible for resettlement benefits as stand-alone households and are
recognized as PAPs:
  ❖    Households with multiple generations or many couples living together on a plot of acquired
       land who are eligible to separate households according to the local regulations.
  ❖    Verification of commune People’s Committee that the household has split.
  ❖    Newly born children, spouses of persons named in the household registration books, people
       who have completed military service, and people who have just returned from schools to live
       with the PAHs from the cut-off date to the date of compensation payment will be entitled to
       compensation and support outlined in this document.
66.     In case the GOV regulations will be changed and there will be some entitlements, which are
better than the ones described in this document, these better entitlements will be applied for the
affected people (if possible).
5.6.   Forced Eviction
67.    The Borrower will not resort to forced evictions of affected persons. “Forced eviction” is
defined as the permanent or temporary removal against the will of individuals, families, and/or
communities from the homes and/or land which they occupy without the provision of, and access to,
appropriate forms of legal and other protection, including all applicable procedures and principles in
the ESS5.
68.     The exercise of eminent domain, compulsory acquisition or similar powers by local
authorities will not be considered to be forced eviction providing it complies with the requirements
of national law and the provisions of the ESS5, and is conducted in a manner consistent with basic
principles of due process (including provision of adequate advance notice, meaningful opportunities
to lodge grievances and appeals, and avoidance of the use of unnecessary, disproportionate or
excessive force).
69.    The prohibition against “forced eviction” does not prevent action by local authorities to
remove a person who continues to occupy land upon completion of the legal process of eminent
domain or compulsory acquisition. Eviction is not considered to be forced eviction if it conforms to
national law, including compliance with, and completion of, all relevant legal and administrative


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 41
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


procedures, including appeals processes; complies with all the relevant requirements of ESS5, and is
carried out in a way that respects basic principles of due process.
70.     Due process is understood to include the following types of procedural protections:
  (a)   an opportunity for genuine consultation with those affected.
  (b)   adequate and reasonable notice for all affected persons prior to the scheduled date of eviction.
  (c)   information on the proposed evictions, and, where applicable, on the alternative purpose for
        which the land or housing is to be used, to be made available in reasonable time to all those
        affected.
  (d)   especially where groups of people are involved, government officials or their representatives
        as well, if requested, impartial observers to be present during an eviction.
  (e)   all persons carrying out the eviction are to be properly identified.
  (f)   evictions are not to take place in inclement weather or at night, or during festivals or holidays
        unless the affected persons consent otherwise.
  (g)   provision of legal remedies.
  (h)   provision, where possible, of legal aid to persons who are in need of it to seek redress from
        the courts.
71.     Monitoring and Evaluation: The PMU must report the forced eviction to the CPC and the
World Bank to review before implementing the process. Reporting should be carried out on a regular
basis and submitted to CPC and WB for review and agreement.
72.    Independent monitoring by third party should be carried out to ensure the forced eviction
process conforms to national laws and regulations, including compliance with, and completion of, all
relevant legal and administrative procedures, including appeals processes; complies with all the
relevant requirements of ESS5, and is carried out in a way that respects basic principles of due
process.
5.7.    Valuation of Replacement Cost
73.     “Replacement cost” is defined as a method of valuation yielding compensation sufficient to
replace assets, plus necessary transaction costs associated with asset replacement. Where functioning
markets exist, replacement cost is the market value as established through independent and competent
real estate valuation, plus transaction costs. Where functioning markets do not exist, replacement cost
may be determined through alternative means, such as calculation of output value for land or
productive assets, or the undepreciated value of replacement material and labor for construction of
structures or other fixed assets, plus transaction costs. In all instances where physical displacement
results in loss of shelter, replacement cost must at least be sufficient to enable purchase or
construction of housing that meets acceptable minimum community standards of quality and safety.
74.     The valuation method for determining replacement cost should be documented and included
in relevant documents of resettlement preparation and implementation. According to the provisions
of Article 158 - Land Law 2024, the land valuation methods prescribed in the Land Law 2024 include:
(i) comparison method; (ii) income method; (iii) surplus method; and (iv) land price adjustment
coefficient method. Please see the detailed analysis and evaluation of land valuation methods in
section 14.2. The determination of specific land prices according to the above methods will be based
on the investigation, collection of information on land plots, market prices and information on land
prices in the land database, applying appropriate land valuation methods. Therefore, the
determination of specific land prices will be based on market prices, transaction/conversion prices
and are compatible and in accordance with the replacement cost principles required by ESS5. The
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 42
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


exact method to determine the specific land price will be determined by the Independent Valuation
Consultant during the compensation implementation process5.
75.    Transaction costs include administrative charges, registration or title fees, reasonable moving
expenses, and any similar costs will be included in the specific land price. In addition, to ensure
compensation at replacement cost principle, the land prices may require updating in project areas
where inflation is high or the period of time between calculation of compensation rates and delivery
of compensation is extensive.
76.     The valuation methods are presented in detail in Appendix 1 of the report. According to the
World Bank: Replacement cost is defined as a method of valuation yielding compensation sufficient
to replace assets, plus necessary transaction costs associated with asset replacement. Land valuation
methods are conducted in accordance with the Government's Decree No. 71/2024/ND-CP dated June
27, 2024, regulating land prices, and the Government's Decree No. 226/2025/ND-CP dated August
15, 2025, amending and supplementing a number of articles of decrees detailing the implementation
of the Land Law.
77.     Transaction costs include administrative charges, registration or title fees, reasonable moving
expenses, and any similar costs imposed on affected persons. To ensure compensation at replacement
cost, planned compensation rates may require updating in project areas where inflation is high or the
period of time between calculation of compensation rates and delivery of compensation is extensive.

VI.       COMPENSATION, SUPPORT, AND RESETTLEMENT POLICY
6.1.     Required Waivers
78.    To comply with Environmental and Social Standard 5 (ESS5) on land acquisition, restrictions
on land use and involuntary resettlement, articles in the laws and regulations of Vietnam that do not
guarantee the PAP’s right to compensation at replacement costs, or eligibility articles that do not
extend the right of being restored and/or assisted to households without valid land papers, or
otherwise limit the compensation required by WB ESS5, will not apply. The requirements of WB
ESS5 will fully apply in all cases.
79.     As a World Bank Group member, the Government of Vietnam has committed that if
international conventions signed by the government and the World Bank contain provisions that
differ from those in Vietnam's current resettlement legal framework, the provisions of international
agreements with the World Bank will supersede (Clause 2, Article 40, Land Law 2024)
80.    The basic principle of managing and using official development assistance (ODA) loans and
concessional loans from foreign donors, as outlined in Article 46 of Decree No. 114/2021/ND-CP
dated December 16, 2021 and Decree No.20/2023/ND-CP dated May 4th 2023 (amendment,
supplement to the Decree No.114/2021), is to “Comply with the current regulations and the
international treaties on the ODA to which Vietnam is a member. If there is a discrepancy between
the regulations of the Government of Vietnam (GoV) and the provisions of international treaties, the
provisions of international treaties will supersede”.
6.2.      Principles and Objectives
81.    The principles mentioned in WB ESS5 are used for the preparation of this RP. The following
principles and objectives will be applied:



5 The Independent Valuation Consultant may use one or more of the four methods mentioned above, depending on the specific

conditions of each locality and the availability of input data.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                               Page | 43
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


 (i)    Land acquisition and asset impacts as well as resettlement of DPs must be minimized as far
        as possible.
 (ii)   All PAPs residing, working, doing business or farming in the project areas will be provided
        with rehabilitation measures, sufficient enough for them to improve or at least maintain their
        living standards, income earning and production capacity the same as their pre-project
        conditions. Lack of legal rights to acquired land will not prevent PAPs from their entitlement
        to access such rehabilitation measures.
 (iii) Plans for land acquisition and other assets and provision of rehabilitation measures must be
       taken under the consultation with PAPs to minimize their disturbance. Entitlements shall be
       provided to PAPs prior to the expected commencement of works at the respective project
       areas.
 (iv) Existing public services shall be maintained or improved.
 (v)    Budget for resettlement shall be available in the project implementation stages.
 (vi) The executing organization must ensure that the design, planning, consultation and
      implementation of the RAP is effectively and timely.
 (vii) Checking, monitoring and evaluating the implementation of RAP timely and effectively
       should be conducted.
 (viii) All PAPs who have assets within or reside within the area of project land acquisition before
        the cut-off date are entitled to compensation for their losses as per this RP. Those who have
        lost their income and/or subsistence will be eligible for livelihood rehabilitation assistance
        based on the criteria of eligibility defined by the project in consultation with the PAPs. If, by
        the end of the project, livelihoods have been shown not to be restored to pre-project levels,
        additional measures should be considered.
 (ix) The WB's ESS5 give priority to "land for land" option for the agricultural land acquired. If
      the "land for land" option is impossible, then the compensation in cash at replacement cost
      will be applied. Agricultural land that is lost will be compensated with replacement land of
      equivalent economic value; in cases where the project cannot allocate sufficient land fund for
      equivalent compensation, cash at the full replacement cost. These PAPs will be assisted in
      their livelihood subsistence and making their own arrangements for relocation.
 (x)    PAPs who must relocate will be resettled as regulated; their houses, lands and other properties
        affected by the project will be compensated in cash at full replacement cost.
 (xi) Compensation for all residential, commercial, or other structures will be offered at the
      replacement cost, without any of the structure and without deduction for salvageable
      materials.
 (xii) The PAPs will be provided with a transportation allowance for transporting personal
       belongings and assets to a new resettlement place, in addition to the compensation at
       replacement cost of their houses, lands, and other properties.
 (xiii) Land acquisition for the project will be announced to PAPs by a state competent agency at
        least 90 days prior to the acquisition for agricultural land and 180 days for non- agricultural
        land. The announced contents will include a plan of land acquisition, investigation, surveys,
        and detailed measurements.
 (xiv) Transfer of the acquired lands to the project will be completed within 30 days of the PAPs
       receiving full compensation or assistance from the project.
 (xv) Public services and resources at the resettlement site will be improved to be better than those
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 44
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


         in the PAP’s previous location.
  (xvi) Temporary resettlement: Relocation of any households more than once, should be avoided
        because it leads to PAPs being impacted twice or more and will delay the livelihood
        restoration process. If this happens, these households should be considered for additional
        benefits as they have been impacted twice. Temporary resettlement will only occur if the
        PMU has verified that temporary resettlement is unavoidable for reasons such as:
  ❖      DPs who are planning to resettle in the Project resettlement site are requested to hand over
         their land to the Project, but the Project resettlement site is not ready to receive them.
  ❖      PAPs whose houses are partly affected and require rebuilding and repair, need temporary
         resettlement in the period during which their houses are being of rebuilt or repaired.
  ❖      DPs who select the self-relocation option need temporary resettlement while searching for a
         new residence.
  (xvii)If it is unable to contact the affected household to pay compensation and support despite
        numerous announcements in the media (TV, newspapers, radio, etc.) for the regulated time,
        the compensation and support amount will be deposited into an escrow account opened at a
        commercial bank with interest to avoid disrupting the project's progress while ensuring the
        compensation payment when possibly getting in touch with these affected households.
6.3.     Project Policies on Compensation, Support and Resettlement
6.3.1. Compensation for Agricultural Land
6.3.1.1. Land users eligible for compensation (Legal or legalizable land users)
82.   PAPs will receive compensation in cash for affected agriculture land and assets on the land at
100% replacement cost.
  •      If the remaining land is not economically viable to continue production (for annual crop land,
         the minimum area is 200m²; for perennial crop land, the minimum area is 150m²; for
         aquaculture land, the minimum area is 1,000m²; for other agricultural land, the minimum area
         is 360m²) 6, the Project will acquire the entire area and provide compensation in cash at 100%
         replacement cost.
  •      In addition, PAPs will receive detailed support described in the item below. If the affected
         land is equal to 30% or more of total arable landholding, PAPs will be eligible to participate
         in the Livelihood Restoration Program (LRP) based on their desires.
  •      If the land area to be acquired is 30% or more of total production area or the remaining area
         is not economically feasible, the affected people will be compensated in cash with full
         replacement costs for the acquired area plus training/job creation support and a life
         stabilization, and will be eligible to LRP such as agricultural extension, vocational training,
         access to credit, or other measures based on the aspirations of the affected people.
  •      If the land area to be acquired is less than 30% of total production area and the acquired land
         area is not lower than the minimum land area for separating into smaller land plots according
         to the regulations of the CPC, based on the extent of impact on the livelihoods of household
         groups (the level of impact will be determined by the project's independent monitoring




6 The minimum land area thresthold is stipulated in Article 12 of Decision No. 31/2024/QD-UBND of the Hai Phong CPC dated

October 26, 2024.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                                   Page | 45
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


       consultant), households will receive financial assistance equivalent to the support provided to
       vulnerable groups under the project.
6.3.1.2. Land users have no legal rights or claims to the land
 •     Following the project policy, the support and restore livelihoods shall be provided for all
       affected people regardless of their legal status or land use rights. If acquired agricultural land
       used before July 1, 2014 will be compensated at 100% of the replacement cost. If agricultural
       land used after 1 July 2014 until the cut-off date (date of land acquisition notification) and
       affected persons whose livelihoods are primarily depended on that land will be provided with
       financial assistance, in lieu of land compensation, sufficient to meet the objectives of the
       World Bank standards on land acquisition, land use restriction and involuntary resettlement
       (to restore livelihoods to pre-project levels).
 •     Residential land and non-agricultural land will be supported at least 50% of the replacement
       cost of the land.
 •     If the above measures are insufficient to re-establish residence or livelihood with security of
       tenure rights, the affected people shall be provided with additional assistance to ensure that
       the ESS5 objectives are met.
 •     Households that encroach the project site after the cut-off date will not receive compensation
       or support.
6.3.1.3. Land tenant
 •     PAPs who are currently renting land managed by the State or state-designated owner on a
       contractual basis for agricultural, forestry, or aquaculture purposes (excluding land under
       special use forests and protected forests), will be compensated for crops, trees and other assets
       on land in cash at 100% replacement cost, while PAPs will be assisted in recovering the loss
       of investments made in the affected land equivalent to 30% of the affected land value at
       replacement cost approved by Hai Phong CPC. PAPs will also receive additional support for
       income rehabilitation if they are directly involved in agricultural activities as per
       Government’s regulations.
 •     Where PAPs are renting land on a contractual basis with individuals, organizations, or
       households but are other than specified as point (i) above, they will receive compensation for
       crops, trees and other assets on land in cash at 100% replacement cost.
 •     Where PAPs are using the rented land under a contract with individuals, organizations or
       households subject to the provisions of point (ii) mentioned above, but the contract expired
       at the cut-off date, they will be considered for support no more than 70% of the level specified
       in point (ii).
6.3.2. Compensation for Non-Agricultural Land
83.   PAPs whose land for non-agricultural production and business is acquired will be
compensated as follows:
 •     All PAPs with LURC or legalizable: (a) if land in the locality is available and at PAP’s choice,
       “land for land” compensation is priority; and (b) if land is unavailable or at the PAP’s choice,
       they will receive compensation in cash for loss of land and assets on land at 100% replacement
       cost or land with different using purpose or housing for loss of affected agriculture land.
       (Clause 1, Artical 96, Land Law 2024).
 •     PAPs who have no recognizable legal right or claim to the land or assets they occupy or use
       are entitled to receive financial assistance with an amount determined by the CPC for the loss
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 46
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


         of assets other than land, and other improvements to the land, at replacement costs. If the
         assistance is not sufficient to obtain secure tenure on a viable plot at an alternative site then
         additional assistance will be provided to meet the standard. Severely affected persons and
         vulnerable households will be provided with an allowance to ensure their livelihood
         restoration.
  •      PAPs who rent lands with annual rent payment or lump-sum rent payment but were rental
         exempted will not be compensated for lands but compensated for their investments equivalent
         to the remaining values invested in such lands and assets on the land at 100% replacement
         cost.
84.    In case household/individual using agricultural land or non-agricultural land is not used for
residential purpose eligible for land-for-land compensation according to Article 95 of the Land Law
2024 wishes to receive residential land or housing provided that land/housing fund in the locality is
available, they will be provided residential land or resettlement housing. (Clause 6, Artical 111, Land
Law 2024).
6.3.3. Compensation for Residential Land
6.3.3.1. Land users eligible for compensation (Legal or legalizable land users)
85.     The Project affected land-users will be compensated in the form of “land-for-land” or housing
or in cash at 100% of replacement cost or land with different using purpose for losing of residential
land. (Clause 1, Artical 98, Land Law 2024).
86.     If the affected people's residential land is acquired but the remaining land is not suitable for
living (7), it cannot be used to build a new house), the project will acquire the remaining land if the
affected people agree and provide cash compensation at 100% replacement cost. Eligible affected
individuals may select one of the following options:
  •      Those who opt for the “resettlement plot” compensation will receive cash compensation,
         enabling them to purchase a standard plot of land or apartment at the province's resettlement
         site. Affected individuals will receive a free land or apartment use certificate. The affected
         person will receive the difference if the compensation amount exceeds the price of the land
         plot or apartment in the resettlement area. If the compensation amount is less than the price
         of the land lot or apartment in the resettlement area, the project will pay the difference so that
         the affected person can own that land lot or apartment.
  •      If the affected individuals opt for cash compensation and/or self-relocation, they will receive
         cash compensation at replacement cost, which includes relocation assistance. Self-relocating
         people who qualify for resettlement will be provided with an amount of money equivalent to
         the infrastructure investment for a minimum plot of land or apartment in the resettlement area.
         The level of support is determined and decided by the Commune People's Committee at the
         time of land acquisition implementation.
87.    If the remaining land is not enough to rebuild the house, but there is a pond/garden/agricultural
land on the same acquired land, the affected person can propose to convert part of the
pond/garden/agricultural land into residential land according to the regulations of the Provincial
People's Committee for on-site resettlement.

formed land plot is 3.5 meters; the minimum depth of a newly formed land plot is 3.5 meters; and newly formed land plots must ensure
that the narrowest cross-section of the plot is greater than or equal to 2 meters.

88.     Those eligible for compensation for the disputed acquired land will receive 100% of the
replacement cost. However, this person will only receive compensation after the dispute has been
resolved. To prevent unnecessary project delays and ensure compensation payment after the dispute
resolution, we will deposit the compensation amount into an ascrow account in a commercial bank
with interest during the dispute resolution process.
6.3.3.2. Land users have no legal rights
89.     Land users without land use right certificates may still be eligible for land compensation if
they meet the conditions for issuance of Land Use Right Certificates and certificates of ownership of
assets attached to land as prescribed by the Land Law. For land occupied illegally or used for
incorrect purposes but with stable housing constructed prior to July 1, 2024, where land use complies
with planning, has no disputes, compensation for land may be considered depending on the time of
violation and construction safety corridor boundaries.
90.     For land users who have no recognizable land use right, financial assistance according to
decision of the CPC will be provided.
6.3.4. Compensation for Houses and Structures
91.    Regardless of their titles to the affected land or possession of a construction permit for the
affected structures/houses(8) compensation or support in cash will be made for all affected private-
owned houses/structures at 100% of the replacement costs. The replacement cost is counted for
rebuilding the new houses/structures to a similar standard without deductions of depreciation or
salvageable materials.
  •       For houses/structures that are partly affected, but the remaining area is not viable,
          compensation or assistance in cash will be made at 100% of the replacement cost for the
          whole affected houses/structures.
  •       In case the remaining area of the affected houses is sufficient to be repaired for living, the
          DPs will be paid in cash at 100% of the replacement cost for the dismantled area, including
          the demolished part from Right of Ways (ROW) to the nearest bearing frame. Additionally,
          the affected person (BAH) will receive a 10% support on the compensation value for the
          current value of the demolished portion (Article 14 of Decree No. 88/2024/ND-CP (or apply
          the support policy of PPC, whichever is higher) to assist the PAPs in restoring the
          houses/structures affected to former or better conditions. It should be noted that the houses
          fully demolished will not be applied this assistance amount.
  •       The categories and technical standards of house/structures will be determined by the local
          competent agencies in accordance with the national laws and regulations on construction.
92.     PAPs who have no recognizable legal right or claim the land or assets they occupy, or use are
entitled to receive financial assistance for the loss of assets other than land, and other improvements
to the land, at replacement costs.
  •       Where the affected person is living in a house/structure, has to be relocated and has no other
          place to live in the ward/commune, he/she will be supported with an amount in lieu of land
          compensation or resettlement arrangements sufficient for them to restore their standards of
          living at a suitable alternative site.

6.3.5. Compensation/support for Tenants
93.     Tenants who are renting and residing in state-owned rental housing shall be supported in
accordance with Articles 10 and 19 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-UBND dated
September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee: (i) shall not be compensated
for the land area and housing owned by the State but shall be fully compensated in cash at
replacement value for renovation, repair, and upgrade works; (ii) supported with rental housing at
the resettlement area; the rental price shall be the rental price for state-owned housing; housing rented
at the resettlement area may be sold by the State to the current tenant in accordance with the law on
housing; (iii) if having no other residence in the commune, ward, or special zone but requiring
allocation of residential land, the commune-level People's Committee, based on the local land fund,
shall consider supporting the allocation of 01 (one) residential land plot with land use fee collection
as prescribed; and (iv) in case of self-arranging residence, supported with a one-time cash amount of
100 million VND.
94.    Tenants who are residing in leased private houses will be provided with a transportation
allowance for moving assets to their new residential areas. For the vulnerable tenants as defined in
this RP, in addition to transportation allowance, they will get additional assistance according to
CPCs’ regulations.
6.3.6. Compensation for Trees, Crops and Livestock
95.     Affected people will be compensated in cash for the full replacement costs at the time of
compensation for crops, harvests, and livestock on the land, regardless of the legal status of the land.
Compensation for crops and livestock shall be implemented in accordance with Article 103 of the
Land Law and Articles 7 and 13 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-UBND dated September
24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee: (i) compensation level for annual crops
shall be calculated based on the yield value of the harvest for such crops; (ii) compensation level for
perennial crops shall be calculated based on the actual damage value of the tree garden; (iii)
compensation level for livestock shall be 100% of the livestock value determined by market value or
legal and reasonable investment costs into the livestock at the time of inventory for the compensation
plan. For movable livestock not yet at harvest time, support shall be provided for relocation costs
equivalent to 30% of the compensation price for the same type of livestock as promulgated by the
CPC. For unharvested crops that can be relocated to another location, compensation shall be provided
for relocation costs and actual damages incurred due to relocation and replanting.
6.3.7. Compensation for Income and/or Business/Production Assets
96.     Pursuant to the provisions of Article 12 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-UBND
dated September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee, the following policies
will apply to those who lose income and/or business/production assets due to land acquisition for the
project:
 •     Support for stabilizing production and business: All businesses and business households with
       business registration licenses that have affected income will receive compensation or support
       equivalent to 30% of their actual annual income based on the average income of the last three
       years declared to the tax authority. For households that do not have a business license but
       have fulfilled their tax obligations will be compensated equivalent to a half of support level
       for registered businesses.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 49
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


 •     Employees of state production and business establishments, as well as agencies affected by
       land acquisition, will receive benefits comparable to the stipulated minimum pay throughout
       the conversion period (up to 6 months) and will be aided in finding new employment.
 •     If the business must relocate, the project will assist in finding an alternative location with
       similar location and physical conditions to the affected location so that the business can easily
       reach basic customers, satisfy the business's requirements, or compensate in cash for the
       affected land and assets on the land at replacement cost, as well as support for transportation
       costs of movable assets.
97.     This compensation and support will be monitored throughout project implementation. In case
the livelihoods of the affected people are not restored, the project will adjust support to meet the ESS
5. The livelihoods of the affected people will be monitored until it is confirmed that they have been
restored to pre-project levels.
6.3.8. Compensation for Affected Public Utilities
98.     Public infrastructure directly related to community livelihoods and uses, such as irrigation
canals, water supply, schools, health centres, roads, electricity poles, telephone and transmission
cables (except for structures with construction permits requiring relocation when necessary) damaged
by the project will be restored or repaired as soon as possible after consultation with the owner and
the affected community. Affected communities will not be responsible for any repair expenditures.
6.3.9. Compensation for Grave Relocation
99.    Pursuant to the provisions of Article 9 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-UBND
dated September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee, grave relocation shall
include costs for excavation, relocation, reburial, and other related costs. Excavation, exhumation,
and reconstruction costs shall range from VND 5 million to VND 20 million per grave depending on
the case. For graves with special decorations having separate design estimates, the compensation
organization shall prepare the compensation plan based on the design documentation as prescribed.
Depending on the relocation distance, grave relocation costs shall range from VND 1,500,000 to
VND 3,500,000 per grave. Other costs shall include new urn replacement at VND 3,000,000 per
grave and incense, flowers, and offerings at VND 2,000,000 per grave. For graves relocated without
family members performing the relocation, the Cemetery Management Board shall be paid VND
500,000 per grave to cover incense, flowers, and offerings costs.
100. In case of self-arranging grave relocation outside the designated area with confirmation from
the Ward People's Committee of the receiving location, additional land cost support of VND
20,000,000 per grave shall be provided.
101. The ward-level People's Committee shall be responsible for allocating planned cemetery land
funds for grave relocation upon land recovery. Where the Ward People's Committee area with
recovered land has no remaining land fund for allocation, it shall proactively review and report to the
City People's Committee for arrangement of land funds at planned cemeteries in adjacent communes,
wards, or special zones near the recovered land area to facilitate procedures and family grave
maintenance.
6.3.10. Compensation for Other Assets
102. Other assets of households affected by the project will be compensated in cash at the new
installation price.




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 50
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


6.3.11. Compensation for Temporary Impacts During the Construction Phase
103. In case of temporary use of land for construction, after returning it to land users, in addition
to compensation for assets on land like permanently affected people, they will also be provided the
rental cost as agreed with the AHs.
6.3.12. Compensation for Impacts That Arise During the Project Implementation
104. Any other impacts and business interruptions identified during the project implementation
will be compensated in accordance with the provisions of this Resettlement Plan and ESS 5.
6.3.13. Support During the Transition Period
105. In addition to receiving payment for property damage, impacted individuals will get
assistance with transition expenses. Rising costs and inflation are considered in the supports at the
time of payment. The supports include, but is not limited to, the following:
6.3.13.1. Support for career training, change and job search
106. Pursuant to the provisions of Article 14 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-UBND
dated September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee, affected persons, or
those whose agricultural land area is affected, will be supported with cash calculated at 05 times the
price of agricultural land of the same type and location in the land price table promulgated by the
City People's Committee for the entire recovered land area; the supported area shall not exceed the
local agricultural land allocation limit.
107. The Ward People's Committee shall, based on the training, job conversion, and job search
support mechanism and policies prescribed by the Prime Minister and the City People's Committee,
implement the preparation, appraisal, and approval of the training, job conversion, and job search
plan for working-age persons in the locality and organize implementation as prescribed..
6.3.13.2. Support for life and production stability
Life stabilization: Pursuant to the provisions of Article 11 as stipulated in Decision No.
171/2025/QĐ-UBND dated September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee,
the life stabilization support shall be specifically stipulated as follows:
 •     Households affected from 30% to below 70% of total productive land will receive cash
       support equivalent to 30kg of rice per person for 3 months if not relocation and 6 months if
       relocation. The support period is 12 months for moving to areas with particularly difficult
       socio-economic conditions
 •     Households affected by more than 70% of the agricultural land area will receive cash support
       equivalent to 30kg of rice per person for 12 months if they do not must move, or 24 months
       if they do. The support period is 36 months for moving to areas with particularly difficult
       socio-economic conditions.
108. In addition, the following subjects shall receive life stabilization support due to the potential
impact on household livelihoods resulting from the project's land recovery:
 •     Households losing less than 30% of their total production land area or with remaining land
       not meeting the minimum land size requirements for the affected land type as stipulated by
       the City People's Committee, and experiencing livelihood impacts (severity to be determined
       by the project's IMC), shall receive financial support equivalent to the vulnerable household
       allowance of VND 2 million per month for 6 month.
 •     Households and individuals currently using land who are ineligible for land compensation, or
       who have received land under contract allocation for agricultural, forestry, aquaculture, or

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 51
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


       salt production purposes from state-owned agricultural and forestry farms, agricultural and
       forestry companies converted from such state farms, agricultural production collectives, or
       agricultural cooperatives and have a land allocation contract, shall be provided with support
       for livelihood and production stabilization for a period of 03 months.
Production stabilization:
109. Pursuant to the provisions of Clause 1 Article 12 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-
UBND dated September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee, households
and individuals subject to agricultural land recovery (including contracted land) shall be entitled to
one-time cash support at the level equal to 30% of the price of agricultural land of the same type and
location per m² recovered. The compensation land price shall be determined according to the land
prices prescribed in the City's land price table.
Support for movement and temporary accommodation:
110. Relocation support: Individuals who are affected and must relocate to a new location will be
provided with financial support in the form of cash assistance (Article 15, Decision No.
171/2025/QD-UBND).
111. Compensation for property relocation costs: Households and individuals owning houses
attached to residential land, which must relocate due to land acquisition by the State, shall be
compensated for dismantling, relocation, and reinstallation costs at a rate from VND 10,000,000 to
VND 20,000,000 per household, depending on the destination area.
112. House renting/accommodation allowance: Households required to resettle shall be entitled to
support for rental or temporary accommodation costs pursuant to city regulations during the period
calculated according to the investment project schedule as set forth in the investment project initially
approved by the competent state authority. The minimum support level shall be 5 million đồng per
household per month for households with fewer than 03 members; 08 million VND per month for
households with 3 or more members. The resettlement plan must be clearly consulted with affected
households to minimise the temporary accommodation period, avoiding impacts on income-
generating activities and livelihoods.
113. Land use rights certificates: For resettled households, all costs related to issuing land use
rights certificates for their new land/house – whether within the project's resettlement area or
elsewhere (if the affected person self-relocates) – will be covered by the project. For resettled
households whose land and house are partially affected, the costs related to updating the land use
rights certificate will be paid for by the project.
Support for vulnerable households:
114. In addition to the compensation and assistance measures stipulated under the policy
framework, the project proposes a specific support policy for vulnerable groups, including: (i)
female-headed households with dependents that face economic hardship (single, widowed, or with
disabled husbands); (ii) individuals with physical or mental disabilities who are unable to work; (iii)
poor households identified in accordance with the criteria of the Ministry of Labor, Invalids and
Social Affairs; and (iv) elderly persons living alone. All of these vulnerable households will receive
additional one-time cash assistance equivalent to VND 2,000,000 per month for a duration of six
months.
Other allowances (Incentive bonus):
Pursuant to the provisions of Clause 2 Article 15 as stipulated in Decision No. 171/2025/QĐ-UBND
dated September 24, 2025, issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee, persons possessing
assets on land subject to recovery who comply with and execute the demolition and relocation of
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 52
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


assets on such land, and hand over the site, shall be entitled to progress bonuses as follows: (i) prior
to the date of approval of the compensation plan and not falling within cases subject to compulsory
inventory decisions, they shall be entitled to a cash progress bonus equivalent to 5% of the value of
compensated assets but not exceeding VND 20,000,000 per household (or per case); and (ii) site
handover after the date of approval of the compensation and support plan but prior to issuance of the
land recovery decision, and previously not falling within cases subject to compulsory inventory
decisions or compulsory enforcement of inventory: the support level shall be a cash amount
equivalent to 5% of the value of compensated and supported assets, with a maximum limit of VND
10,000,000 per household (or per case).
115. In addition to the above supports, based on the actual situation, the project may consider other
supports to support the process of stabilizing people's lives, including agricultural production and
other income generating activities of the affected person.
6.3.13.3. Requirement on escrow account
116. In certain cases, where repeated efforts to contact absentee owners have failed, where PAPs
have rejected compensation that has been offered to them in accordance with the approved plan, or
where competing claims to the ownership of lands or assets are subject to lengthy legal proceedings.
On an exceptional basis, with prior agreement of the Bank, and where the Borrower demonstrates
that all reasonable efforts to resolve such matters have been taken, the Borrower may deposit
compensation funds as required by the plan (plus a reasonable additional amount for contingencies)
into an interest-bearing escrow or other deposit account and proceed with the relevant project
activities. Compensation placed in escrow will be made available to eligible persons in a timely
manner as issues are resolved.
6.4.   Entitlement Matrix
117. An entitlement matrix was established for the project, which integrated government policies
and regulations of Hai Phong city on compensation, support and resettlement, as well as the World
Bank's ESS5.

VII. SOCIO-ECONOMIC CONDITION IN THE PROJECT AREA
7.1.     Objectives and Methods of Socio-Economic Survey (SES)
7.1.1. Objectives
118. The socio-economic survey of affected households helps to understand the general context of
the project area and the current socio-economic situation of the affected households. The socio-
economic survey provides inputs to prepare resettlement tools and develop livelihood restoration
measures related to the situation of households to ensure the sustainability of the project benefits.
119. Specifically, the Socio-Economic Survey (SES) aims to collect information about affected
households, such as (a) Demographic characteristics, (b) Occupation, (c) Living standard ( income,
expenditure, loan, health status, environmental sanitation, etc. the participation of the affected
people..., (d) The affected households under the vulnerable group, (e) The impact of the project on
people's assets, (f) Consultation with PAPs on potential impacts and mitigation measures, (g)
Resilience of their livelihoods, (h) Priority to the settlement solutions, and (i) Project implementation
support.
7.1.2. Survey method
120. A combined qualitative and quantitative method is used for SES, including in-depth interview,
focus group discussion, rapid assessment and sample survey. In addition, document review and field
observations are also used to collect data and information:
a.       Desk study
121. Relevant documents have been collected, reviewed, researched and analyzed/evaluated,
including: project proposal report, feasibility study report of the project; cadastral maps, planning
maps, socio-economic reports, environmental and social frameworks of the World Bank (ESF) and
guidelines, Land Law 2024 and related decrees, circulars and decisions of Hai Phong city, especially
Environmental and Social Standard No. 5 (ESS5), which have been compared with the land law 2024
and related decrees to determine the relevant different contents and propose corresponding mitigation
measures.
b.       Qualitative methods
122. The consultant conducted group discussions, in-depth interviews and collected the following
secondary documents
     ❖   Group discussions with People's Committees of communes, group discussions with design
         consultant and PMU.
     ❖   In-depth interviews with leaders of People's Committees of ward.
     ❖   Collecting secondary documents at the People's Committees of communes, including: Report
         on implementation of socio-economic tasks in tasks in the first 9 months of 2025, report on
         activities of Women's Union and Farmers' Union; Cadastral map of the commune.
123. Consultation, focus group discussions and exchanges with various stakeholders including
implementing agencies, civil society organizations, representatives of local leaders, severely affected
households, and vulnerable groups. Specifically:
     ❖   Community meetings: 11 meetings have been conducted at 11 headquarters of the People's
         Committees of communes affected by the project of which 135/306 women accounted for
         44.1%. Participants included representatives from the client, consultancy unit, local

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 62
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


         government, mass organizations, village chiefs/deputy chiefs and households directly
         affected by the project, beneficiaries and/or interested parties.
     ❖   In-depth interviews: 11 in-depth interviews have been conducted with representatives of some
         affected households and severely affected households.
     ❖   Focus group discussions: 11 focus group discussions have been conducted with participants
         including village heads and beneficiaries (groups of 3-10 people).
c.       Quantitative methods
124. Consultant has implemented the following methods
     ❖   Integrate the design map of master plan with the cadastral map to identify households within
         the site clearance area of the subproject.
     ❖   Interviewed 463 affected households by questionnaire.
     ❖   Quantitative processing by the lastest version of SPSS software.
7.2.     Socio-Economic Condition in Hai Phong City
7.2.1. Geographical location
125. Hai Phong is a coastal city in the Red River Delta region, with the following geographic
location: To the north, it borders Quang Ninh Province and Bac Ninh Province; to the west and south,
it borders Hung Yen Province; to the east, it borders the Gulf of Tonkin within the East Sea. The
extreme points of Hai Phong City are
     ❖   Northernmost point: Nguyen Trai Ward.
     ❖   Westernmost point: Cam Giang Commune.
     ❖   Southernmost point (mainland): Hoang Hoa Tham Village, Vinh Hai Commune.
     ❖   Southernmost point (islands): Bach Long Vi Special Zone.
     ❖   Easternmost point (mainland): Do Son Cape, Do Son Ward.
     ❖   Easternmost point (islands): Bach Long Vi Island, Bach Long Vi Special Zone.
126. On June 12, 2025, the National Assembly issued Resolution No. 202/2025/QH15 on the
arrangement of provincial-level administrative units (effective from June 12, 2025). Accordingly,
Hai Duong Province is merged into Hai Phong City. Following the merger, Hai Phong City has a
natural area of 3,194.72 km² and a population of 4,664,124 people.
127. Hai Phong holds a strategic location, serving as the maritime gateway connecting the entire
Northern region to the world. Therefore, the city's seaport system was prioritized for investment and
expansion from a very early stage. During the late 19th and early 20th centuries, Hai Phong was
developed by the French into a commercial and financial center, and most notably, a renowned
seaport in the Pacific. By the early 20th century, Hai Phong Port had established close connections
with numerous major ports in Southeast Asia, Asia, Oceania, North America, the Indian Ocean rim,
the Mediterranean, the Atlantic, and the North Sea...
128. Hai Phong is one of the few localities in Northern Vietnam that possesses all 5 essential modes
of transport, including: road, sea, rail, inland waterway, and air transport.
     ❖   Road Transport System: The road system in Hai Phong is strongly developed, acting as a vital
         link connecting with neighboring provinces and international regions.
     ❖   Expressways: The Hanoi – Hai Phong Expressway (CT.04) is a crucial route that significantly
         shortens travel time between the two major cities. The Hai Phong - Ha Long Expressway

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                             Page | 63
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


       (CT.06) connects the Northern key economic development triangle (Hai Phong - Hanoi -
       Quang Ninh). Additionally, the Coastal Expressway (Quang Ninh - Hai Phong - Ninh Binh)
       is currently under development.
 ❖     National Highways: Including National Highway 5, National Highway 10, and National
       Highway 37, connecting Hai Phong with other areas within and outside the province.
 ❖     Urban Traffic: The network of streets and bridges (such as Binh Bridge, Lac Long Bridge)
       receives investment, alongside a bus system with many operating routes such as: Cau Rao -
       Western Bus Station, VSIP Industrial Park - An Lao, VSIP Industrial Park - Do Son.
 ❖     Maritime Transport System: Dubbed the "Port City", Hai Phong is home to one of the oldest
       and largest seaports in the North, serving as a crucial international trade gateway. The ports
       in Hai Phong serve as national key traffic hubs.
 ❖     Railway Transport System: The Hanoi – Hai Phong Railway Line, built in 1901 and put into
       operation in 1902, has a length of approximately 102 km passing through 4 provinces/cities.
       It constitutes one side of the Northern key economic development triangle.
 ❖     Inland Waterway Transport System: Due to a dense river network (where downstream
       branches of the Thai Binh River flow into the sea), Hai Phong has strongly developed inland
       waterway transport, serving the transportation of goods and passengers in the region.
 ❖     Air Transport System: Cat Bi International Airport ensures vital air connectivity for the city
       and the region.
129. Geographical location characteristics become one of the favourable conditions for economic,
cultural and social development of Hai Phong city.

7.2.3. Socio-economic situation
131. On August 5, 2025, the Government issued Resolution No. 226/NQ-CP regarding growth
targets for sectors, fields, and localities, as well as key tasks and solutions to ensure that the national
growth in 2025 reaches 8.3-8.5%. Accordingly, the Government assigned the 2025 GRDP growth
target for Hai Phong City (post-arrangement) at 12.2%. Departments, branches, and localities shall
continue to closely adhere to the Economic Growth Scenario Plan (GRDP) and the Public Investment
Capital Disbursement Scenario for the last 6 months of 2025; proactively address task gaps; and
effectively organize the implementation of Resolution No. 205/NQ-CP dated July 6, 2025 (on the
regular Government meeting of June 2025) and the Government's Resolution No. 226/NQ-CP. The
City maintains its determination and strives to achieve a full-year growth target of 12.35%, which is

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                  Page | 65
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


higher than the 2025 growth target assigned by the Government9. It is expected that 07/09 key socio-
economic indicators for August will meet and exceed the growth scenario.
132. Regarding public investment disbursement in the first 8 months, the City disbursed VND
21,767.731 billion, reaching 60.6% of the capital plan assigned by the Prime Minister (VND 35,893.2
billion) and 55.4% of the capital plan assigned by the City (VND 39,298.252 billion). This result is
higher than the same period in 2024 (when the City disbursed VND 9,249.7 billion, equalling 38.6%
of the plan assigned by the Prime Minister (VND 23,850.893 billion) and 30.6% of the plan assigned
by the City (VND 30,263.8 billion)).
133. The total state budget revenue in the City for the first 8 months is estimated to reach VND
131,647.25 billion, achieving 89.3% of the estimate assigned by the Central Government (reaching
79.8% of the annual scenario), and equal to 128.9% compared to the same period last year. Of which:
Domestic revenue is estimated at VND 73,708.75 billion, achieving 98.7% of the estimate assigned
by the Central Government (reaching 88.8% of the annual scenario), equal to 135.8% compared to
the same period last year; import-export revenue is estimated at VND 56,387.72 billion, achieving
84.7% of the estimate assigned by the Central Government (reaching 75.1% of the annual scenario),
equal to 125.9% compared to the same period last year. Within domestic revenue, revenue from land
use fees in the first 8 months is estimated at VND 31,552.97 billion, achieving 119.7% of the estimate
assigned by the Central Government (exceeding the annual scenario target, reaching 104.6%), and
equal to 174.8% compared to the same period last year.
7.2.4. Labor and employment situation
134. In August 2025, it is estimated that 09 job transaction sessions were organized, attracting 148
enterprise participations with a recruitment demand of 25,760 positions; the labor supply at the
exchange reached 15,220 workers (meeting 59.08% of the recruitment demand). Unemployment
insurance registration is estimated at 2,520 people (a decrease of 9.09% compared to the same period
last year); unemployment insurance benefits have been settled for 2,915 people (a decrease of 5.7%),
with a cost of VND 110.5 billion (an increase of 37.3%). Through the processing of unemployment
benefits, job consultancy and introduction were provided to 2,520 people.
7.3.     Characteristics of Economic Conditions of the Project Area
7.3.1. Agricultural - forestry - fishery production
135. Cultivation: In August, the seasonal rice crop showed favorable growth. The planted area of
summer-autumn vegetables and crops is estimated to reach 15,000 ha, equivalent to the same period
last year; many vegetable areas are currently being harvested, with favorable product consumption
and stable selling prices. The area of longan trees reached approximately 2,490 ha, and custard apple
(Na) trees reached about 1,640 ha; harvesting is currently being concentrated.
136. Livestock: Livestock herds were maintained stably, and disease control was effective. The
total cattle herd is estimated at 20,964 heads, a decrease of 3.16% compared to the same period last
year; the buffalo herd is estimated at 9,547 heads, a decrease of 4.07%; the pig herd is estimated at
617,177 heads, an increase of 4.99%; the poultry flock is estimated at 26,170 thousand heads, an
increase of 2.9%. As of the reporting time, there have been no cases of sick or dead pigs, nor culling
due to African Swine Fever in the City.

137. Fisheries: The aquaculture area in the first 8 months is estimated at 23,920 ha. Aquaculture
output in August is estimated at 17,260 tons, an increase of 11.35% compared to the same period last
year; overall, the output for the first 8 months is estimated at 129,260 tons, an increase of 6.41%
(achieving 64.02% of the annual scenario).
138. Forestry: Continued to strengthen forest protection management, patrols, urging forest
owners, and forest fire prevention and fighting work. In August, no forest fires occurred; no cases
related to the construction of works or architectural structures on forestry land arose; and no forest
exploitation activities took place. Maintained the implementation of 05 afforestation projects."
7.3.2. Industry and civil works
139. Regarding industrial production: The Index of Industrial Production (IIP) in August is estimated
to increase by 15.42% over the same period last year, an increase of 0.08 percentage points compared
to July (not meeting the August scenario of 17.03%). Specifically: The processing and manufacturing
industry increased by 15.45%; The production and distribution of electricity, gas, hot water, steam, and
air conditioning increased by 16.08%; The water supply, waste and wastewater management and
treatment activities increased by 9.48%; The mining industry decreased by 25.08%.
140. Generally for the first 8 months of the year, the IIP increased by 14.51% over the same period
last year (The annual plan is an increase of 16.8%). Specifically: The processing and manufacturing
industry increased by 16.40%; The water supply, waste and wastewater management and treatment
activities increased by 6.89% year-on-year; The production and distribution of electricity, gas, hot
water, steam, and air conditioning decreased by 6.94%; The mining industry decreased by 16.89%.
Several key industries achieved fair growth compared to the same period last year, playing a leading
role in the overall growth of the sector, including: Manufacture of transport equipment increased by
45.14%; Manufacture of motor vehicles increased by 30.18%; Manufacture of fabricated metal
products increased by 24.57%; Manufacture of computers, electronic and optical products increased by
13.41%; Manufacture of electrical equipment increased by 27.07%.
141. Development of Industrial Zones and Clusters: Focused on urging investors to accelerate the
progress of site clearance and infrastructure construction investment for Industrial Zones (IZs) and
Industrial Clusters (ICs), basically ensuring the set scenario targets. Reviewed and compiled the list of
current ICs and planned ICs up to 2030; grasped the situation of enterprises currently operating in
production and business within the ICs.
142. Compiled a list of enterprises with large revenue and export turnover, which are decisive for
the IIP index; developed solutions to ensure growth. Agreed on the selection of the layout plan for the
gas pipeline and LNG terminal serving the Hai Phong LNG Gas Thermal Power Plant Project.
Developed the list of Key Energy-Using Facilities in 2024 in the City area after arrangement. The
power supply situation in the City in the first 8 months was basically stable, ensuring full, continuous,
and safe power supply for the City's socio-economic development activities. Total commercial
electricity output of the whole city in August is estimated to increase by 0.64% compared to the
previous month; generally, in the first 8 months, it is estimated to increase by 7.12% compared to the
same period in 2024.

7.4.   Socio-Economic Information of Affected Households
7.4.1. General information
148. A sociological survey was conducted with 463 affected households (corresponding to 1,660
persons) in the area of 08 wards.
149. Data related to affected households was collected from a socio-economic survey conducted
in the project area. The main objective of this section is to provide an overview of the socio-economic
conditions of the AHs, including demographic characteristics, income sources, living conditions,
infrastructure and sanitation, poverty status, etc. This information can be used as baseline data for
monitoring and evaluation during project implementation.
7.4.2. Household size
150. The socio-economic survey was conducted covering a total of 463 households. The survey
results regarding average household size show that: The Dong Hai area has the largest household size
with an average of 6.0 persons/household; however, it should be noted that the sample size here is
very small (only 3 households), resulting in low representativeness. Nam Trieu follows with an
average of 5.05 persons/household (a large sample of 98 households), indicating that this is an area
with a tradition of large or multi-generational families.

7.4.4. Age of surveyed household members (excluding household heads)
154. The total number of surveyed households is 463 (based on household head data). The total
number of recorded household members is 1,660 people. The average age of all household members
is 31.7 years; meanwhile, the average age of household heads is significantly high, reaching 62.0
years. The 30-year gap between the overall average age and the age of household heads indicates that
the multi-generational family model ('Three generations under one roof') remains very prevalent. The

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                         Page | 72
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


elderly hold the main decision-making role (household heads), while the younger generation lives
together to provide care or remains dependent.
155. Among all household members, females have a significantly higher average age than males
(Female: 35.3 years vs. Male: 27.4 years), suggesting that women's life expectancy is higher than
that of men in the project implementation area.

7.4.12. Household’s domestic water sources
164. Clean water is one of the criteria used to evaluate the development level and civilization of
urban residents. In the survey on water sources, the majority of surveyed households are using tap
water, with 455 households, accounting for 98.27%. There are 4 households (0.86%) stating they still
use drilled/dug well water, and 1 household (0.22%) still uses water from the irrigation system for
domestic purposes.

165. Relying on a single water source can pose high risks if that source is interrupted or encounters
an incident, leading to difficulties in daily activities. However, along with the increasing speed of
urbanization, the issue of water security, supply, and assurance of clean water is always a top priority;
therefore, the trend of using a single water source in urban areas is increasing.
166. Regarding production activities, most respondents stated that they use water from the clean
water supply system with 279 households (60.26%); 76 households (16.41%) use water from rivers

7.4.15. Average monthly income and expendicture of the PAHs
176. Income: The average income of the affected households is 5.36 million VND per person per
month, but there are differences between wards.
                            Table 29. The average monthly income of the PAHs
                                                                               Prescribing the multidimensional poverty
          Ward               Average monthly income PAHs (VND)
                                                                                standards for the 2021 - 2025 period10

 An Hai                     6,573,020                                                              2,000,000

177. The above data in the area shows a clear disparity, meaning that most households have income
at average, while a few households have high income.The median income reaches 4.25 million VND
per person, lower than the average of 5.36 million VND per person, indicating significant disparity
between households. The median being lower than the average shows that most households have
income below the average level. According to urban near-poor household standards, the median
indicates that most households exceed the urban poverty standard.
178. Income Sources: Many affected households have more than one income source. Households
with salary income account for a high proportion of 329/463 households. Next are income from
agricultural production activities and trading/services. Among households with agricultural income
sources, most have additional income sources. SES survey results show that among 243 households
with agricultural income, 225 households have income from other activities such as salaries,
trading/business/services, and other sources.

179. Expenditure: The majority of household expenditures focus on basic family living needs,
including living expenses (100% of households), education expenses (53.66% of households),
medical expenses (76.72% of households), and ceremonial expenses (83.59% of households).
Notably, households show considerable attention to social and community activities, evidenced by
83.59% of households reporting monthly expenditures for such purposes. Other specific expenditures
account for low proportions, such as house repair/construction (12.64% of households),
production/business costs (25.72% of households), and other expenses (0.67% of households).
180. The general household expenditure pattern in the project area is relatively uniform, with
households prioritizing spending on essential needs and the maintenance of social relationships.
However, average per capita expenditure varies significantly across wards:

181. Average expenditure levels range from VND 2.25 million (Đông Hai) to VND 4.07 million
(An Dương), with a differential of approximately 81% between the highest- and lowest-spending
wards. Wards such as An Dương and An Hai exhibit expenditure levels above the average
(approximately VND 3.22 million). In contrast, Đông Hải and Lưu Kiếm fall below this level. This
reflects the current state of economic development across wards in the project area. An Dương and
An Hải wards are located near the center of Hai Phong City, attracting foreign direct investment
(FDI) and logistics activities.

7.4.16. Household borrowing needs
182. Borrowing capital from credit institutions plays an important role in supporting households
to achieve production and business goals, especially in the fields of agriculture and aquaculture.
Access to credit provides households with financial resources to purchase materials, expand
production scale, invest in infrastructure, or apply new technologies to improve productivity. The
survey results show that only 9.29% of surveyed households have borrowed capital from credit
institutions. Among them, 30.23% of borrowers used the funds for investment in trading/services,
27.91% borrowed for construction and house repair, 18.6% invested in education, and notably, up to
27.91% of respondents stated that the purpose of the loan was for medical examination and treatment.
Regarding loan sources, households mainly borrowed from relatives, friends, and neighbors,
accounting for 46.51%; other channels such as the Vietnam Bank for Agriculture and Rural
Development (Agribank) and the Vietnam Bank for Social Policies (VBSP) accounted for 16.28%
and 11.63%, respectively; borrowing from other banks accounted for 25.58%, and borrowing from
moneylenders accounted for only 2.33%.

7.4.17. Changes in Households’ living standards in the last 3 years
183. Hoa Binh Commune is an area requiring special attention in the Resettlement Action Plan
(RAP) as it has the highest number and percentage of vulnerable households (16 households,
accounting for 15.84%). These are particularly concentrated in the group of elderly people living
alone (6 out of the 7 cases in the entire project are located here) and social policy households (8
households). Nam Trieu Commune ranks second in terms of the number of vulnerable households (9
households), mainly consisting of social policy households and female-headed households.
184. Attention should be paid to the case of the single near-poor household under the project,
located in Bach Dang Ward. Specific income restoration measures are needed for this household to
prevent the risk of falling back into poverty.
185. Regarding Ethnic Minorities: No ethnic minority households were recorded in any of the
surveyed areas.

7.4.19. Use of electricity and fuel
188.      Survey results show that all affected households now have access to the national grid.
189. Cooking fuels are diverse, with two main sources being electricity and gas. Only a very small
fraction (2 households) uses firewood or straw as cooking fuel. Specifically, 367 households use gas,
and 93 households use electricity for cooking activities.
7.4.20. Legal Status of Land
190. For households, land and housing are not only places of residence but also valuable assets;
therefore, the Land Use Rights Certificate serves as the legal basis to prove the legality of citizens'
land use. For affected households, the Land Use Rights Certificate is an important basis and legal
foundation for determining compensation value as well as support amounts for the households.

7.5.      Gender Issues
195. In order to understand the division of labor by gender, it has been conducted interview with
households by questions related to who will be mainly responsible for tasks such as shopping,
cooking, and taking care of children.… in the family. It will consider different duties and
responsibilities between men and women, who will do, what will they do, when will they do, how
and how long etc. and social recognition of labor. The division of tasks on the basis of gender is
known and understood by all members of each community/society.
196. Women in the family not only have to be responsible for production work but also carry the
burden of jobs that are considered as " odd jobs", making them always "busy". The progressing of a
community is measured by the progressing of women in that community. And the progressing of
women is reflected in whether they are "liberated", shared housework in the family and participated
in the common work of society? In general, women must fully perform the following tasks: (i)
Production work (production of goods and services for household consumption or income generation)
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                                   Page | 94
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


(ii) Reproduction work (giving birth, taking care of children, doing housework and maintaining
family life) (iii) Community work (providing and maintaining resources used by people such as
water, health care, education, leadership participation). Men tend to participate in community and
production work.
197. Regarding the division of labor in the region, there is no difference compared to other studies
and gender-based division of labor analyses in Vietnam: women participate in production,
reproduction, and childcare/family care activities, while men mainly participate in production tasks
and attend meetings at the commune and residential group levels.
