7.6.     Vulnerable Households
200. Out of the total 463 households affected by the project, 44 households belong to vulnerable
groups, comprising: 14 female-headed households with dependents; 07 elderly households (small
size of 1-2 people) living alone or without support; and 23 policy households with meritorious
services to the revolution.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                  Page | 96
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


VIII. LIVELIHOOD RESTORATION PROGRAM
8.1.    Purpose
201. The LRP is fundamental to achieving the objective of the World Bank’s ESS5. For those who
lose land-based income, these are more likely to face the risk of impoverishment, particularly those
who are poor and rely on agriculture for income generation, or rely on retailed business in areas with
access to a large number of patrons .
8.2.   Eligible Households/Persons to the LRP
202. Since the LRP aims to help PAPs improve, or at least restore, their livelihood/income, the
following households are eligible to participate in program:
  ❖     Households who lose 30% or more of their agricultural land;
  ❖     Poor/vulnerable households who lose 10% or more of the agricultural land;
  ❖     Household who must relocate;
203. Based on IOL result, there are 1,373 households that will be eligible to participate in the LRP,
including (i) 1,292 households losing 30% or more of which 128 vulnerable households losing 10%
or more of their agricultural production; (ii) 181 relocation households. These households are eligible
to take part in LRP.
204. The Livelihood Restoration Program will include appropriate livelihood restoration support
measures. These measures are consulted and developed based on the needs and socioeconomic
conditions of affected persons. As presented above, the occupations and income sources of
households affected by agricultural land acquisition are highly diverse, deriving from salaries,
revenues from production and business activities, and other sources. In Haiphong City, agriculture
currently constitutes a minor proportion of the economic structure. In 2024, within the former Thuy
Nguyen area, agriculture, forestry, and aquaculture accounted for approximately 5.5% of total
production value, while industry-construction represented 60% and services 34%. Currently,
agriculture is no longer the mainstay sector contributing to local GRDP. The project implementation
area is undergoing urbanization. Labor demand in the project area is currently very high, driven by
the development of industrial clusters and major enterprises in the locality, such as VSIP and Nam
Cau Kien. In 2025, labor recruitment demand at enterprises in Haiphong increased by approximately
30% compared to the same period in 2024. According to information from the Haiphong
Employment Service Center in February 2025, 38 enterprises in the area had recruitment needs for
3,552 workers, predominantly unskilled labor, production/technical workers in manufacturing,
construction, textiles, transportation, and related fields. Additionally, over 60 enterprises in industrial
zones required approximately 4,500 workers.
205. The aforementioned indicators demonstrate that the economic structure in the project area is
shifting toward industry-construction-services as the dominant sectors. Therefore, to further identify
beneficiaries for the Livelihood Restoration Program, affected persons in eligible households are
determined to participate in the program.
206. By convention, occupations potentially impacted by land acquisition among household
members are identified as those related to agricultural, forestry, and fishery production activities.
Based on demographic information from 1,708 surveyed households, the number of individuals
potentially affected by land acquisition activities is projected as follows:



Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                  Page | 97
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


                                               Number of
                                                affected           Aged 21–40          Aged 41–60       Aged 41–60
                                                persons

 Households losing 30% or more of
 agricultural land                                        789              200                 300                  251

 Vulnerable households losing 10% or
 more of agricultural land                                 92               30                  37                   23

 Households to be relocated                                78               14                  39                   33

 Total                                                    959              244                 376                  307

207. The data indicate that a portion of households losing agricultural land do not engage in
agricultural production activities. Livelihood restoration programs will prioritize individuals of
working age who are involved in agricultural production and express interest in participating in the
program.
208. The livelihood restoration measures for affected households will be developed based on the
consultation with the affected households and implemented through coordination by the PMU,
PMU’s consultant, local authorities and relevant agencies such as the Department of Labor, War
Invalids and Social Affairs, Vocational Training Centers, local Policies Bank
8.3.       Assessment of Households’ Demands
209. According to the results of the initial needs assessment involving 463 households
participating in the livelihood restoration programme, the majority of households have not identified
specific programme options; 180 households have no demand to participate in the livelihood
restoration programme, some households wish to access concessional interest rate loan capital, some
households wish to convert land use purposes to seek employment opportunities at their new places
of residence, and a small proportion wishes to receive support for vocational training costs and
production guidance training. Some households have expressed wishes for support unrelated to direct
livelihood restoration but focused on social welfare measures, such as issuance of health insurance
cards and assistance with children's schooling expenses. Specific information is as follows.
            Table 44. Demands for participating in the Livelihood Restoration Programs
   No                              Demands                              Number (of people)           Percentage (%)

       1    Access to concessional interest rate loan capital                    132                      28,5

       2    Vocational training and production guidance training                 40                       8,6

       3    Conversion of land use purpose                                       70                       15,1

       4    Not yet decided/no demand for vocational training                    180                      38,9

       6    Other                                                                41                       8,9

                                Total                                            463                     100%

8.4.       Proposed Activities in the Livelihood Restoration Program
210. Based on the local socioeconomic development context, the labor characteristics of affected
households, and survey findings on demand for participation in income restoration initiatives, the
specific livelihood restoration programs proposed include the following:

8.4.1. Technical training courses in animal husbandry and crop cultivation techniques
211. Through consultations with the commune authorities, local communes/wards are in the
process of organizing courses on agricultural extension programs which is provided by local
Agricultural Extension Center, in conjunction with local agricultural cooperatives and the Divisions
of Labor, Invalids and Social Affairs of the districts. Given this on-going program, agricultural
households who are severely affected but will continue their crop production will be invited to join
the existing agricultural extension program that are appropriate to them. Existing training courses
include: (i) Care and disease prevention for cattle and poultry; (ii) application of new technology for
fruit trees and industrial trees.
212. Based on the needs and wishes of affected households for technical training support, the
Project Management Unit will coordinate with local ward authorities within the project area to
support affected households in participating in existing local technical training courses. The project
will send a list of people affected by the project who are looking for the technical training courses,
along with their resumes during project implementation
8.4.2. Vocational training courses
213. Affected households whose family member within labor age wish to participate in a suitable
vocational training to learn new job other than the existing one can apply for (i) short-term vocational
courses (elementary level or vocational training time less than 3 months) under the GoV’s Project on
Vocational Training for Rural Workers; (ii) Vocational training at intermediate and college levels.
8.4.3. Support for Vulnerable Groups
214. These are special groups that might suffer disproportionately impacts or might suffer risks of
impoverishment due to impacts of resettlement. The group includes : (i) single female headed
households with dependents and economic disadvantage (single, widow, disabled husband); (ii)
people with physical or mental disability (loss of working ability); (iii) the poor under MOLISA
poverty standard; (iv) the elderly alone; (v) social policy families. They may be people who can
hardly be competitive on the labor market when their livelihoods depend on the land area
acquired/affected by the project. Therefore, the special support programs for these groups should be
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 99
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


carried out. These programs may coincide with the general assistance programs to all households
affected by the project but there are certain priorities for vulnerable households.
8.4.4. Credit Loan Support
215. In the recent years, the Vietnam Bank for Social Policy (VBSP) – Hai Phong branch regularly
coordinated with other agencies, political and social organizations implementation of credit programs
to provide preferential loans to poor households and other policy objects. So, many households have
escaped from poverty. Currently, Hai Phong social policy bank has been implementing 05 credit
programs including: loan for poor households, employment solutions, labor export, pupil-student,
clean water- rural sanitation. The LRP will guide and support PAPs to borrow loan from the VBSP
and other banks if they have demand.
8.4.5. Employment Creation
216. As stated previously, PAHs have a need for employment support during construction phase.
The project will collaborate with project contractors to assist those in need of employment. After
that, they can apply for jobs directly with the contractor or through the PMU.
217. During the project implementation phase, affected people will be interviewed about their need
for LRP activities. To receive support, affected people need to provide proof that they are affected
households of the project, including (i) certificate of residence; (ii) compensation documents, or
certified copies of relevant communes.
8.4.6. Estimation cost for LRP
218. The cost for implementing the Livelihood Restoration Program will be elaborated in detail
during the implementation of the Livelidhood Restoration Program later. During project
implementation if the AHs would change their mind for LRP implementation and need budget from
project. Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and Sustainable Development Projects
(HPRSDP PMU) will arrange sufficient budget for LRP implementation as the requirements of
project.
8.4.7. Implementation of livelihood restoration program
219. The livelihood restoration program will be implemented on severely affected people and
vulnerable groups immediately after compensation payment. Households will be thoroughly
surveyed for income restoration activities and the PMU, with the support of consultants, will
coordinate with relevant stakeholders to implement livelihood restoration program for households,
with the following specific steps:

8.4.8. Monitoring and provision of additional supports
220. During the LRP implementation, Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and
Sustainable Development Projects (HPRSDP PMU )and project consultant will regularly engage with
these affected households to monitor their ability in order to recover their livelihoods and income. If
necessary, PMU will provide additional supporting measures for AHs to ensure that the income and
livelihoods of the affected households at least as before project according to requirements of ESS5.

IX.    RESETTLEMENT ARRANGEMENT
9.1.   The Resettlement Activities of the Project
221. According to the Inventory of Losses (IOL) survey conducted between September and
December 2025, a total of 350 households will be impacted by the loss of their houses and residential
land. Of these, 181 households will lose both their houses and residential land entirely and do not
have no other shelter to live within their wards. These households are therefore eligible for
resettlement arrangements. Additionally, 99/181 households currently living with the relocating
families meet the criteria for household separation and will be allocated at least one minimum-sized
resettlement plot. In total, 280 households will be entitled to relocate to the two designated
resettlement areas. The remaining 169 households, whose entire houses will also be affected, will be
permitted to rebuild on their remaining land parcels, as these parcels meet the city’s residential land
threshold of 60 m².
222.    The project implementation area, although undergoing rapid urbanization, still retains the
characteristics of traditional multi-generational Vietnamese families. The number of couples living
on the same land plot is high. The IOL results indicate that the demographic size of the affected
households is 4.75 persons/household. Based on the population of relocating households, the project
requires allocation of approximately 100 additional resettlement plots to accommodate couples living
together on the same land plot who will separate households following land acquisition.


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                     Page | 101
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


223. Consultation activities regarding resettlement options for displaced households were
conducted in October 2025. During community consultation meetings, affected persons were
provided with information about the locations of resettlement sites and the applicable resettlement
support policies for the project. Detailed resettlement options and specific financial support levels
were communicated to affected persons through both consultation sessions and in-depth interviews
combined with survey questionnaires.
224. The consultation results on resettlement arrangements indicate that residents are concerned
about: (i) whether the location of the upcoming resettlement sites will be convenient for access to
public infrastructure, (ii) the resettlement allocation policy for households with multiple married
couples living on a single land plot, and (iii) the plot sizes of each resettlement lot. Many households
wish to be allocated more than one resettlement plot for married couples who are currently living
together in the same household.
225. The SES survey results show that, when queried on preferences for project-arranged
resettlement, 127 respondents (26.4%) expressed interest in the designated resettlement areas, 184
respondents (38.2%) remained undecided, and 170 respondents (35.4%) preferred self-arranged
resettlement options. The assessment of resettlement preferences among affected households will
continue during the land acquisition preparation phase.
226. The project does not develop dedicated resettlement areas exclusively for project displacees.
Within Hai Phong City, in the two affected wards of Nam Trieu and Bach Dang, the city is preparing
to construct two resettlement areas to accommodate displaced households from various land
acquisition projects across the city. Affected residents of the Hai Phong City Development Project
Adapting to Climate Change have been provided information about the location, area, and
resettlement capacity of these two city resettlement areas as potential relocation options. Should
residents choose to move to the city resettlement areas, they may select from the following two
options:
                          Table 46. Information about resettlement areas
                                                       Expected      Area of each
No           Resettlement area              Area                                        Development Situation
                                                      lot number   resettlement plot.

 1   Nam Triệu Ward Resettlement Area      13.54 ha      451       54,4m2 – 134,4m2      Approved planning;

 2   Bach Dang Ward Resettlement Area      19.98 ha      958       60,6m2 – 210,1 m2      Under construction
                                                                                             preparation

                Total                      33.52 ha     1,409

227. Two resettlement areas will feature plots of varying sizes starting from 54,4 m² upwards to
meet the diverse needs of affected persons. In addition to providing complete basic infrastructure to
enable residents to stabilize their livelihoods, these two resettlement areas will also include dedicated
spaces for residents to perform clan ancestral rituals, as recorded in community consultation
feedback.
228. Based on the results of community consultations, the results of the socio-economic survey of
severely affected households, the actual situation of the locality, and in accordance with the
regulations of the Hai Phong City People’s Committee on cases where multi-generation families or
multiple married couples living on a single land plot subject to land recovery are eligible to separate
into individual households and may be considered for allocation of one to two additional residential
land plots with land use levy collection within the resettlement area, the project needs to arrange
approximately 280 resettlement plots for households affected by the project.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                     Page | 102
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


229. A resettlement allocation plan is developed to ensure that households affected by land
recovery for residential purposes are provided with new housing in a timely, equitable, transparent
manner, and in alignment with the legitimate aspirations of the affected population. The resettlement
allocation adheres to the following principles: public disclosure of information, community
participation, public lottery drawing, prioritization of vulnerable households, and safeguarding the
legitimate rights of land users. This plan encompasses the following activities:
230. Public Disclosure of Resettlement Area Information: Local authorities and the Project
Management Board organize the public disclosure of resettlement area information at the People's
Committee offices at the commune level, village/hamlet cultural houses, and local mass media
outlets. The disclosed content includes: location and scale of the resettlement area; number of plots,
area, and specifications of each plot; allocation criteria and priority order; procedures for lottery
drawing – plot selection – land allocation – issuance of Land Use Rights Certificates; and timelines
and venues for implementation.
231. Organization of Lottery Drawing and Plot Selection: Based on the approved list of eligible
resettlement households, the Compensation, Support, and Resettlement Council prepares the lottery
list and notifies each household of the time and place for participating in the lottery drawing. The
lottery drawing is conducted publicly, with minutes recorded, in the presence of household
representatives, local authority representatives, the Fatherland Front, and mass organizations,
ensuring principles of fairness, objectivity, and prevention of complaints.
232. Following the lottery drawing, each household is informed of the anticipated plot number and
has the right to verify the corresponding planning diagram, area, and plot location. For households
under policy provisions, vulnerable households, or those facing special difficulties, the arrangement
of lottery order and/or allocation of more advantageous plot locations is implemented in accordance
with pre-announced priority criteria.
233. Land Allocation, Plot Receipt, and On-Site Handover: On the basis of lottery results, the
competent authority issues land allocation decisions for resettlement to each household, specifying
the location, area, land type, usage purpose, and financial obligations (if any). The Project
Management Board, in coordination with the commune-level People's Committee, organizes on-site
handover sessions, providing detailed guidance on boundaries, usage scope, and associated technical
infrastructure systems (roads, electricity, water, drainage) for each plot.
234. Households sign on-site plot receipt minutes, confirming boundaries, area, and plot condition
at the time of handover. These minutes serve as the basis for completing dossiers for Land Use Rights
Certificate issuance and for resolving disputes (if any) thereafter.
235. Resettlement plot handover and land use rights certificate issuance: Upon households
fulfilling financial obligations as stipulated (if any) and ensuring complete legal dossiers, the natural
resources and environment agency submits for competent authority approval to issue Land Use
Rights Certificates for the resettlement area. Certificate handover is conducted centrally or directly
at the commune-level People's Committee, with signatures, dossier archiving, and clear notification
of land users' rights and obligations.
236. Concurrently, the Project Management Board and local authorities continue coordinating
support for households during new housing construction, linking to livelihood restoration programs,
social welfare, and essential services (education, healthcare, employment) to ensure resettlement
households achieve housing stability and progressively restore and improve their livelihoods
compared to pre-land recovery conditions.

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 103
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


9.2.   Resettlement Arrangements
237. Nam Trieu Ward is one of the localities implementing the project, specifically the site for the
Nam Trieu Resettlement Area (approximately 15.2 hectares). Nam Trieu Ward (established on the
basis of the merger of Tam Hung, Nam Trieu Giang and Lap Le communes) has an area of 29.51 km²
with a population of approximately 40,224 people.
238. Bach Dang Ward was established through the merger of the entire area and population of
Minh Duc Ward, Bach Dang Commune, Pham Ngu Lao Ward (former Thuy Nguyen City) and the
former Do Son District, under Hai Phong City. The ward has an area of 53.5 km² with a population
of 51,633 people.

X.      GRIEVANCE REDRESS MECHANISM                                                (GRM)         ON        LAND
        ACQUISITION AND RESETTLEMENT
10.1.   Objectives of the GRM
244. The purpose of a Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM) is to set forth procedures, methods,
and process that assist the resolution of a grievance that may arise during the Project implementation.
It offers process that is transparent, credible, and predictable to all parties that could result in
outcomes considered fair, effective, and lasting. More specifically, the GRM aims to:

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                           Page | 108
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


  ❖     Provide affected people with avenues for making a complaint or resolving any disputes that
        may arise during Project implementation.
  ❖     Ensure that appropriate and mutually acceptable redress actions are identified and
        implemented to the satisfaction of complainants; and
  ❖     Avoid the need to resort to judicial proceedings.
10.2. Grievance Redress Mechanism
245. Grievance redress mechanism of the Project will be established and implemented in
compliance with the Law on Complaints (Law No.02/2011/QH13, dated 11 November 2011), and
the Law on Denunciation (Law No.25/2018/QH14, dated 12 June 2018). The grievances will be
redressed in two steps before escalating to court.
246. Affected people have the right to file complaints concerning their project-related benefits and
responsibilities, including but not limited to land acquisition, resettlement, compensation policies,
benefits, compensation rates, and other livelihood restoration program benefits.
247. As a result, a GRM was created to address concerns about the project's land acquisition and
resettlement. This mechanism establishes procedures, methods, and processes for resolving any
complaints that may arise during project implementation. Furthermore, the mechanism provides
stakeholders with a transparent, credible, and accessible procedure that leads to fair, effective, and
long-term grievance redress. Furthermore, the availability of legal remedies, as well as traditional
and community grievance resolution methods, should be considered.
248. The GRM will be applicable and accessible to parties affected by the project, as well as parties
that are positively or negatively involved and/or may influence the project outcome.
249.   The project’s GRM includes the following steps:


                    • People send written claims to the one-stop office of the Ward People's
                      Committee
 Ward People's      • The period of time for resolving claims is 30 days
Committee Level




                    • People send written claims to the City People's Committee
                    • The period of time for resolving claims is 45 days
   City People's
    Committee




                    • People send written claims to the People's Court at the competent level for
                      sentence
                    • The Court's decision will be final
       Court




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                            Page | 109
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


 •     Step 1 – Ward People's Committee: If a household or individual has a complaint, it may
       submit a written complaint or verbally inform the WPC's one-stop office. The officer in
       charge of this office is responsible for notifying the commune leaders of a resolution. The
       WPC's will meet personally with the complainant. The time limit for settling complaints shall
       be 30 days from the time the complaints are received. The WPC's secretariat is responsible
       for documenting and filing all complaints within its jurisdiction.
 •     Step 2 – City People's Committee: If after 30 days, the aggrieved affected household does
       not hear from the PC of commune or if the affected household is not satisfied with the decision
       taken on his or her complaint, the affected household may bring the case, either in writing or
       in person, to the CPC. The CPC has 45 days to resolve the complaint. The CPC secretariat is
       responsible for maintaining records of complaints, actions, and outcomes. Complainants can
       also submit their complaints to the Court if they wish.
 •     Step 3 (final) - Administrative Court: If, after 45 days following the lodging of the
       complaint with the CPC, the aggrieved household does not hear from the CPC or if he or she
       is not satisfied with the decision taken on his or her complaint, the case may be brought to the
       Court for adjudication. The court's decision will be final.
250. The decision to resolve the complaint must be sent to the complainant and relevant parties
and posted at the committee’s office where the complaint is resolved.
251. Commune-level community organizations will incorporate existing GRMs, which are
currently chaired by commune People's Committee leaders. GRM will resolve complaints using
available local resources, addressing not only safety-related conflicts but also other issues during the
implementation process. Based on this structure, community organizations will assist in the project's
preparation, design, implementation, and future development. The GRM will be applicable to
individuals or groups directly or indirectly affected by the project, as well as those who may have an
interest in the project and/or have the potential to be positively or negatively affected by the results
of the project.
252. To minimize complaints to the province, the PMU will coordinate with the Resettlement
Committee of the communes to resolve issues. The PMU will designate an officer who will keep a
database of project-related complaints, detailing the complaint's nature, source, and date, the
complainant's name and address, the necessary actions, and the current status. In the case of a verbal
complaint, the Reception Committee will record the complaint on the Complaint Form during the
first meeting with the complainant.
253. The project's complaint resolution process, including contact information for the unit and
individual in charge of complaints, will be included in the project information leaflet and posted at
the People's Committee offices of project communes and PMU. All complaints will be recorded and
kept at the Commune People's Committee and resolved in a transparent and proactive manner by the
PMU. Documents and complaint reports will be made public. All costs related to the complaint
resolution process are paid by the project.
254. To avoid delays of the project implementation while ensuring compensation payments to
impacted people after their complaints have been resolved, the project will open an escrow account
for compensation and support payments at commercial banks with interest.




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 110
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


XI.         STAKEHOLDER                    ENGAGEMENT                  AND           INFORMATION
            DISCLOSURE
11.1.       Objectives
255. Information dissemination to PAPs and related agencies is an important part of project
preparation and implementation. Consultation with PAPs and ensuring their active participation will
minimize the possibility of conflicts and minimize the risk of delay of the project. This will also
allow the Project to design the resettlement and livelihood restoration program as a comprehensive
development program to be suitable with the needs and priorities of the affected people, thereby
maximizing the economic and social benefits of investments. The objectives of information
dissemination and consultation are as follows:
 (a) Ensure that local communities as well as representatives of affected households are included
            in the planning and decision-making process. The PMU will closely coordinate with the City
            People's Committee, and Ward People’s Committee of the project and related departments
            and agencies during the project implementation. The PAP's participation in the project
            implementation will continue throughout the project cycle; for example, the PAP's
            representative to be a member of the Compensation and Resettlement Committee, and
            participate in resettlement activities (asset assessment, compensation, resettlement and
            monitoring).
 (b) Share full information about the components and activities of the proposed project with the
            PAPs.
 (c) Obtain information on the needs and priorities of the PAPs, as well as receive their feedback
            on the project's policies and activities.
 (d) Ensure that project-affected people can provide full information on the impacts on their
            income and living standards, and they will have the opportunity to participate in activities and
            make decisions on issues that will directly affect them.
      (e) Obtain cooperation and participation of PAPs and communities in necessary activities for
              Resettlement Planning and Implementation.
      (f)     Ensure transparency in all project activities including land acquisition, resettlement and
              restoration.
11.2.       Stakeholder Engagement and Consultation
11.2.1. Consultation during the project preparation
❖       Implementation method:
256. Methods of information dissemination and public consultation include: rapid assessment with
participation in the rural and stakeholder consultation, Survey of affected areas, interviews with
affected households, community meetings, focus group discussions, and socio-economic interviews
and surveys.
❖       Information dissemination and consultation contents
257. In the early stages of project preparation, local authorities at all levels were informed about
the project, its objectives, components and activities, and were consulted and engaged in discussions
about local development needs and priorities. Local authorities were consulted on the potential
negative impacts of the project, measures to minimize the impacts and the benefits of the project.
Local authorities were also consulted on their consensus and commitment to implement the
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                  Page | 111
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


resettlement policy as described in the RP. After the project is approved, the provincial and local
mass media will widely introduce the project in public places, including the objectives, components
and activities of the project.
  •      Community meetings: 14 meetings11 were conducted at the offices of the People's
         Committees of the ward/neighborhood group affected by the project, with 1.831 participants,
         of which 40.5% were women. Participants included representatives from the Client,
         consultancy units, Ward People's Committee leaders, cadastral officers, Officer of the
         Division of Economy, Infrastructure and Urban Development, local organizations, village
         heads/deputy head, households directly affected by the project, beneficiary households, and
         concerned parties
  •      In-depth interviews: 15 in-depth interviews have been conducted with representatives of
         some affected households and severely affected households.

11.2.2. Consultation on the draft version of RP
259. The draft final RP will be officially consulted with the local authorities such as Department
of Agriculture and Environment, Department of Finance and other stakeholders and the official
response from local authorities will be provided in the appendix of the RP.
11.2.3. Consultation during the project implementation phase
260. After the project is approved, the Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and
Sustainable Development Projects (HPRSDP PMU) will coordinate with local authorities to
publicize project information, including project objectives, locations, components, and conduct
consultations with the affected parties during the project implementation. Furthermore, the PMU,
with the Consultant’s assistance, will carry out the following tasks:
 •     Provide information to relevant agencies at all levels during consultation meetings, including
       detailed information project land acquisition policies and procedures.
 •     Organize consultation and publicize information for parties affected by the project.
 •     Coordinate with the project's Compensation and Resettlement Committee to conduct DMS,
       update the compensation rates in the updated Resettlement Plan, and reconfirm the scale of
       land acquisition and impact on assets based on the consultation with affected people, and
       develop and complete compensation plans for each affected household.
 •     Complete the compensation plan including the types of affected assets and rights and have
       this plan signed by the affected households to confirm that they agree with the results of the
       damage assessment and record all questions of the affected people about compensation plan.
 •     Distribute the questionnaire to affected households eligible for relocation (a) to inform them
       of resettlement options (clearly explaining the consequences of choosing each option) and (b)
       to require affected households to confirm the resettlement option they have chosen and
       preliminary confirmation of the resettlement location, and (c) to propose affected households
       to clarify the services they are using such as education/ health care/market and the distance
       from their homes to these places serve as the basis for the development of infrastructure in
       the Resettlement Site.
 •     Consult affected households about their wishes for the livelihood restoration program. This
       consultation will be implemented for severely affected and vulnerable households of the
       project. The resettlement board will inform affected people about the plan and their right to
       receive technical assistance before asking them to clarify their desire to receive assistance to
       restore their income.
11.2.4. Information disclosure
261. The Vietnamese version of this resettlement plan will be available for public viewing at the
Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and Sustainable Development Projects (HPRSDP
PMU) offices, the People's Committees of communes, and the electronic information portal of Hai
Phong city. The English version will be uploaded on the World Bank website before and after this
plan is approved.
262. In addition, project information booklets (PIBs) will be prepared and distributed to affected
parties during the project preparation and implementation phases to ensure that affected people are
clearly aware of the project and its benefits. The PIBs will include information about the
compensation and support policies mentioned in the resettlement plan.


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 115
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


XII. IMPLEMENTATION ARRANGEMENT
12.1.   Institutional Framework
263. The implementation of the project's resettlement activities requires the participation of
agencies and organizations at the central, provincial and commune levels. Hai Phong Provincial
People's Committee will be responsible for the overall implementation of the Resettlement Plan. The
Compensation, Support, and Resettlement Board will be established at the provincial or commune
level according to the provisions of Decree No. 151/2025/CP. The Resettlement Plan's regulations
and policies will serve as the legal foundation for the project's compensation and resettlement
activities. Agencies managing land acquisition and resettlement include: (i) Haiphong City People's
Committee; ( (ii) Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and Sustainable Development
Projects (HPRSDP PMU); (iii) Regional Project Management Unit (Formerly the unit implementing
site clearance for district-level projects); (iv) Commune People's Committee; (v) Representatives of
the affected community and parties; and (vi) Independent Environmental and Social Monitoring
Consultant (IMC).
264. Main responsibilities of each unit participating in implementing the project's resettlement
plan:
12.2.   Responsibilities of Relevant Authorities
12.2.1. Provincial People's Committee
265. The Hai Phong City People's Committee is the highest authority to issue regulations, resolve
issues on plan and policies, direct the implementation of the Project and act as the focal point for
linking functional organizations in the project implementation.
266.    CPC shall have the following general responsibilities:
 (i)    Approve the Resettlement Plan;
 (ii)   Promulgate regulations to strengthen compensation, assistance and resettlement mechanisms
        in line with law and practice.
 (iii) Issuing the land price list, decisions to adjust, amend and supplement the land price list;;
 (iv)    Approving the conversion of the purpose of using rice-growing land, special-use forest
        land, protective forest land, production forest land to other purposes according to
        regulations;
 (v)    Direct the coordination between relevant agencies and departments, agencies and units at
        province level to carry out compensation, support and resettlement in accordance with the
        approved RP;
 (vi) Decision on land allocation, land lease, permission to change land use purpose for cases
      stipulated in the 2024 Land Law;
 (vii) Provide adequate and timely budget for resettlement activities of the project;
 (viii) Ensure that the objectives of the RP are achieved upon completion of resettlement
        implementation.
 (ix) Resolve complaints/grievances related to the project at the province level.
12.2.2. Project Management Unit (PMU)
267. The Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Regional and Sustainable Development Projects
(HPRSDP PMU); is the agency responsible for supporting the provincial People's Committee and

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 116
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


directly managing the implementation of the project. The PMU is responsible for implementing the
RP of the project, and its main tasks are
 (i)    Develop or update the resettlement action plan for submission to the City People's Committee
        for approval;
 (ii)   Identify resettlement sites before organizing the relocation of households to the new
        residential areas (if any);
 (iii) Develop a detailed implementation plan for site clearance and resettlement plan; sign
       contracts with relevant units to carry out compensation, assistance, and resettlement
       activities;
 (iv) Participate in the Compensation and Site Clearance Committees (CSCC) of the project,
      providing all necessary information related to the project and compensation and assistance
      plans to support the evaluation process by the CSCC;
 (v)    Provide guidance on the implementation of project policies to ensure compliance with the
        project's RP;
 (vi) Develop and implement internal monitoring plans for the resettlement activities of the project
      to ensure that all activities comply with the project's policies
 (vii) Recruit, supervise, and regularly review the recommendations made by the Independent
       Monitoring Agency (IMA) regarding the implementation of the RP;
 (viii) Receive land from the affected persons (PAP) and hand it over to the construction contractor;
 (ix) Prepare quarterly internal reports on resettlement activities to WB.
12.2.3. Ward People Committee
268.    The main task of WPCs are:
 (i)    To instruct, organize propaganda and mobilize all relevant agencies, households and
        individuals to implement the policy on compensation, support and resettlement and site
        clearance in accordance with the decision of the State’s competent agency.
 (ii)   To instruct the CCARB on the implementation of compensation, support and resettlement for
        the project and approve the compensation and resettlement plan on the basis of
        decentralization of the City People's Committee;
 (iii) To approve the replacement cost if authorized by the Provincial People's Committee;
 (iv) To direct relevant departments, agencies, organizations, and CCARB to carry out resettlement
      in compliance with the approved RP;
 (v)    To handle disputes, complaints, grievance and recommendation of people on compensation,
        support and resettlement in accordance with their competence;
 (vi) To decide on land acquisition for site clearance and land acquisition within its competence.
 (vii) To issue LURCs for land lots in resettlement sites.
12.2.4. Ward Compensation, Assistance and Resettlement Board (WCARB)
269. The WCARB an agency directly under the Ward People's Committee, is responsible for the
preparation and implementation of all resettlement activities. In this project, Responsibilities of
WCARB are:
 (i)    To coordinate with the PMU in compensation, support and resettlement;
 (ii)   To provide the PMU with a detailed plan outlining how the RP will be implemented in the
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                           Page | 117
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


        project;
 (iii) To work closely with the PMU in implementing activities to support land acquisition as
       required by the project;
 (iv) To fully comply with the requirements, principles and terms specified in the RP approved by
      the City People's Committee and follow the standardization steps for land acquisition in
      accordance with the law;
 (v)    To conduct Detailed Measurement Survey (DMS) of all affected properties, establish and
        publish detailed compensation measures of each PAH;
 (vi) To mobilize an independent valuation company to conduct replacement cost surveys for
      affected land, crops and structures and use them as a basis for designing compensation and
      support packages;
 (vii) To prepare the compensation plan and consult the affected people and submit it to the
       Commune People's Committee for approval of the compensation plan;
 (viii) To coordinate with the PMU to pay compensation for each affected household;
 (ix) To receive complaints and support competent agencies to settle;
 (x)    To coordinate with the PMU and relevant agencies to implement the Livelihood Restoration
        Program (LRP);
 (xi) Support the PMU to conduct detailed measurement survey (DMS) for the Project, and prepare
      land acquisition dossiers;
 (xii) To verify the entittlement of PAPs by the project or certify their land use to determine the
       eligibility and criteria for compensation;
 (xiii) To support the PMU and other units and agencies in publishing or disseminating information;
        organizing community meetings and consultations with AHs;
 (xiv) To support the affected people in improving their livelihoods and living standards;
 (xv) To ensure full implementation of the mechanism to handle complaints from AHs; record all
      complaints and make dossier of complaints at commune and commune level;
 (xvi) To work closely with independent monitoring agencies.
12.2.5. Project Affected households (PAHs)
270.    The PAHs have the following responsibilities:
 (i)    To coordinate with research groups to examine and confirm the affected properties and land
        and their entitlements;
 (ii)   To participate in all meetings and public consultations during project preparation and
        implementation and provide feedback to improve RP quality and solutions for effective RP
        implementation; and
 (iii) To hand over the acquired land to the project after receiving full benefits.
12.2.6. Independent monitoring consultant (IMC)
271. Independent Monitoring Consultant (IMC): An agency/organization or research institute
specialized in social sciences should be identified and hired to conduct socio-economic baseline
surveys, periodical monitoring and evaluation of RP implementation. PMU will recruit and contract
with the Independent Monitoring Agency (IMC). The IMC will periodically report on progress and
compliance issues to the donor and provide recommendation for non-compliance issues.

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                             Page | 118
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

XIV. MONITORING AND EVALUATION
14.1.   Objectives of Monitoring
274. To ensure full and timely performance of activities and commitments described in approved
RP, the Contractors shall carry out regular monitoring and assessment of RP implementation.
Monitoring of RP implementation is to collect information about RP implementation while
assessment of RP implementation will analyze collected information to weigh the performance,
compliance with schedule and agreed methods and evaluate conformity with the WB’s ESS5. In case
of differences between RP and actual implementation, mitigation measures will be proposed timely
by the PMU. Monitoring includes 2 following purposes:
  ❖     Verify whether the Project activities are completed efficiently or not, including quantity,
        quality and time.
  ❖     Assess whether these activities reach the objectives and purpose of the Project or not, and if
        not, how much do they reach.
14.2.   Internal Monitoring
275. Internal monitoring of the RP implementation is the main responsibility of the PMU with the
support of the Project consultants, which will be regularly implemented through progress reports
made by the PMU in coordination with Project WPCs. Key assignments of internal monitoring are
as below:
  ❖     Coordinate with related agencies in process of RP implementation;
  ❖     Collect necessary data, to set up a database of resettlement for the RP implementation
        progress reports for internal monitoring purpose;
  ❖     Identify any pending issues/non-compliance issues during RP implementation;
  ❖     Work closely with the Independent Monitoring Consultant to oversee the implementation of
        RP;
  ❖     Receive and report complaint of the affected people to competent authorities for resolving.
276. The PMU will submit internal monitoring reports on RP implementation to the World Bank
individually or jointly in the project's quarterly progress reports or as stand-alone reports. The
following main contents should be included in the internal monitoring report:
  ❖     Number of PAHs according to different impact types, condition of the compensation
        reimbursement, relocation and income recovery of the PAHs;
  ❖     Finance allocation to the activities andreimbursement of compensation and the reimbursed
        budget for each activity;
  ❖     Final result on complaints redress and any remaining issue which require the administrative
        authorities of some levels to solve;
  ❖     Pending, complianceissues during the implementation stage;
  ❖     Implementation schedule of the updated actual resettlement.
14.3.   External Monitoring (independent monitoring)
277. The PMU will mobilize the IMC to monitor the implementation of the RP. This consulting
unit must have environmental and social expertise, as well as extensive experience in independently
monitoring RP implementation. The consultant's monitoring tasks are carried out according to the

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                             Page | 124
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


Terms of Reference approved by the World Bank. The consultant will begin work as soon as the
project begins or, at the latest, after the compensation payment has been completed.
278. Independent monitoring aims to provide periodic independent assessments of the
implementation of resettlement objectives, including changes in living standards and employment,
income recovery, the social base of affected people, the effectiveness, impact, and sustainability of
benefits, the need to implement additional measures to mitigate impacts (if any), and the
identification of strategic lessons for policymaking in the future.
279. Every six months, IMC will conduct monitoring tasks in addition to evaluating information
from internal monitoring reports. IMC will conduct monitoring for all severely affected and
vulnerable households, as well as at least 30% of the remaining affected households. The IMC will
monitor and evaluate the following, including but not limited to:
  ❖     Monitoring the implementation of resettlement sites which include the status in compare with
        the plan, progress and impact on resettled PAPs;
  ❖     Payment of compensation will be as follows: a) full payment to be made to all affected
        persons sufficiently before land acquisition; (b) adequacy of payment to replace affected
        assets.
  ❖     Provision of assistance for PAPs who have to rebuild their houses on their remaining land or
        building their houses in new places as arranged by the Project, or on newly assigned plots.
  ❖     Income and livelihood restoration allowances.
  ❖     Community consultation and public dissemination of compensation policy: (a) PAPs should
        be fully informed and consulted about land acquisition, leasing and relocation activities; (b)
        public awareness of the compensation policy and entitlements will be assessed among the
        PAPs; and (c) assessment of awareness of various options available to DPs as provided for in
        the RP.
  ❖     Income and livelihood restoration of PAPs.
  ❖     Operation of the complaint mechanism and complaint settlement of PAPs.
  ❖     Monitor the implementation of mitigation measures for social risks (if any) posed by labor
        influx of contractors into the communities surrounding the Project area;
  ❖     PAPs’ satisfaction level on various aspects of the RP will be monitoring and recorded.
  ❖     Through the implementation, trends on living standard will be observed and surveyed. Any
        potential issues in the recovering living standard are reported and suitable measures will be
        proposed to ensure the Project objectives.
280. The IMC must submit periodic reports every six months, reflecting the findings made during
the monitoring process. The PMU will review each report before submitting it to the World Bank,
ensuring it includes the following: (i) the progress of RP implementation; (ii) any differences between
implementation and RP regulations and principles; (iii) any outstanding issues and proposed
solutions for implementing agencies to promptly identify and resolve; and (iv) the progress in
monitoring issues identified in the previous reporting period.
281. In addition, IMC will conduct a post-resettlement assessment within 6 to 12 months after all
resettlement activities are completed. The post-resettlement assessment report will be included in the
project completion report. Resettlement is only considered complete when the post-resettlement
assessment and project completion audit confirm that all displaced persons have received full
compensation and assistance, and that their livelihoods and lives have been restored as planned.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                             Page | 125
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


XV. COST ESTIMATE AND BUDGET
15.1.   Source of Funding
282. The budget for the implementation of the Resettlement Plan will come from the counterpart
fund of the Hai Phong City People's Committee. The fund for compensation and resettlement will be
included in the total investment cost of the Project.
283. The PMU will transfer the budget for land acquisition, support and resettlement of the project
in full and on time through the Commune Compensation Council/Land Fund Development Center/
People's Committee of ward level. These units will make direct payments to households affected by
the project.
15.2.   Replacement Cost Method
284. The main objective of the replacement cost survey is to ensure compensation for all affected
properties at replacement cost. The replacement cost will be calculated through the actual survey
conducted by the independent appraiser as follows:
  ❖     The land price is determined at the time of making the resettlement report;
  ❖     Prices of trees and crops are determined at the present time;
  ❖     Prices of materials, labor, houses and works are regulated at the present time.
285. During the preparation of the RP, the replacement cost rapid assessment survey was carried
out in November 2025 through:
  ❖     Direct interview by questionnaire with households in the affected area and surrounding areas
        to collect information on market prices of different types of land and properties on land in the
        project area;
  ❖     Consult with representatives of relevant communes on land prices, houses/works, trees, crops
  ❖     Consult with some construction companies in the locality on construction unit prices and
        construction materials.
  ❖     Access to real estate companies, local real estate websites to find out information.
286. The results of the rapid survey on replacement costs indicate that the proposed prices of the
province are generally in line with market prices (In fact, the 2024 Land Law will come into effect
from August 1, 2024 and the Hai Phong City People's Committee has issued new regulations on
compensation, assistance, and resettlement, as well as unit prices for compensation of structures,
trees, and crops in 2024). Therefore, these results are used for estimating compensation payment
costs. Replacement costs will be updated at the time of resettlement to ensure compensation is based
on the current market price. The detailed approach and methods for surveying replacement prices are
summarized in Appendix 3
15.3.   Replacement Cost for Land
15.3.1. Principles for determining specific land prices
287. The Land Law 2024 (Article 158) stipulates that the principle of land valuation is to comply
with market principles, honesty, objectivity, transparency, independence and ensure harmony of
interests. Specifically:
  ❖     According to market principles: Specific land prices must be consistent with common land
        prices on the market.


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 126
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


  ❖     Compliance with procedures: Must comply with the correct methods, order and procedures
        for land valuation.
  ❖     Honesty, objectivity, transparency: Ensure publicity and transparency in the process of
        determining specific land prices.
  ❖     Ensuring independence: The valuation consultancy unit, the valuation council and the price
        approval agency must be independent of each other;
  ❖     Harmonization of interests: Must ensure a balance of interests between the State, land users
        and investors
15.3.2. Method for determining specific land prices
288. The land valuation methods prescribed in the Land Law 2024 include: (i) comparison method;
(ii) income method; (iii) suRAPlus method; and (iv) land price adjustment coefficient method.
289.

15.3.3. The compensation prices applied to estimate the cost for RP
   •   Compensation price for affected land
291. On 5 August 2025, the People's Committee of Hai Phong City promulgated Decision No.
3163/QĐ-UBND concerning the continued application of the land price table for the period 2020-
2024 throughout Hai Phong City until the promulgation of the 2026 land price table. Accordingly, it
authorises the continued application of the land price table promulgated by the People's Committee
of Hai Phong City pursuant to Decision No. 54/2019/QĐ-UBND dated 31 December 2019, as
amended and supplemented by Decision No. 22/2022/QĐ-UBND dated 28 April 2022, in respect of
the administrative boundaries of Hai Phong City prior to reorganisation and merger; and the
application of the land price table promulgated by the People's Committee of Hai Duong Province
pursuant to Decision No. 55/2019/QĐ-UBND dated 20 December 2019, as amended and
supplemented by Decisions No. 29/2021/QĐ-UBND dated 17 December 2021, No. 18/2023/QĐ-
UBND dated 9 May 2023, No. 1858/2023/QĐ-UBND dated 31 August 2023, No. 30/2024/QĐ-
UBND dated 12 August 2024, and No. 43/2024/QĐ-UBND dated 18 December 2024, in respect of
the administrative boundaries of Hai Duong Province prior to reorganisation and merger, until the
promulgation of the 2026 land price table of Hai Phong City. For reference purposes, the Consultant
has collected land transaction price unit in the real estate market from various sources:
       a.   Mua Ban Newspaper; Information from real estate companies;
       b.   Refer to unit prices of some projects in the nearby areas;
       c.   Consultation with local authority;
       d.   Survey of price through affected households in the project area
292. Land in the affected area includes residential land, non-agricultural land, agricultural land for
perennial trees and agricultural land for annual crops. Some land unit prices in the project area are
determined based on results collected from replacement cost survey, working with local authorities,
referring to information on Mua Ban newspapers, transaction prices at real estate office. On that
basis, a reference price is proposed for compensation calculation.
   •   Replacement cost for houses and structures
293. The characteristics of houses within the project's scope of influence are mainly temporary
houses. For houses and other construction works within the Project, the value of the house is
determined based on the market price of construction materials at the time of compensation
determination to enable the construction of a replacement house with at least the same area and
quality as the old house, or to repair the affected structural parts. Depreciation of assets and the value
of materials that the affected household can take advantage of are not included. The results of the
survey of house and architectural prices are presented in Appendix 3. Therefore, the unit price
proposed by the consultant to calculate compensation for houses and structures for households
mentioned in this report will be applied according to Decision No. 196/2025/QD-UBND dated
October 24, 2025 by the People's Committee of Hai Phong city on promulgating unit prices for actual
damage compensation for houses, residential buildings, and construction works to serve as the basis
for calculating compensation when the State recovers land in Hai Phong city.
   •   Replacement price for crops and trees
294. Because the project is invested and constructed mainly in areas outside residential areas, the
survey results of prices for crops and trees show an insignificant difference from the unit price
regulated by the Hai Phong City People's Committee. Therefore, the unit price proposed by the
consultant to calculate compensation for crops for households mentioned in this report will be applied
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 132
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)


according to Decision No. 3859/2025/QD-UBND dated September 24, 2026 by the People's
Committee of Hai Phong City on promulgating the regulations on unit price for compensation for
crop damage when the State acquires land in Hai Phong City.
15.4.   Estimated Cost
295. Costs for compensation and resettlement, including expenses for preparation and
implementation of the resettlement plan, administrative and management costs are estimated with the
following items:
        a.   Cost of compensation for land and other affected assets in the project area;
        b.   Cost for livelihood restoration programs and special support for vulnerable groups (single
             elderly, poor households, female-headed households with dependents, disabled heads of
             households, households under preferential treatment policy, families with meritorious
             services to the revolution, ...);
        c.   Support, allowances, bonus for the affected people who have to relocate out of the
             affected area;
        d.   Cost for the Compensation, Support and Resettlement Council at commune level and
             local officials to implement the Resettlement Plan;
        e.   Cost for independent monitoring consultant;
        f.   Contingency.
296. The estimated budget for the RP implementation of the project is approximately VND
1,729,374,156,689 (equivalent to USD 65,655,814.60 with an exchange rate of 1 USD = 26,340
VND). This budget includes compensation/support costs for land and non-land assets affected by the
project, livelihood restoration programs, management and land acquisition implementation costs,
replacement cost surveys, cost for independent monitoring activity and contingency fees. The funding
for land clearance activities will be allocated from the counterpart fund of Hai Phong City People's
Committee.

Appendix 3. Rapid assessment of livelihoods and business activities
         RAPID ASSESSMENT OF LIVELIHOODS AND BUSINESS ACTIVITIES
I. SCOPE OF THE SURVEY
a. Survey scope
Pursuant to discussions between the Project Management Unit (PMU) and the technical design
consultant, the subprojects will not necessitate temporary land acquisition for constructing project
components. During project implementation, however, certain households engaged in business
activities within the construction zones of Component 1 and Component 3 will experience partial
disruptions. To mitigate these effects, construction will employ segmented approaches, nocturnal
operations, sequential phasing, and progressive site restoration. A dedicated project impact
assessment has evaluated the extent of these disruptions on affected households. Furthermore, should
the social impact assessment reveal substantial and prolonged income reductions for these
households, the project will provide commensurate financial assistance.
This report delineates the survey scope as encompassing wards within the construction areas of
Components 2 and 3. Investigations focused on prospective temporary impacts, including disruptions
to street-based vending (arising from pipeline and pump station works) and fishing livelihoods along
the Re River (stemming from embankment construction). Drawing on a comprehensive review and
evaluation of impact severity, the report proposes mitigation measures tailored to prevailing
conditions in Hai Phong City.




       Re River (area with fishing activities)      Blue and red lines: Sewer pipelines to be
                                                    installed along the streets.
         Figure 5. Estimated scope of temporary impacts on businesses and livelihoods
b. Survey on Temporary Livelihood/Business Impacts
The survey on temporary livelihood and business impacts—encompassing street-based activities
under Component 3 and fishing operations on the Re River due to river embankment works—
encompasses, but is not limited to, the following principal tasks:
   •   Reviewing extant Vietnamese regulations, policies, and guidelines on support mechanisms
       for business disruptions.
   •   Consulting representatives from Ward People's Committees, irrigation management agencies,
       and cadastral officers in affected wards regarding provisional construction impacts.
   •   Conducting field surveys of prevailing business conditions and infrastructure along streets
       targeted for drainage system upgrades, alongside fishing activities on the Re River.
   •   Assessing and proposing suitable replacement unit rates for compensation and support related
       to land and associated assets affected by the project.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                           Page | 156
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

II. METHODOLOGIES FOR INVESTIGATION AND EVALUATION
a. Methods for Rapid Assessment of Impacts on Businesses and Livelihoods
   ➢ Qualitative Methods (In-depth Interviews)
   Target respondents: Owners of large enterprises, vulnerable business households (e.g., female-
   headed or elderly-led households), and vendors of relocation-challenged goods.
   Guiding questions:
           o   Have prior construction activities (e.g., road excavations or infrastructure works)
               disrupted your business operations or livelihoods?
           o   What specific impacts arose from those activities?
           o   What was the magnitude and duration of effects on your operations or livelihoods?
           o   What mitigation measures did you employ?
           o   Did you receive support from local authorities or contractors during implementation?
           o   What recommendations do you offer to the project owner and contractors for
               forthcoming activities?
   ➢ Key Informant Interviews (KII): Engaging functional agencies to validate data from local
     administrative perspectives on construction impacts to businesses and livelihoods, while
     eliciting recommendations and lessons learned.
   ➢ Field Observation: Undertaking site visits to document and photograph current business and
     livelihood conditions, enabling the consultant to quantify and classify potentially affected
     enterprises and activities.
b. Survey Results
      Drawing from direct stakeholder consultations, interviews with management agencies, and
local residents, the following synthesizes stakeholder observations, evaluations, and
recommendations concerning temporary impacts on business and livelihood activities under
Components 2 and 3:
c. Impacts on Re River Fishing
        Prior to the construction of the Cai Tack sluice, the Re River abounded in aquatic resources,
sustaining household livelihoods through tidal ingress of marine species into brackish and freshwater
zones. However, sluice installation since the 1980s—for river regulation purposes—has precipitated
a sharp decline in fish stocks, diminished resource quality, and reduced shrimp and fish sizes.
Presently, fishing involves approximately 20 small boats and constitutes only a supplementary
income source.
        In-depth interviews with Mr. T., a local boat operator, confirm that fishing serves as an
ancillary household activity, pursued primarily during idle periods from primary employment.
Current Re River fisheries yield predominantly small tilapia, with occasional catches exceeding 1 kg.
Larger specimens are sold for supplemental income, while smaller ones are retained for household
consumption or shared with kin and acquaintances. Mr. T. fishes approximately once or twice
weekly, underscoring the small-scale, non-primary nature of these operations. His activities have
proceeded uninterrupted in recent years, including during An Hai Company's recent riverbank
revetment works.
      The Re River, which also supplies domestic and irrigation water, undergoes routine
maintenance by its operator, including a current ~200 m upstream embankment project. With a wide

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                            Page | 157
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

riverbed (50–60 m in segments), the ~10 m embankment footprint minimally impedes navigation or
fishing. Phased construction further limits disruptions to small-scale local fishing in Hai Phong.
Officials from An Duong Ward affirm no obstructions to flows or navigation during ongoing
operations, maintenance, or embankment activities.
d. Impacts on Component 3 Affected Households' Temporary Business
        Construction activities along the culvert alignment will disrupt roadside businesses. The
HDPE D315–D500 collector line extends 2,600 m, with a total construction duration of
approximately 65 days using two work fronts. Mitigation employs nighttime construction and
daytime restoration via a segmented rolling method (20–30 m segments), with sequential piping
installation and terrain reinstatement. On dense or narrow roads, nighttime work includes daytime
coverage with 2 cm steel plates; wider, low-traffic roads permit daytime operations.
       Preliminary surveys of temporarily affected Component 3 businesses identify four categories:
(1) eateries, cafés, pharmacies, and lodging; (2) groceries and household goods; (3) beauty and
fashion services; and (4) consulting and banking services.
        In-depth interviews with affected business households revealed varied experiences. One
household selling steamed rice rolls (bánh cuốn) in mornings and evenings reported suspending
operations for excavation days during prior water supply pipe installation due to dust and access
difficulties, deterring customers. Business gradually normalized after initial days, but cumulative
closures spanned about ten days, yielding substantial income losses.
       Conversely, a nearby flower and coffee vendor experienced negligible disruption to flower
sales—attributable to location and product nature—and minimal revenue impact from indoor coffee
operations, as customer access persisted.
        Insights from prior projects employing analogous methods (road excavation for pipe laying)
indicate that segmented construction substantially curtails disruptions. Nonetheless, efficacy
demands rigorous adherence to temporary road restoration and backfilling protocols to sustain
customer access. Interviews with previously affected households affirm that the proposed plan—
short-segment rolling construction with rapid restoration—will limit cumulative full closures to
under half a month per household.

III. CONCLUSION
       Evidence from prior projects employing comparable construction techniques—such as road
excavation for pipe laying and river embankment works—demonstrates that segmented methods
substantially mitigate disruptions to business and livelihood activities.
        Effectiveness, however, hinges on stringent compliance with temporary road restoration and
backfilling measures to preserve customer access. In-depth interviews with previously affected
business and fishing households corroborate that the proposed plan—featuring short-segment
rolling construction and expedited restoration—will minimize impacts on commercial operations
and seasonal livelihoods.
