Appendix 4. Project Information Booklet (PIB)
                 Project: Hai Phong City Resilience Development Project (HPRDP)
  I.      General Project Information:
      -   Project Name: Hai Phong City Resilience Development Project (HPRDP).
      -   Executing Agency (Line Agency): Hai Phong City People’s Committee (Hai Phong CPC).
      -   Project Owner (Implementing Agency): Hai Phong Project Management Unit for
          Investment in Construction of Transport and Agriculture Works.
      -   Financier: International Bank for Reconstruction and Development (IBRD) under the World
          Bank Group (WB).
      -   Project Location: Hai Phong City.
      -   Total Investment Capital: VND 9,908.17 billion, equivalent to USD 394.433 million, of
          which:
             1. WB IBRD Loan: VND 6,684.98 billion, equivalent to USD 266.121 million,
                accounting for 67.46% of the preliminary total project investment; to cover
                investment costs for construction items of Component 1, Component 2, Component
                3, and part of Component 4.
             2. Domestic Counterpart Fund: VND 3,223.18 billion, equivalent to USD 128.311
                million, accounting for 32.54% of the preliminary total project investment; to cover
                costs for compensation and site clearance, taxes, project management, construction
                investment consultancy, and other implementation costs during the project
                implementation process.
      -   Tentative Implementation Timeline:
             1. Project Preparation: 2023-2026 (from the approval of the Project Proposal until the
                signing of the ODA Loan Agreement).
             2. Project Implementation: 2026-2030 (Counting from the time capital is allocated by
                the competent authority).
II.       Project Objective
II.1. Overall Objective:
To foster the socio-economic development and growth of Hai Phong City and promote sustainable
urban development through a multi-sector integrated investment package focusing on urban
connectivity and regional linkage; ensuring environmental sustainability, water security, and urban
flooding reduction; adapting to regional climate change; upgrading public spaces and enhancing
urban resilience.
II.2. Specific Objectives:
      •   To reduce urban flooding and adapt to climate change for the inner city of Hai Phong through
          the construction, upgrading, and rehabilitation of the drainage system.
      •   To improve environmental conditions towards climate change adaptation, combining
          drainage, environmental sanitation improvement, spatial development, and the creation of
          urban landscapes; creating drivers for green development and advanced services; and
          improving the quality of life for residents in the inner city area, specifically along both banks
          of the Re River, and Hai Phong City in general.

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                 Page | 161
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

       •   To enhance regional transport connectivity to create a driving force for the development of
           the Northwest - Southeast marine economic axis, promoting logistics development, aimed at
           building and developing Hai Phong into a regional linkage hub.
       •   To enhance the capacity for flood risk management and water quality control of river basins,
           ensuring safe and sustainable water supply for the city through construction, training, and
           technology transfer regarding intelligent management and monitoring systems; contributing
           to administrative reform and the formation and development of Hai Phong as a smart city.
III.       Project Implementation Scope
       •   Project Study Area: Includes the area on both sides of the Cam River extending to the Gia
           River in the North and the Lach Tray River in the South; the inter-provincial An Kim Hai
           river system to the East and the Bach Dang River to the West of Hai Phong City, covering an
           area of 193 km² (located in Thuy Nguyen City and the districts of Hong Bang and former An
           Duong). This includes research and general planning of contents according to project
           objectives, based on which specific construction investment items of the project will be
           phased to ensure investment efficiency, synchronization, and long-term viability.
       •   Construction Footprint of Project Items: Located within the administrative boundaries of
           Hong Bang, An Hai, An Duong, Gia Vien, Le Chan, An Bien, Ngo Quyen, Dong Hai, Thuy
           Nguyen, Nam Trieu, Bach Dang, Luu Kiem, and Hoa Binh wards of Hai Phong City, with an
           area of approximately 109 km².
Based on the specific objectives mentioned above, the Project is proposed to include 04
components. The general layout of the Components and proposed project items is presented in the
figure below.
1. Component 1: Integrated Development of Thuy Nguyen Urban Infrastructure Adapted to
Climate Change
This component aims to construct the Ring Road 3 route connecting Hai Phong City's beltway
transport infrastructure with regional transport and the Thuy Nguyen area, and to synchronously
build urban infrastructure to minimize environmental pollution, avoid traffic congestion, and save
travel time.
       •   Ring Road 3 Overview:
              o   Southern Start Point: Km0+00, at the intersection between Bui Vien Road (WB
                  Road) and Lien Phuong Road, connecting to the Hanoi - Hai Phong Expressway at
                  station Km104+200 (Hanoi - Hai Phong Expressway chainage), within Ngo Quyen
                  ward.
              o   End Point: Km18+680 at the intersection with National Road 10 (Km13+700 - NR10
                  chainage), within Hoa Binh ward.
              o   Alignment: From the Hanoi - Hai Phong Expressway, the route crosses the Cam River
                  (via Ngo Quyen Bridge) to Thuy Nguyen, continues across the Ruot Lon River,
                  follows the Eastern boundary of the VSIP area and along the Hau Long River, meets
                  Provincial Road 359 (at approx. Km10+906 - PR.359 chainage), then turns West and
                  continues straight to the end point at the intersection with NR 10.
              o   Scale: The total length of the entire route is approximately 18.65 km, including about
                  2.67 km of bridges crossing the Cam River and Ruot Lon River. Regarding scale and
                  classification, according to the approved planning, Ring Road 3 is classified as a Main
                  Urban Street (according to Table 5, TCVN 13592-2022), with a cross-section width
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                               Page | 162
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

               of 68m, including a 44m roadway (2x15m main route + 2x7m service roads), a 9m
               median strip (including a 5m center median and 2.0m separators between the main
               route and service roads on each side), and 7.5m sidewalks on each side.
           o   Phasing: However, in the immediate phase, investment will be carried out in phases
               (full site clearance, but service roads not yet constructed) with a Phase 1 cross-section
               scale as follows:
                   ▪   Main route roadway: 2x10.5m = 21.0m
                   ▪   Center median strip: = 5.0m
                   ▪   Shoulders on both sides: 2x0.5m = 1.0m
                   ▪   Total roadbed width: = 27.0m
2. Component 2: Re River Environmental Upgrade
This component aims to ensure freshwater security, improve water quality and environmental
sanitation of the Re River, enhance stormwater drainage management, prevent saline intrusion, and
adapt to climate change and sea-level rise. At the same time, it combines synchronous investment
in roads and infrastructure on both sides of the Re River to connect with transport along the river,
creating landscape and a public green space axis for the area from An Duong to Hong Bang.
a. Sub-component 2.1: Re River Infrastructure Upgrade
   •   Construction of the road along the Re River:
           o   The Re River is approximately 9.5km long, starting from Re 2 Bridge (intersection
               with National Road 10) to the end point at Cai Tat Sluice. The river width is
               approximately (40÷110)m. This sub-component will upgrade the existing road along
               the Re River bank and build a new management road along both sides of the river
               while creating space to arrange the wastewater collection system.
           o   Scale: The route has a cross-section right-of-way (ROW) width of approximately
               11.0m; except for areas with existing residential settlements close to the riverbank,
               where the ROW is 3.5m. This includes a 3.5m roadway, a 2.0m sidewalk adjacent to
               the river, and a 2.0m opposite sidewalk + earth slope. The total length of the newly
               invested management road along the river is approximately 13.77 km.
   •   Upgrading existing embankments and constructing additional river embankments in
       other areas:
           o   Upgrade, construct new embankments, and rehabilitate existing embankments with a
               total length of approximately 9.04 km, of which some sections use vertical
               embankments to create sufficient space for arranging wastewater collection
               infrastructure (as mentioned above).
b. Sub-component 2.2: Re River Basin Environmental Sanitation Upgrade
   •   Wastewater Collection System: Construct a system of interceptor sewers collecting
       wastewater on both sides of the Re River with 14.0 km of gravity sewers, 4.3 km of pressure
       sewers, and 12 wastewater pumping stations along the Re River management road and
       transmission pipelines leading to the An Duong 1 Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP),
       planned at Dong Thai commune, An Hai ward, adjacent to the left dike of the Lach Tray
       River; construct approximately 8.42 km of tertiary sewer network collecting household
       wastewater for synchronous connection to the wastewater collection sewer line.

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 163
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

   •   Wastewater Treatment Plant: Construct the An Duong 1 WWTP Phase 1 with a capacity
       of 10,000 m³/day. Treated wastewater meeting Type A standards according to
       QCVN14:2025/BTNMT will be discharged into the Lach Tray River located adjacent to the
       treatment area.
   •   Equipment: Provision of equipment for urban flood risk management systems, water quality
       management, and air environment management for areas within the project investment scope.
3. Component 3: Central Urban Flooding Reduction
This component aims to enhance storage and regulation capacity, reduce flooding, control water
levels, and improve the water environment of Tam Bac River/Lake, creating conditions for public
space development, urban redevelopment, embellishment of historical cultural values, and a
modern, attractive urban area. Main items include:
   •   Regulator Sluices: Construction of 01 regulator sluice at Tam Bac Bridge with Thuong Ly
       River and 01 regulator sluice at Thuy Doi Point at the mouth of Tam Bac River flowing into
       Cam River, forming a new Tam Bac River retention lake. Within the dam body of the
       regulator sluice at Thuy Doi Point, a stormwater pumping station with a capacity of 12 m³/s
       will be built to pump rainwater from the Tam Bac River lake out to the Cam River outside
       the urban area. The Tam Bac River lake combined with the existing Tam Bac lake creates a
       chain of retention lakes in the central urban drainage basin, with a total area of approximately
       14-15 ha.
   •   Connecting Culvert: Construction of a box culvert (WxH = 2.5x2.0m, Length L = 220m) connecting the existing
       Tam Bac Lake with the Tam Bac River lake. Construction and renovation of a number of drainage sewer lines to
       ensure corresponding capacity and enhance drainage capability, consisting of sewers with dimensions from WxH =
       1.0x1.0m to WxH = 3.0x2.0m, length 4.18km. The total length of stormwater drainage lines is approximately 4.40
       km.
   •   Wastewater Collection: Construction of a wastewater collection system including
       wastewater collection sewer lines and wastewater pumping stations from both sides of the
       Tam Bac River leading to Vinh Niem WWTP, with approximately 2.61 km of main
       wastewater collection sewers, diversion chambers (CSOs), 05 wastewater pumping
       stations, and renovation to upgrade the capacity of the existing Lan Be Pumping Station and
       tertiary sewers.
4. Component 4: System and Capacity Development for Climate Change Adapted Urban
Improvement
a. Sub-component 4.1: Enhancing Flood Risk Management Capacity Enhancing urban flood
management capacity. This sub-item will support the development of a system allowing technical
experts and decision-makers to better forecast and respond to floods through:
   •   Developing and calibrating a dynamic hydraulic model for flood forecasting and early
       warning scenarios for the areas of An Duong, Hong Bang, Thuy Nguyen, Le Chan, Ngo
       Quyen, and Dong Hai;
   •   Operating an integrated flood risk management system for the inner city area, including
       operating procedures for sluice gates and stormwater pumping stations when extreme
       conditions are forecast;
   •   Establishing a framework and information system to improve the Operation and
       Maintenance (O&M) of flood control infrastructure for the areas of An Duong, Hong Bang,
       Thuy Nguyen, Le Chan, Ngo Quyen, and Dong Hai; and
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                          Page | 164
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

   •   Providing training, workshops, and technical assistance to Hai Phong City officials to enhance
       flood risk management capacity, including the integration of Nature-based Solutions (NbS)
       into flood control infrastructure.
   •   This sub-component contributes directly to the project's objective of addressing the city's
       resilience risks and promoting the effectiveness of Components 1-3 of the project.
b. Sub-component 4.2: Enhancing Water Quality and Environmental Management Capacity
Proposal to establish air and water environmental monitoring systems at project investment items
and within Hai Phong City, connected to the Environmental Monitoring Center or the city's
environmental management agency, and operating procedures, including:
   •   Monitoring the quality and quantity of wastewater and effluent of the An Duong 1 WWTP
       and water quality at the Tam Bac sluice gate constructed under the project, connecting to the
       City's Environmental Monitoring Center;
   •   Monitoring air quality (H2S) of the An Duong 1 WWTP;
   •   Supporting the establishment of O&M procedures for the wastewater treatment system in the
       city to improve this activity.
   •   This sub-component contributes directly to the objectives of the Project and Components 2
       and 3.
c. Sub-component 4.3: Project Management Technical and financial resources provided by Hai
Phong City to ensure effective project implementation, construction quality, compliance with the
Bank's environmental and social standards, while ensuring transparency in procurement and high-
quality construction. Activities include the following work contents:
   •   Project Preparation Support: Surveys, Pre-Feasibility Study (Pre-FS) Report; Feasibility
       Study (FS) Report; Detailed planning for a number of project items; Other supporting reports
       serving WB appraisal.
   •   Project Implementation Support: Detailed design and preparation of Bidding Documents;
       Construction supervision services and other consulting services.
   •   Technical Assistance for Component 4: Establishing an early warning system including
       hydraulic models, GIS database, and establishing operating management and flood risk
       management procedures after constructing the early warning system; Supporting the
       finalization of water treatment system O&M procedures.
   •   Technical Assistance and other support services during the project implementation
       phase: Independent Audit; Independent Environmental and Social Monitoring to comply
       with WB social and environmental standards while still ensuring transparency in procurement
       bidding and high-quality construction; Post-project evaluation; and other technical support
       services. Training, workshops, and study tours; Propaganda and community awareness
       raising; and other technical support services.
   •   Project Management Support: Project implementation costs of the Project Management
       Unit (PMU); Training, workshops, and study tours; and other technical support services.
PROJECT GRIEVANCE REDRESS MECHANISM
The project’s GRM includes the following steps:
   •   Step 1 – Ward People's Committee: If a household or individual has a complaint, it may
       submit a written complaint or verbally inform the WPC's one-stop office. The officer in
       charge of this office is responsible for notifying the commune leaders of a resolution. The
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                           Page | 165
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

         WPC's will meet personally with the complainant. The time limit for settling complaints shall
         be 30 days from the time the complaints are received. The WPC's secretariat is responsible
         for documenting and filing all complaints within its jurisdiction.
     •   Step 2 – City People's Committee: If after 30 days, the aggrieved affected household does
         not hear from the PC of commune or if the affected household is not satisfied with the decision
         taken on his or her complaint, the affected household may bring the case, either in writing or
         in person, to the CPC. The CPC has 45 days to resolve the complaint. The CPC secretariat is
         responsible for maintaining records of complaints, actions, and outcomes. Complainants can
         also submit their complaints to the Court if they wish.
     •   Step 3 (final) - Administrative Court: If, after 45 days following the lodging of the
         complaint with the CPC, the aggrieved household does not hear from the CPC or if he or she
         is not satisfied with the decision taken on his or her complaint, the case may be brought to the
         Court for adjudication. The court's decision will be final.

Appendix 6. DDR for the project’s resettlement sites
         LEGAL AND ENVIRONMENTAL AND SOCIAL DUE DILIGENCE FOR
                BACH DANG RESETTLEMENT AREA – HAI PHONG CITY
            (Review of Compliance with Vietnamese Laws in Support of the HPRDP)
1. PURPOSE AND SCOPE OF THE DUE DILIGENCE
This Legal, Social and Environmental Due Diligence (DDR) has been prepared in support of the Hai
Phong City Resilience Development Project (HPRDP) to assess the compliance with Vietnamese
laws and regulations of the Investment Project for Construction of Infrastructure of the Bach
Dang Resettlement Area, which will be used to accommodate a portion of households affected by
HPRDP.
The Bach Dang Resettlement Area is an independently financed public investment project of Hai
Phong City, developed to serve multiple public investment projects, including HPRDP. The
resettlement project does not use World Bank financing and is not part of the HPRDP investment
scope.
Accordingly, this due diligence has been conducted on the basis that:
   •   The project complies with applicable Vietnamese laws and regulations on investment, land,
       environment, and resettlement;
   •   The Environmental and Social Standards (ESSs) of the World Bank ESF are not
       mandatorily applicable to the Bach Dang Resettlement Project;
   •   The review satisfies the World Bank’s requirement to demonstrate national legal
       compliance for shared resettlement areas that are not financed by the Bank.
2. OVERVIEW OF THE BACH DANG RESETTLEMENT PROJECT
2.1 General Information
   •   Project name: Investment in Construction of Infrastructure for the Bach Dang Resettlement
       Area
   •   Location: Bach Dang Ward, Hai Phong City
   •   Project owner: Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Transport and Agricultural Works
   •   Implementation period: 2025–2028 (According to the information confirmed at the meeting
       with the Project Owner, the Project is expected to be completed and put into operation before
       30 December 2026.)
   •   Total investment: approximately VND 544.1 billion
2.2. Geographic Location
The resettlement area is developed on a total land area of approximately 19.93 hectares located in
Bach Dang Ward, Hai Phong City, as detailed below:
Location and boundaries:
   •   To the East: bordering Battalion 158 and the existing rural residential area;
   •   To the West: bordering the section from Phan Dat Canal to Gia River (adjacent to the Minh
       Duc ring road as per the approved plan);
   •   To the South: bordering Phan Dat Canal;
   •   To the North: bordering the existing rice cultivation land.
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                           Page | 183

2.3. Land Use Scale and Technical and Social Infrastructure
The project is planned on a total land area of approximately 19.93 hectares, comprising two
resettlement areas, with the following key characteristics:
(i) Residential Resettlement Land
   •   Total number of residential resettlement plots: about 958 plots;
   •   Plot size: generally ranging from 80 m² to 120 m² per plot, in accordance with urban planning
       standards;
   •   Each plot is provided with access to internal roads and full technical infrastructure, including
       power supply, water supply, drainage, and public lighting.
(ii) Drainage and Wastewater Treatment Infrastructure
The project includes a centralized wastewater treatment plant (WWTP) with:
   •   Design capacity: The resettlement area has 1 WWTP (with designed capacity of 950 m³/day),
       suitable for a planned population of about 3,832 people;
   •   Collection system: separate wastewater drainage system, independent from stormwater
       drainage;
   •   Treatment technology: biological treatment combined with sedimentation and disinfection.
(iii) Green Areas, Parks, and Public Spaces
   •   Green space and park areas: accounting for approximately 10–12% of the total project area;
   •   Including centralized parks, buffer green belts, and roadside trees along internal roads;
   •   These green spaces contribute to microclimate improvement, reduction of dust and noise, and
       provision of community spaces.
(iv) Other Social and Technical Infrastructure
   •   Internal road network and parking areas;
   •   Power supply, water supply, public lighting, and fire prevention and firefighting systems;
   •   Land reserved for small-scale public facilities serving the resettlement community;

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                             Page | 184
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

   •   Land allocated for cultural, religious, and educational facilities.
(v) Public Utilities and Services
   •   Educational facilities: The surrounding area includes educational institutions such as Pham
       Ngu Lao High School (approximately 300 m away), Ngu Lao Primary School (approximately
       500 m away), and Ngu Lao Kindergarten, meeting the learning needs of children. In addition,
       according to the approved planning, land within the Project area is allocated for the
       construction of a kindergarten, contributing to the completion of on-site educational
       infrastructure.
   •   Healthcare facilities: Healthcare facilities and medical service providers are located within a
       radius of approximately 0.5–1.0 km from the Project site, meeting the needs for primary
       healthcare, general medical examination and treatment, and basic first aid for resettled
       residents.
   •   Cultural and social facilities: The Project area includes a community cultural house,
       community activity points, sports grounds, and local religious and belief facilities, meeting
       the needs for cultural, spiritual activities and community interaction of local residents.
   •   Commercial and service facilities: Markets and a system of grocery stores, food services,
       pharmacies, post offices, and other essential services are located near the Project area,
       basically meeting the daily living needs of residents.

Overall, the resettlement area being located close to existing healthcare, educational, commercial,
and cultural–religious facilities enables residents to easily access essential services, quickly stabilize
their lives after resettlement, and contributes to improving quality of life, ensuring harmonious
development of the local community.
3. RELATIONSHIP WITH HPRDP
   •    The Bach Dang Resettlement Area has been planned, approved, and implemented
        independently of HPRDP;
   •    HPRDP does not provide financing for the construction of the resettlement area;
   •    The use of the Bach Dang Resettlement Area for HPRDP utilizes only part of the approved
        resettlement plots and does not result in additional construction items, expansion of scale,
        or changes to the approved design;
   •    Accordingly, the Bach Dang Resettlement Area is considered a shared resettlement site,
        prepared and implemented in compliance with Vietnam’s national legal framework.
4. APPLICABLE LEGAL FRAMEWORK
The Bach Dang Resettlement Project has been prepared and implemented in accordance with the
following key legal documents:
   •    Law on Public Investment;
   •    Land Law and its guiding decrees;
   •    Law on Environmental Protection (2020);
   •    Decree No. 08/2022/ND-CP;
   •    Decree No. 05/2025/ND-CP of the Government;
   •    Circular No. 02/2022/TT-BTNMT;
   •    Circular No. 07/2025/TT-BNNMT of the Ministry of Agriculture and Environment;
   •    National technical regulations on environment (QCVNs);

   •   Relevant regulations on planning, construction, fire prevention and firefighting, water supply
       and drainage, and waste management.
5. LEGAL AND ENVIRONMENTAL STATUS OF THE PROJECT
5.1 Investment Policy and Planning
   •   The Project has been approved in principle by the Hai Phong City People’s Committee
       (Decision No. 3639/QD-UBND dated 05 September 2025 of the Hai Phong City People’s
       Committee).
   •   The 1/500-scale detailed plan of the Bach Dang Ward Resettlement Area has been approved
       under Decision No. 814/QD-UBND dated 28 November 2025 of the Bach Dang Ward
       People’s Committee.
5.2 Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA)
   •   The Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA) of the project was prepared in accordance with
       the Law on Environmental Protection (2020).
   •   The provincial-level EIA appraisal council convened the appraisal meeting in November
       2025, following receipt of the EIA dossier on 3 November 2025.
   •   Based on the appraisal comments, the project owner revised, supplemented, and submitted
       the completed EIA dossier on 4 December 2025.
   •   At the time of preparation of this DDR, the EIA dossier is under final administrative
       procedures for issuance of the approval decision by the competent authority.
From a legal and technical perspective, the EIA has completed all required steps under Vietnamese
law.
6. KEY ENVIRONMENTAL CONTENTS OF THE EIA
6.1 Environmental Baseline Conditions
   •   The current land use is mainly agricultural land (rice cultivation), interspersed with water
       bodies, existing roads, vacant land, and a number of scattered buildings and small-scale
       technical infrastructure facilities.
   •   The project area does not fall within environmentally sensitive zones and does not include
       protected areas or endangered species;
   •   Air, water, and soil quality at the time of survey complied with applicable national standards.
6.2 Environmental Impacts and Mitigation Measures
Pre-construction Phase
During the preparation and pre-construction phase, the Bach Dang Resettlement Area infrastructure
development Project will acquire approximately 19.93 ha of land, of which agricultural production
land (mainly rice cultivation land) accounts for a large proportion (approximately 16.72 ha). Land
acquisition will result in the loss of agricultural production land and affect the livelihoods of
households engaged in agricultural activities in the Project area. In addition, the Project will also
acquire a portion of internal field roads, vacant land, and some scattered structures and small-scale
technical infrastructure facilities.
Within the Project boundary, construction activities will occupy approximately 500 m of the Phan
Dat Canal and several irrigation canals and ditches associated with the Dong Chuong and Vung
Thanh pumping stations, which may affect irrigation and drainage activities of surrounding
agricultural production areas if not properly addressed.
                                                                                          P a g e | 188
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

To manage and mitigate potential impacts during the pre-construction phase, the Project has allocated
budget for compensation, assistance, and land clearance in accordance with current legal regulations.
Land acquisition and site clearance will be implemented following these steps: identification of
affected persons, detailed inventory; issuance of land acquisition notices; public disclosure of Project
information; preparation, consultation, and approval of compensation and assistance plans; and
payment of compensation and assistance. Households whose agricultural land is acquired will be
fully compensated in accordance with applicable unit prices and policies, and will also be considered
for assistance in livelihood stabilization, occupational transition, and livelihood restoration. For
affected irrigation canals and ditches, the Project Owner commits to study, propose, and implement
appropriate restoration/replacement solutions to ensure irrigation capacity for agricultural production
areas outside the Project boundary and drainage capacity for adjacent residential areas; specific
solutions will be calculated, documented, and publicly disclosed during subsequent implementation
stages.
Unexploded ordnance (UXO): The Project Owner will enter into a contract with a licensed military
unit to carry out UXO clearance prior to the commencement of construction works.
Construction phase:
Key impacts include dust, noise, vibration, domestic wastewater from construction workers,
construction solid waste, and localized traffic safety risks.
Mitigation measures include dust suppression, covering of materials, appropriate construction
scheduling, proper waste collection and disposal, installation of barriers and warning signs, and
implementation of occupational safety measures.
Operation phase:
Main impacts include domestic wastewater, municipal solid waste, and potential odor risks from the
WWTP if not properly operated.
Mitigation measures include stable operation of the WWTP, organized solid waste collection through
municipal services, regular maintenance of technical infrastructure, and enhancement of green
spaces.
Overall environmental impacts are assessed as low to moderate and manageable.
6.3 Design Standards and Effluent Quality Requirements of the Wastewater Treatment Plant
   •   Design capacity: 950 m³/day;
   •   Type of wastewater: domestic wastewater;
   •   Effluent quality standard: QCVN 14:2025/BTNMT – Column A;
   •   Key controlled parameters include pH, BOD₅, COD, TSS, Ammonium, Total Nitrogen, Total
       Phosphorus, and Coliform.
The application of Column A as the design effluent standard demonstrates a high level of
environmental protection, ensuring safety for the receiving water body and consistency with Hai
Phong City’s sustainable urban development objectives.
7. COMMUNITY CONSULTATION AND STAKEHOLDER PARTICIPATION
Community consultation was conducted during the EIA preparation process in accordance with the
Law on Environmental Protection (2020).
   •   Consulted stakeholders: Bach Dang Ward People’s Committee, the Fatherland Front and
       mass organizations, representatives of affected households, and local community members;

                                                                                           P a g e | 189
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

   •   Consultation methods: public meetings and disclosure of EIA information as required by law;
   •   Scale: approximately 100 participants attended the consultation meetings (based on signed
       attendance lists included in the EIA dossier).
Consultation results:
   •   The majority of opinions supported project implementation;
   •   No significant objections were recorded;
   •   Comments mainly related to implementation schedule, infrastructure quality, and
       environmental management during construction;
   •   These comments were incorporated into the EIA.
Consultation with households affected by HPRDP continues to be conducted under the
Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP) and Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM) of HPRDP.
8. OVERALL ASSESSMENT FOR HPRDP
The due diligence concludes that:
   •   The Bach Dang Resettlement Area has been prepared and implemented in compliance with
       Vietnamese laws and regulations;
   •   No significant unaddressed environmental or social risks have been identified;
   •   The use of this resettlement area for HPRDP does not give rise to additional legal,
       environmental, or social obligations beyond those under national law.
9. CONCLUSION
The Bach Dang Resettlement Area is an independently financed public investment project, not
using World Bank funds, and has been prepared and implemented in accordance with Vietnamese
legal requirements on investment, land, environment, and resettlement.
The resettlement area is legally and environmentally suitable for accommodating households
affected by the Hai Phong Urban Development and Flood Resilience Project (HPRDP) and
meets the World Bank’s requirement regarding compliance with the national legal framework.

         LEGAL AND ENVIRONMENTAL AND SOCIAL DUE DILIGENCE FOR
                NAM TRIEU RESETTLEMENT AREA – HAI PHONG CITY
            (Review of Compliance with Vietnamese Laws in Support of the HPRDP)
1. PURPOSE AND SCOPE OF THE DUE DILIGENCE
This Legal, Social and Environmental Due Diligence (DDR) has been prepared in support of the
Hai Phong City Resilience Development Project (HPRDP) to assess the compliance with
Vietnamese laws and regulations of the Investment Project for Construction of Infrastructure
of the Nam Trieu Resettlement Area, which will be used to accommodate a portion of
households affected by HPRDP.
The Nam Trieu Resettlement Area is an independently financed public investment project of
Hai Phong City, developed to serve multiple public investment projects, including HPRDP. The
resettlement project does not use World Bank financing and is not part of the HPRDP
investment scope.
Accordingly, this due diligence has been conducted on the basis that:
   •   The project complies with applicable Vietnamese laws and regulations on investment, land,
       environment, and resettlement;
   •   The Environmental and Social Standards (ESSs) of the World Bank ESF are not
       mandatorily applicable to the Nam Trieu Resettlement Project;
   •   The review satisfies the World Bank’s requirement to demonstrate national legal
       compliance for shared resettlement areas that are not financed by the Bank.
2. OVERVIEW OF THE NAM TRIEU RESETTLEMENT PROJECT
2.1 General Information
   •   Project name: Investment in Construction of Infrastructure for the Nam Trieu Resettlement
       Area
   •   Location: Nam Trieu Ward, Hai Phong City
   •   Project owner: Hai Phong Project Management Unit for Transport and Agricultural Works
   •   Implementation period: 2025–2028 (According to the information confirmed at the meeting
       with the Project Owner, the Project is expected to be completed and put into operation before
       30 December 2026.)
   •   Total investment: approximately VND 356.3 billion
2.2. Geographic Location
The resettlement area is developed on a total land area of approximately 13.66 hectares located in
Nam Trieu Ward, Hai Phong City, comprising two sub-areas, as detailed below:
5.09-ha Resettlement Area
Location and boundaries:
   •   Northeast: adjacent to the Dau Cau residential area;
   •   Southwest: adjacent to the Lach Se residential area;
   •   Northwest: adjacent to the rural residential development project in the Dau Cau area;
   •   Southeast: adjacent to Lap Le Primary School area.
8.56-ha Resettlement Area

Location and boundaries:
   •   Northeast: adjacent to an existing residential area;
   •   Southwest: adjacent to the cemetery area and Huong Road;
   •   Northwest: adjacent to agricultural land (paddy fields);
   •   Southeast: adjacent to the rural residential development project in the Dau Cau area.

       area.

       of the Project area, serves as a hub for essential goods supply and adequately meets the daily
       livelihood needs of residents in the resettlement area.

6. KEY ENVIRONMENTAL CONTENTS OF THE EIA

       interspersed with ponds, lakes, internal irrigation canals, existing transportation land, a

   •   The project area does not fall within environmentally sensitive zones and does not include
       protected areas or endangered species;
   •   Air, water, and soil quality at the time of survey complied with applicable national standards.
6.2 Environmental Impacts and Mitigation Measures
Pre-construction Phase
During the preparation and pre-construction phase, the Project will acquire approximately 13.66 ha
of land, including about 11.31 ha of agricultural land, and is expected to affect approximately 420
households. Land acquisition will result in the loss of productive land, require the relocation of a
number of households, and affect the livelihoods of farming households and small-scale business
operators in the Project area. In addition, the Project will involve the relocation of three (03)
individual graves within the 8.56-ha area, the relocation and undergrounding of the existing medium-
voltage power line, and the temporary occupation of a section of internal irrigation canals.


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                            Page | 196
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

To manage potential impacts during the pre-construction phase, the Project has allocated budget for
compensation, land acquisition, and resettlement, including compensation for land, structures, and
assets attached to land; assistance for relocation, livelihood stabilization, and livelihood restoration
through vocational training, job transition, and employment support, with the objective of ensuring
that affected households are able to maintain or improve their living standards compared to pre-
project conditions. Affected households will receive full compensation in accordance with applicable
regulations for agricultural land, crops, and livestock. For individual graves, financial assistance will
be provided to allow households to carry out relocation in accordance with their preferences.
With respect to the medium-voltage power line, the Project will implement relocation, removal of
utility poles, and undergrounding works, including the reuse or relocation of transformers in
accordance with the approved technical plan. Regarding the irrigation canals, the Project Owner
commits to reinstating or replacing affected irrigation infrastructure to ensure continued irrigation
and drainage for areas outside the Project boundary and adequate drainage for adjacent residential
areas. The scale and specific technical solutions will be calculated, described, and publicly disclosed
in subsequent project stages.
Unexploded ordnance (UXO): The Project Owner will enter into a contract with a licensed military
unit to carry out UXO clearance prior to the commencement of construction works.
Construction phase:
Key impacts include dust, noise, vibration, domestic wastewater from construction workers,
construction solid waste, and localized traffic safety risks.
Mitigation measures include dust suppression, covering of materials, appropriate construction
scheduling, proper waste collection and disposal, installation of barriers and warning signs, and
implementation of occupational safety measures.
Operation phase:
Main impacts include domestic wastewater, municipal solid waste, and potential odor risks from the
WWTP if not properly operated.
Mitigation measures include stable operation of the WWTP, organized solid waste collection through
municipal services, regular maintenance of technical infrastructure, and enhancement of green
spaces.
Overall environmental impacts are assessed as low to moderate and manageable.

Appendix 7. Guidelines for preparation of IRP during the project implementation
1. Objectives
The primary objective of the Income Restoration Program (IRP) is to assist severely affected
households and vulnerable groups in restoring their livelihoods and improving, or at least
maintaining, their living standards and income levels to pre-project levels, in compliance with the
World Bank’s Environmental and Social Standard 5 (ESS5).
2. Eligible Beneficiaries
Based on the results of the Inventory of Losses (IOL) and Social Assessment (SA) of the HPRDP,
the eligible subjects for the IRP include:
   1. Severely Affected Households (SAHs): Households losing 30% or more of their total
      agricultural landholding; or households who must relocate their housing and concurrently
      lose their income source from business/production.
   2. Vulnerable Households (VHs): Poor households, near-poor households, female-headed
      households with dependents, households with persons with disabilities, elderly households
      living alone, and other social policy beneficiaries.
   3. Affected Business Households: Households that must discontinue production or business
      activities due to land acquisition or project construction (including both temporary and
      permanent impacts).
3. Preparation and Implementation Process
The IRP will be implemented according to the following steps during the project implementation
phase:
   ➢ Step 1: Needs Assessment
A needs assessment survey must be updated immediately after the detailed compensation plan is
established.
   •   Action: The Project Management Unit (PMU) shall coordinate with the Women's Union,
       Farmers' Union, and the People's Committees of the project wards to organize separate
       consultation meetings with eligible households.
   •   Survey Content:
           o    Current capacity (education level, vocational skills, available capital).
           o    Aspirations for career transition (cultivation, livestock breeding, small-scale trading,
                vocational training, or factory work).
           o    Note: The Social Assessment indicates that many household heads are elderly
                (average age 62); therefore, livelihood models must be appropriate for this age group
                (prioritizing high-tech agriculture, livestock, or small business over industrial
                vocational training).
   ➢ Step 2: Design of Support Activities
Based on the needs assessment, the IRP will include the following components:
a. Vocational Training and Job Introduction:
   •   Collaborate with Continuing Education Centers and Agricultural Extension Centers to
       organize training courses on: Garment making, civil electricity, mechanics, cooking, and
       agricultural techniques.


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 199
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

   •   Prioritize children of affected households for recruitment into simple labor jobs during project
       construction or introduce them to jobs in industrial zones in Hai Phong (e.g., VSIP, Trang
       Due).
b. Credit Support and Financial Management:
   •   Facilitate access to preferential loans from the Vietnam Bank for Social Policies (VBSP) or
       credit funds managed by the Women's Union.
   •   Provide training on financial literacy and the effective use of compensation money for
       livelihood reinvestment.
c. Support for Agricultural/Business Restoration:
   •   Provide support in terms of crop seeds, livestock breeds, and fertilizers for households
       continuing agricultural production on the remaining land.
   •   Support legal procedures, business registration, and tax exemptions/reductions during the
       initial period for relocated business households.
   ➢ Step 3: Budget Approval
   •   The budget for the IRP is a separate component within the total Resettlement Budget.
   •   Detailed cost estimates for each model (e.g., cost per training course, cost of seedlings per
       household) must be prepared and submitted to the Hai Phong City People's Committee for
       approval.
   ➢ Step 4: Implementation Arrangements
   •   Project Management Unit (PMU): Holds overall responsibility, manages the budget, and
       signs contracts with service providers (vocational schools, agricultural extension centers).
   •   Ward People's Committees & Mass Organizations: Supervise directly, mobilize
       households to participate, and assist in resolving arising difficulties.
   •   Independent Monitoring Consultant (IMC): Monitors the progress and effectiveness of
       the program.
4. Monitoring and Evaluation
The IRP will be monitored through the following indicators:
   •   Number of households registered and completing training courses.
   •   Number of people finding new jobs or stabilizing businesses after 6 months/1 year.
   •   Average household income after participating in the IRP compared to pre-project levels
       (Target: Equal to or higher).
   •   Level of satisfaction of participants with the program.
5. Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM) for IRP
Any inquiries or complaints related to the identification of eligible subjects, delays in livelihood
support disbursement, or the quality of training will be addressed in accordance with the project's
established Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM).

RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

Appendix 8. Rapid assessment of replacement cost
RAPID REPORT ON THE SURVEY RESULTS OF REPLACEMENT COST
1.        SCOPE OF THE SURVEY
1.1.      Survey scope
This report defined the scope of the investigation to be limited within 8 wards in Hai Phong city,
which are planned to use loans from the World Bank (WB). Studies and surveys on replacement cost
for land, crops and vegetation, and assets in the area were conducted to determine the current market
value in comparison with the current prices issued by the People's Committee of Hai Phong city.
Reviewing and evaluating the differences (if any) to propose unit prices that will be applied for the
development of Resettlement Action Plans for Component 1, 2.
1.2.      Replacement cost survey
The implementation of the Replacement cost Survey in the Component 1, 2. The replacement cost
survey carried out will include but not be limited to the following main tasks:
Reviewing the existing regulations, policies and guidelines of Vietnam and the localities on the
development of unit prices of land and assets on land, the World Bank’s policies and principles of
replacement cost surveys applied to projects funded by international donors.
Consulting with representatives of the People's Committees of communes/ward, cadastral officers of
communes affected by the subproject on the existing price list of land and assets on land, the
suitability of the current price list as well as the replacement cost survey method used by the survey
team. Consulting with the mentioned units on the results of the replacement cost survey after
implementation.
Surveying the replacement costs for land, assets, plants and crops on land.
In addition to determining unit prices for land types and assets on land, related transaction costs
include fees, charges, taxes for land transfer transactions, change of land use purpose, application for
construction permits, etc.
Assessing and proposing appropriate replacement costs for compensation and support for land and
assets on land affected by the Project.
2. STAKEHOLDERS               AND     METHODOLOGIES              FOR      INVESTIGATION           AND
EVALUATION
2.1.      Stakeholders
       According to the World Bank: Replacement cost is defined as a method of valuation yielding
compensation sufficient to replace assets, plus necessary transaction costs associated with asset
replacement.
       Land valuation methods are conducted in accordance with the Government's Decree No.
71/2024/ND-CP dated June 27, 2024, regulating land prices, and the Government's Decree No.
226/2025/ND-CP dated August 15, 2025, amending and supplementing a number of articles of
decrees detailing the implementation of the Land Law.
          Methods used for the replacement cost survey:
    - Comparison method: Surveys on construction costs for new houses and structures, and selling
prices of crops were conducted. These survey prices are compared with the approved replacement
costs and compensation rates under current regulations of the City People's Committee to propose a
reasonable replacement cost.
       − Cost method:
Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                              Page | 201
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

       •   Residential land: Reviewing transaction information and collected market prices, and
           consulting with local people in the project area; comparing surveyed land prices in the
           affected areas (including taxes and fees) with the benefits received by people from the project
           (receiving land in resettlement sites at prices stipulated by the Provincial People's Committee
           for displaced households); and examining actual compensation rates currently applied in the
           area and agreed upon by local people.
       •   Houses and structures: Surveying unit prices of materials, equipment, and costs for
           constructing assets similar to the acquired assets; comparing with the estimated results from
           the comparison method to propose a reasonable replacement cost.
       •   Trees and crops: Calculating costs from seeding, seedling, cultivation, and harvesting;
           comparing with the estimated results from the comparison method to propose a reasonable
           replacement cost.
       •   For assets where replacement costs have been approved by the City People's Committee:
           Price fluctuations for similar assets will be determined by the Consultant through the
           Consumer Price Index (CPI). If the fluctuation rate does not exceed 5%, the approved
           replacement cost remains applicable but must be equivalent to the compensation rates
           approved at the same time by the City People's Committee.
Based on the task requirements, stakeholders were identified and consulted and interviewed to collect
information and documents related to land prices, assets on land, etc. The main stakeholders
identified for discussion, interviews and information/document collection are as follows.
-      Households include those with land use rights affected and unaffected (adjacent to the affected
       land or in the same village/hamlet).
-      Land brokers;
-      Representatives of the People's Committee of communes/ward, cadastral civil servants of
       communes/ward;
-      People buying and selling trees and wood;
-      Shops selling construction materials
2.2.       Survey and evaluation methodologies
The survey team used the following methods to determine replacement costs in 8 ward in Hai Phong
city.
2.2.1. Land
The development of compensation price for acquired land is based on market value. The best method
to determine this market value is to collect data on recent land transactions in the area. However, the
transfer of land use rights between households is not always conducted through local management
agencies, causing transactions to not be recorded and updated. The survey team needs to collect
transaction evidence to support the determination of the price framework. The survey team also needs
to collect information as a basis for price developmen from direct interviews with land users in the
area affected by the subproject, including those whose land is affected and unaffected. The interviews
include the following contents:
Recent land use right transfers in the area;
The value at which (affected and unaffected) land users are willing to sell their land (or transfer land
use rights).
The land price survey will cover all types of land affected by the subproject:

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 202
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

2.2.2. House and structures
According to the field survey, design plan and cadastral map integration, the survey team did not see
any affected houses or architectural objects, therefore, the team will not conduct any steps to
investigate or survey prices for houses and architectural objects.
2.2.3. Trees and Crops
The basis for developing replacement costs is to determine the average market price for each crop
and tree. The basic information for developing prices was collected from interviews with owners of
similar crops and trees in the locality. The interviews included:
The price at which crop/tree owners are willing to sell for each crop/tree type. The price of perennial
trees is valued differently based on the age and use value of the tree (except for valuable ornamental
trees).
Market price: The consulting team surveyed the transaction prices of different crops/trees in the
market
2.3.           Legal base:
       (i)        Decision No. 171/2025/QD-UBND dated September 24, 2025 by the Hai Phong City
                  People's Committee promulgating regulations detailing specific contents on
                  compensation, support, and resettlement when the State acquires land in Hai Phong City.
       (ii)       Decision No. 3163/QD-UBND dated August 5, 2025 by the Hai Phong City People's
                  Committee on the application of the 5-year land price list (2020-2024) in Hai Phong City
                  until the issuance of the 2026 land price list.
       (iii)      Decision No. 54/2019/QD-UBND dated December 31, 2019 by the Hai Phong City
                  People's Committee on promulgating regulations on the price list of land types for the 5-
                  year period (2020-2024) in Hai Phong City.
       (iv)       Decision No. 3859/QD-UBND dated September 24, 2025 by the Hai Phong City People's
                  Committee promulgating unit prices for compensation for damage to crops and livestock
                  when the State acquires land in Hai Phong City.
       (v)        Decision No. 196/2025/QD-UBND dated October 24, 2025 by the Hai Phong City
                  People's Committee promulgating unit prices for compensation for actual damage to
                  houses, residential houses, and construction works attached to land when the State
                  acquires land in Hai Phong City.

5.         CONCLUSION
The project area is located in the old urban areas of Hai Phong City and the areas of the former Thuy
Nguyen district (currently wards of Hai Phong City); land transactions in this area have been almost
non-existent in recent years. On the other hand, the Hai Phong City People's Committee issued a land
price list for the 2020 - 2024 period with appropriate adjustments. Therefore, when evaluating the
compensation unit price for perennial crop land, annual crop land, and aquaculture land, it is found
to be equivalent to the market price; the consultant team only noted that the prices of some locations
adjacent to roads tend to be higher than those in the City's regulations due to recent fluctuations.
Based on the survey results for the agricultural land group, a comparison with the City's unit price
combined with support allowances shows that the price (including support) is equivalent to the
market price and tends to benefit the people whose land is recovered. The unit price for the group of
trees and crops is equivalent to the market price and has received high consensus from the people.
However, there is a significant difference between the market price and the compensation unit price
issued by the Hai Phong City People's Committee for the urban residential land group, due to
relatively large fluctuations in land prices in the former Thuy Nguyen area and the current wards .




Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                            Page | 207
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

Appendix 9. Proposed Terms of Reference (TOR) for Third-party monitoring
SECTION 1. BACKGROUND
1.1    As with all World Bank supported projects, the Bank’s safeguards policies will apply as will
       its procurement policies regarding the engagement of consultants and of contractors and
       suppliers of works and goods. Separate consultants will be engaged to carry out independent
       resettlement monitoring of the project during implementation. The Construction Supervision
       and Management Consultant will be expected to cooperate with and assist the independent
       monitoring consultants in their work.
1.2    This TOR is concerned with the independent resettlement monitoring for the project. The
       independent monitoring is to be conducted by an Independent Monitoring Agency (IMC),
       independent from the PMU. It will also serve as a warning system for the PMU of existing
       problems during the RP implementation as well as a channel for the affected people to make
       known their needs and their reactions to resettlement and environmental execution.
SECTION 2. OBJECTIVES OF THE ASSIGNMENT
2.1.   The aims and objectives for the independent monitoring and evaluation on resettlement are
to:
       ● Verify results of internal monitoring;
       ● Assess whether resettlement objectives have been met; specifically, whether livelihoods
         and living standards have been restored or enhanced;
       ● Assess resettlement efficiency, effectiveness, impacts and sustainability, drawing lessons
         as a guide to future resettlement policy making and planning; and
       ● Ascertain whether the resettlement entitlements were appropriate for meeting the
         objectives, and whether the objectives were suited to PAP conditions.
2.2.   Information requirements
       The IMC will monitor and evaluate achievements and impacts related to the implementation
       of the approved the RP. The IMC will develop a database sufficient to evaluate whether the
       objectives of the Resettlement Plan are being met. This database will be developed to enable
       comparisons of "before" and "after" resettlement conditions. The database will consist of data
       acquired through the Census and Detailed Measurement Survey of each affected household,
       which will form the basis for the Project's record keeping system. The IMC will expand the
       database as necessary with maps, charts, photographs of affected properties, copies of
       contracts and land titles, payments, and valuation documents relating to the resettlement.
2.3.   To achieve these objectives, there are two main component activities:
       ● Periodically monitoring the implementation of the project resettlement and rehabilitation
         of PAPs’ lives during the project implementation; and
       ● Evaluating socio-economic/living standards situation of PAPs after completion of the RP
         implementation.
SECTION 3. SCHEDULE
3.1.   A suggested schedule is expected to provide comments from the team indicated in required
       outputs. Timing for submission will depend on the progress of construction works, subject to
       negotiations and agreements with the PMU.
SECTION 4. SCOPE OF WORKS


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                           Page | 208
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

4.1.   The monitoring targets and functions of independent monitoring shall include: (i) review of
       pre-project baseline data on PAPs; (ii) identification and selection of an appropriate set of
       indicators for gathering and analyzing information on resettlement impacts; (iii) use of
       various formal and informal surveys for impact analysis; (iv) use of participatory methods for
       monitoring and evaluation; and (v) assessment of resettlement efficiency, effectiveness,
       impact and sustainability, drawing lessons as a guide to future resettlement policy making
       and planning.
4.2.   In detail the Independent Monitoring Consultants will:
       (a)   Review the existing baseline data and gather additional socio-economic baseline data
             (if necessary) on sample families which are entitled to receive compensation for all their
             lost assets or for resettlement;
       (b)   Monitor the implementation of the compensation, resettlement and rehabilitation
             policies and public information campaign as designed in the RP;
       (c)   Identify any discrepancy between the RP and actual practice, problems in RP
             implementation as well as any local level grievances;
       (d)   Propose measures to solve potential problems and complaints (if necessary) or
             outstanding issues to the PMU and the World Bank;
4.3.   Monitoring and evaluation indicators:
       The following indicators will be monitored and evaluated by the IMC:
       (a)   Payment of compensation will be as follows: a) full payment to be made to all affected
             people sufficiently before the land acquisition; (b) adequacy of payment to replace
             affected assets.
       (b)   Provision of technical assistance for house construction to DPs who are rebuilding their
             structures on their remaining land, or building their own structures in new places as
             arranged by the project, or on newly assigned land plots.
       (c)   Support for recovering income sources.
       (d)   Public consultation and awareness of compensation policy: (a) DPs should be fully
             informed and consulted about land acquisition, leasing and relocation activities; (b) the
             monitoring team should attend at least one public consultation meeting to monitor
             public consultation procedures, problems and issues that arise during the meetings, and
             solutions that are proposed; (c) public awareness of the compensation policy and
             entitlements will be assessed among the DPs; and (d) assessment of awareness of
             various options available to DPs as provided for in the RPs.
       (e)   Affected people should be monitored regarding restoration of productive activities.
       (f)   DPs’ satisfaction on various aspects of the RP will be monitoring and recorded.
             Operation of the GRM and speed of complaint settlement will be monitored.
       (g)   Linkage of resettlement and resettlement site preparation: The completion of land
             acquisition and preparation of resettlement activities (should be completed at least one
             month before the start of actual resettlement);
       (h)   Restoration of civil infrastructure: All necessary infrastructures (water supply, drainage
             system, roads, sanitation, etc.) should be developed at the resettlement sites or at the site
             of relocation up to a standard at least equal to the standard at the original location;


Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                                Page | 209
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

       (k)   Resettlement budget and financing: The Independent Monitoring Consultants should
             monitor the resettlement compensation prices, types of allowances and supports, and
             actual resettlement expenditures versus the resettlement budget. The monitor should
             cover resettlement financing as well, including timing and sufficiency of financial
             allocations for resettlement.
       (l)   Public survey and information disclosure:
               ● To check if affected people were informed and consulted about resettlement
                 activities, such as resettlement apartments and site and services allocation;
               ● The IMC should attend some public consultation meetings to monitor public
                 consultation procedures, problems and issues that arise during the meetings, and
                 proposed recommendations to address any resolved outstanding problems; and
               ● To check the availability of RP in the related local institutions.
       (m) Levels of satisfaction:
               ● The levels of satisfaction of the affected people with various aspects of the RP
                 will be monitored and recorded; and
               ● Monitoring the operations of the grievance procedures and the timeframe of the
                 grievance redress will be monitored.
       (n)   Standards of living: Throughout the implementation process, the trends in living
             standards of displaced households will be observed and potential problems during the
             restoration of living standards will be identified and reported;
       (o)   Follow-up Socio-Economic Surveys: One year after the end of resettlement activities,
             the Independent Monitoring Consultants will conduct a follow-up socio-economic
             survey to determine project impacts on income levels and living standards of the
             affected people;
       (p)   Resettlement management: Institutional setup, staffing, and internal monitoring
             mechanisms.
4.4.   Monitoring Methodology:
       Sample survey
       (a)   A socio-economic survey will be required before, during and after the resettlement
             implementation to provide a clear comparison of success/failure of the resettlement plan
             implementation.
        (b) Monitoring will be based on a sample basis. Scale of a survey sample may cover 100%
            of relocated households and severely affected households and at least 20% of the
            remaining households. The sample survey should be conducted twice a year.
       (c)   The surveys should include women, elderly people, and other vulnerable groups, which
             should have equal representation of male and female respondents.
       Database storage
       (a)   The IMC will maintain a database of resettlement monitoring information. It will
             contain files on results of independent monitoring, DPs surveyed and will be updated
             based on information collected in successive rounds of data collection. All databases
             compiled will be fully accessible by the PMU and the World Bank.
       Reports

Hai Phong Resilience Development Project
                                                                                           Page | 210
RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

       (a)   The IMC must report every 6 months which mentions the findings in the monitoring
             process. The monitoring reports will be submitted to the PMU, and then the PMU will
             submit the WB in the form of appendixes of the progress reports.
        (b) The reports should contain (i) a report on the progress of RP implementation; (ii)
            deviations, if any, from the provisions and principles of the RP; (ii) identification of
            problem issues and recommended solutions so that implementing agencies are informed
            about the ongoing situation and can resolve problems in a timely manner; and (iv) a
            report on progress of the follow-up of problems and issues identified in the previous
            report.
       Follow-Up Monitoring Report
         (a) The monitoring reports will be discussed in meetings between the IMC and the PMU.
             The PMU usually holds a meeting immediately after receiving a monitoring report.
             Necessary follow-up actions will be taken based on problems and issues identified in
             the reports and follow-up discussions.
       Ex-post Evaluation
       (a)   An Ex-post Evaluation is an assessment for the whole RP implementation to assess
             whether the stated objectives have been achieved. The independent monitoring
             consultants will conduct an ex-post evaluation of the resettlement process and impacts
             after the completion, 6 to 12 months, of all resettlement activities. The evaluation will
             use the same survey questionnaire and sample that are use

RESETTLEMENT PLAN (RP)

         on HIV/AIDS, STDs and social evils

         officers, workers of construction contractors should be carried out.
      3. People’s awareness of project’s benefits should be enhanced through communication
      4. Impacts on travelling, noise, stagnancy, etc. should be minimized by the construction
         contractors
      5. There should be monitoring agency to ensure that construction activities do not affect
         livelihood of local people.

         activities
      7. Minimize the number of affected households by the project
      8. Subproject construction should be quick and in good quality.
      9. Local people should be informed of when subproject items may temporarily affect
         remaining land of local people
